# Decisions Log

Append-only. Each entry: the decision + *why*. Don't re-litigate a settled
decision — if you change course, add a new entry that supersedes the old one.
(See `ARCHITECTURE.md` for the full spec, `STATUS.md` for current state.)

---

### 2026-06-18 — Foundations
1. **Separate app + repo**, not part of WC2026. *Why:* different domain, different users.
2. **1–2 private users**, no public sign-up. *Why:* it's for Craig's dad (+ maybe one other) — lets us strip all multi-tenant/league machinery.
3. **Garmin via unofficial `garminconnect`**, not the official Health/Connect dev program. *Why:* immediate to prototype; garth token cache persists ~1yr so unattended sync works.
4. **The app generates the analysis itself** (calls Claude directly), Copilot out of the loop. *Why:* the analysis quality *is* the product; we control the prompt + persistent context.
5. **Hive + weather in v1.** *Why:* kills his manual temperature transcription — his #1 sleep lever.
6. **Web app, forking the WC2026 stack/infra.** *Why:* inherit a proven FastAPI/React/Postgres/scheduler/PWA foundation.
7. **Manual entry** stays for BP, subjective/RPE, food, supplements. *Why:* no other source exists for them.

### 2026-06-18 — Build approach
8. **Fork-and-gut WC2026**, don't build fresh. *Why:* day-one working CI/Docker/Railway/Vercel/auth/scheduler.
9. **Reusable starter template distilled LATER** (after this 2nd app), as a **clone-and-own template, not a shared runtime library**. *Why:* extracting from N=1 bakes in wrong abstractions; a library couples independent personal apps — a template gives reuse without coupling.
10. **Deploy live early** (Supabase + Railway + Vercel). *Why:* his dad can use it on his phone from early on.

### 2026-06-18 — Data sources (all validated against real data)
11. **Hive unattended sync = stored-creds re-login**, not refresh token. *Why:* his Hive account has no 2FA (so full login is headless), and pyhiveapi's `refresh_token` is bugged + Cognito device-tracking rejects bare refresh.
12. **Weather = Open-Meteo** (keyless). *Why:* free, no API key, has recent-history + forecast; KA1 2SD → lat 55.6045 / long -4.5249.

### 2026-06-19 — Product shape
13. **Knowledge-base layer is core.** *Why:* his hand-written "handover docs" exist because AIs forget context — the app's job is to hold that as living state.
14. **Verdict = Green/Amber/Red framework + age-adjustment** (sleep +4; REM band 65–90 min). *Why:* it's his own documented decision rule, and Garmin's scores are calibrated for young athletes.
15. **Ignore the phase-frequency cadence — daily always.** *Why:* his explicit preference (phases were only about reducing monitoring; he wants to continue daily).
16. **Training plan: stored in DB (retained) + per-day override; app generates future 13-wk blocks with refine-then-lock** (sequenced to v2). *Why:* unlike Copilot it never forgets the plan; refine-then-lock preserves the "mould it + fix errors" control he values.

### 2026-06-19 — Cross-tool workflow
17. **Built across Claude Code + Codex. `AGENTS.md` is canonical; `CLAUDE.md` is a symlink to it.** Repo is the single source of truth; Claude's private memory is a cache only. *Why:* smooth, drift-free handoffs between tools — neither depends on state the other can't see.

### 2026-06-19 — Batch workflow machinery (deferred build: pre-Phase-1)
18. **Lean batch command set (4), not WC's 7:** `batch-start`, `batch-verify`, `closeout`, `next-batch-prompt`. `closeout` folds WC's `phase-closeout` + `strike-batch` + `ship-prod` into one (commit → CI → merge to main → deploy → update STATUS/DECISIONS/ARCHITECTURE → strike the batch row). *Dropped:* `ship-staging` (Vercel/Railway give a **preview deploy per push** — that's the staging tier; eyeball the preview URL, then `closeout` promotes to the prod his dad uses) and standalone `strike-batch` (folded into `closeout`). *Why:* smaller single-user app + the `STATUS.md`/`handoff` docs already cover some of WC's ceremony. Built as tool-agnostic `docs/agent-commands/*.md` + thin Claude (`.claude/commands/`) and Codex (`.codex/prompts/`, exact path TBC) wrappers, right before Phase 1.
19. **Batch tags are TIER-based with a per-tool model map** (not Claude-only, not pinned to one tool). WC tagged each batch with a Claude model (🟢 Sonnet / 🔴 Opus). Here a batch carries a **complexity tier** (fixed by the batch — it reflects how hard the work is); you choose Claude *or* Codex per session and use the mapped model:

    | Tier | Work | Claude | Codex |
    |---|---|---|---|
    | 🔴 **High** | complex reasoning — analysis-engine prompt design, verdict/scoring logic, scheduler/sync edge cases, debugging | Opus | GPT-5.5 |
    | 🟢 **Mid** | well-specified implementation — CRUD, components, migrations, tests, mechanical refactors | Sonnet | GPT-5.4 |

    `batch-start` states the tier; `next-batch-prompt` notes the tier + this map. *Why:* decouples work-difficulty (the batch's call) from tool-choice (yours, per session), so any batch can run in either tool at the right capability level. (Codex model names per Craig's setup — update here if they change.)

### 2026-06-19 — Phase 0a (football domain strip)
20. **Display-name login, not email.** Profile has `display_name` + `pin_hash`; no email, no avatar, no site_role. *Why:* 1–2 private users; email auth adds complexity that buys nothing.
21. **No signup endpoint.** Admin seeds profiles directly in the DB (or via a future admin panel in Phase 2). *Why:* this is a private app — open signup is never needed; simpler security surface.
22. **`@coach/shared` package is a stub until Phase 1.** Only exports `Role` type. Scoring helpers, schemas, and Garmin/Hive types will be added in Phase 1 once the data model is settled from real spike JSON. *Why:* premature typing bakes in wrong shapes.
23. **Brand wordmark: text-only for Phase 0.** "GARMIN / COACH" two-line mono wordmark instead of the Calcio SVG icon. *Why:* no designer available yet; icon assets added in Phase 1/2 when identity is designed.
24. **`score-input.tsx`, `offlineQueue.ts`, `sw.ts` "predictions" references left in.** These are offline-queue infrastructure — the word "predictions" refers to offline-queued API writes, not football predictions. They will be renamed when the coaching submission flow ships in Phase 1. *Why:* renaming now with no replacement use is noise.

### 2026-06-19 — Zwift integration (validated) + training inputs
25. **Zwift workout delivery via `intervals.icu` relay** (validated end-to-end). App pushes a structured workout to his intervals.icu calendar (free API); intervals.icu's existing Zwift Training-Connections integration delivers it into Zwift's Custom Workouts. *Why:* Zwift's own Training API is partner-only (impractical for 1–2 users); piggybacking intervals.icu's approved partnership gives true "straight-from-app → Zwift". Power + timing came through **perfect** in testing.
26. **intervals.icu is a DELIVERY RAIL, not the system-of-record.** Our own Postgres owns the plan, knowledge base, and AI brain (keeps Decision #16). *Why:* owning the plan keeps us uncoupled and in control; intervals.icu/Zwift could change.
27. **intervals.icu is OUTPUT-only — activity ingestion stays DIRECT from Garmin.** *Why:* Garmin direct is richer (Performance Condition, Stamina); routing ingestion via intervals.icu would be a lossy middleman.
28. **Deterministic `.ZWO` export demoted to a no-dependency FALLBACK** (relay is primary). *Why:* the relay removes the manual step entirely; .ZWO stays as the always-works backup if intervals.icu is unavailable.
29. **Any write to his trainer is propose → he approves → push — never silent.** *Why:* he values control ("mould it, fix errors"); consistent with refine-then-lock (#16).
30. **Closed-loop coaching is now possible** (sense→decide→ACT). v2 elevated: on an Amber morning or a dynamic week-restructure, the app can regenerate the adjusted workout and (on approval) deliver it to Zwift — coaching becomes *executable*, not just advisory.
31. **Lead-time requirement softened.** He no longer hand-builds in Zwift, so "lead time" = the app auto-pushes workouts a couple of days ahead. Still surface the week-ahead in the UI. *Why:* delivery is now the app's job, not his.
32. **Cadence on Zwift repeated-interval (`IntervalsT`) blocks gets Zwift DEFAULTS (100 work / 90 rest), not our value** — intervals.icu stores cadence correctly; Zwift overrides it on repeat blocks. Likely fix: emit cadence-critical reps as **individual steps** (unconfirmed — verify on PC Zwift, mobile can't copy-to-edit). *Why it's not a blocker:* Zwift cadence is advisory, and power/timing are exact; Phase-2 polish, and our deterministic generator controls emit format per workout.
33. **Rønnestad 30/15 endorsed as a VO2 progression** of his Tue VO2 day (build weeks, ~Wk7+, **ERG off** due to 30s-surge lag, even-paced ~105–110% FTP / 15s easy). *Why:* best-evidenced VO2max protocol, age-appropriate; aligns with Copilot's move to 30/30 & 40/20. Feed into the plan generator + KB.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 0b (hosting)
34. **Single Supabase project for both movie app and garmin-coach, isolated by schema.** Movie app uses `public`; garmin-coach uses `coach`. Free tier allows only 2 active projects; this avoids using a second slot. *Why:* trivial for a 1-2 user private app where schemas don't conflict; Alembic targets `coach` via `version_table_schema="coach"` and `SET search_path TO coach, public`.
35. **Supabase session-mode pooler (port 5432), not transaction mode (port 6543).** Railway containers are IPv6-only; Supabase's direct host (`db.*.supabase.co:5432`) is IPv4-only → "Network is unreachable". Supabase Supavisor pooler (`aws-1-eu-north-1.pooler.supabase.com`) is dual-stack. Session mode chosen over transaction mode because asyncpg creates named prepared statements (`__asyncpg_stmt_N__`) that conflict across pooler connections in transaction mode. *Why not transaction mode:* setting `prepared_statement_cache_size=0` disables asyncpg's local cache but doesn't stop it emitting `PREPARE` on the server; two connections sharing a backend get duplicate-name errors. Session mode maps 1:1 to a PG backend for the connection lifetime — prepared statements persist correctly.
36. **Vercel `vercel.json` at repo root (not `apps/web/`).** Vercel's monorepo auto-detection picks `vercel.json` from root; placing it in `apps/web/` caused `@coach/shared: workspace:*` to fail (Vercel used npm, not pnpm). Root config sets `buildCommand: "pnpm --dir apps/web build"` + `installCommand: "pnpm install --frozen-lockfile"`. *Why:* pnpm workspaces require pnpm; only root-level `vercel.json` lets us override the install command.
37. **Railway NOT connected to GitHub auto-deploy (deliberate for now).** Deploying via `railway up` (builds from local source and uploads). Connect to GitHub in Railway dashboard Settings > Source Repo when continuous deployment is wanted. *Why deferred:* faster to ship; auto-deploy can be wired once Phase 1 is stable.
38. **Alembic migration engine needs `prepared_statement_cache_size=0` when using transaction-mode pooler.** The app engine in `database.py` had this; the `_run_async_migrations()` engine in `migrations/env.py` did not — causing startup to crash before uvicorn even started. Fixed in commit 189527b. Moot in session mode but kept as defensive belt-and-suspenders.
39. **GitHub auto-deploy is ON for Railway + Vercel, superseding #37.** Railway service `api` is connected to `CraigR973/garmin-coach` on branch `main`; Vercel project `garmin-coach` is connected to the same repo with production branch `main` and Git deployments enabled. Vercel creates PR/branch previews; Railway stays main-only. *Why:* restores the staging story assumed by #18 (Vercel previews before merge) and removes manual `railway up` / `vercel --prod` as the normal path. Preview deploys still proxy `/api/*` to the production Railway API/DB, so previews are for visual review unless a separate backend environment is added later.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 prep
40. **Codex has no shared project-level custom-prompt path to rely on.** Current OpenAI docs say Codex custom prompts are deprecated and loaded from the user-level `~/.codex/prompts`, while project `.codex/` layers cover config/hooks/rules. This repo keeps reviewable Codex wrapper sources in `.codex/prompts/`, but they must be copied or symlinked into `~/.codex/prompts/` to be invokable. *Why:* keeps the cross-tool procedures in-repo without pretending Codex will auto-load a project prompt folder that the official docs do not promise.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 Batch 1
41. **`profiles` remains the private user table for v1, instead of renaming it to `users`.** Batch 1 extends `profiles` with Garmin/Hive/location metadata and adds the v1 coaching tables around it. *Why:* the stripped auth skeleton, refresh tokens, notification preferences, audit log, and live migration `001` already depend on `profiles`; renaming a live auth table during the data-model batch would add deployment risk without improving the product. The product/API can still describe these rows as users.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 Batch 2
42. **Garmin credentials stay in environment/secrets; Postgres stores only non-secret user metadata.** The app logs into `garminconnect` with `GARMIN_EMAIL` / `GARMIN_PASSWORD` and persists Garmin's own garth token cache under `GARMIN_TOKENSTORE` (default `~/.garminconnect`). *Why:* v1 has 1-2 private users and no admin secret-management UI yet; this keeps credentials out of the repo, DB rows, logs, and tests while preserving unattended sync through Garmin's long-lived token cache.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 Batch 3
43. **`weather_daily` stores explicit overnight wind max/gust columns, not only raw Open-Meteo JSON.** *Why:* sleep disruption depends on overnight environment, and Batch 3's acceptance criteria require overnight low/wind to be first-class queryable context for later morning analysis and thermal monitoring.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 Batch 4
44. **Backfilled morning-analysis baselines live in a dedicated `metric_baselines` table, not ad-hoc JSON on `profiles` or recalculation-only code.** The 84-night spreadsheet importer upserts historical `sleep` + `daily_metrics` rows and then persists reproducible summary stats per metric (mean/median/quartiles/range/stddev) with the source window recorded. *Why:* Batch 6 needs inspectable, queryable baseline helpers, and storing them separately keeps the import rerunnable, the provenance explicit, and future baseline recomputes/admin refreshes simple.
45. **SpO2 and HRV baselines exclude spreadsheet rows before 2026-06-11, while the raw backfill still imports the full 84 nights.** *Why:* Mark's documented data-quality rule says strap-tightening on 11 Jun is the reliability boundary for those metrics; preserving all source rows keeps history intact, but baseline comparisons should not normalize against known-bad physiology data.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 Batch 5
46. **The retained handover context is seeded lazily through an admin-only coaching-state API, then edited through versioned `knowledge_base` and `planned_workouts` records rather than hardcoded frontend defaults.** The first load of `/api/v1/admin/coaching-state` seeds the spec-backed knowledge-base sections plus a 13-week 2121 plan map and workout slate if the user has no retained state yet; subsequent edits create new versions and keep prior rows for audit/history. *Why:* Batch 5 needed a real, inspectable source of truth for the morning engine without introducing a one-off seed script or making the UI depend on bundle-local defaults. Lazy seeding keeps setup friction low for the private single-admin flow while preserving durable backend-owned state.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 Batch 6
47. **Morning analysis uses a thin Anthropic Messages HTTP boundary with explicit prompt/version metadata, not an SDK wrapper or hidden prompt.** `MorningAnalysisService` assembles a stored context packet, stores `prompt_version`, `model_name`, raw response, verdict, and markdown in `analyses`, and the model/key/max-token settings come from environment variables. *Why:* this keeps the Claude call inspectable and fakeable in tests, avoids adding another runtime dependency, and preserves the packet that explains every daily verdict.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 Batch 7
48. **Daily-loop adherence lives on `manual_entries`, linked to the active `planned_workouts` row and its version, instead of mutating the plan row itself or adding a separate table.** Manual check-ins still use `manual_entries` rows with no workout link; adherence rows set `planned_workout_id`, `planned_workout_version`, `adherence_status`, and `actual_workout_json`. *Why:* Batch 7 needed phone-friendly "did he do it / what changed?" capture tied to the exact planned version without overwriting the plan history. Reusing `manual_entries` keeps the schema small and lets later analyses read both subjective check-ins and adherence notes from one source of truth.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 Batch 8
49. **Post-workout analysis reuses the `analyses` table with `analysis_type='post_workout'` and `activity_id`, and surfaces recent outputs on the daily dashboard rather than a separate page.** The hourly Garmin poll syncs recent activities, then generates at most one ride analysis per activity; the stored context packet includes activity summary, FTP-based power zones, time-series channels, plan context, and the morning verdict. *Why:* `analyses.activity_id` already existed for this boundary, so a new table would duplicate storage; the daily dashboard is where Mark already checks verdicts/adherence, so recovery protocol and tomorrow impact belong there for the v1 phone workflow.

### 2026-06-20 — Phase 1 Batch 9
50. **Notification nudges and alerts use `analyses` as the audit/idempotency log instead of a new table.** Evening sleep-protocol nudges, thermal alerts, and stale-source alerts write non-Claude rows with `analysis_type` values `evening_nudge`, `thermal_alert`, and `stale_source_alert`, a notification rule version, the push tag, and `sentCount`. *Why:* the app already needs date-scoped generated outputs with context packets and dedupe checks; reusing `analyses` keeps Batch 9 schema-free while preserving inspectable evidence for why a nudge did or did not send.

### 2026-06-21 — Phase 2 Batch 11
51. **`TokenResponse.player` and `PlayerInfo` schema class names kept unchanged during the player→user rename.** The Python internals (`get_current_user`, `CurrentUser`, etc.) were all renamed, but the JSON response key `player` and the Pydantic class `PlayerInfo` stay as-is. *Why:* the frontend `AuthContext.tsx` reads `data.player.id`, `data.player.display_name`, `data.player.role`, `data.player.timezone` — changing the wire-format key would break the live app without a coordinated frontend + backend deploy.
52. **`ActorType.player` and `ActionType.player_pin_reset` enum values left unchanged.** These are values stored in Postgres enum columns. *Why:* renaming stored enum values requires a DB-level `ALTER TYPE … RENAME VALUE` migration plus potentially backfilling existing rows — disproportionate risk for cosmetic renaming. They will remain as-is unless a substantive schema migration is needed for another reason.
53. **`login_key` rate-limit in `rate_limit.py` fixed to read `display_name` instead of `email`.** This was a pre-existing bug introduced when auth was ported from the WC2026 app (which used email login). *Why:* the Garmin Coach login endpoint uses `display_name` as the login identifier (Decision #20); the old `email` key lookup would have silently failed with `None` and produced a useless rate-limit key. Caught incidentally during the player→user rename pass.

### 2026-06-21 — Phase 2 Batch 12
54. **Zwift delivery approval state lives in `workout_delivery_proposals`, not on `planned_workouts`.** A proposal snapshots the planned workout version, structured workout IR, intervals.icu calendar payload, deterministic `.ZWO` XML, status, approval timestamp, and pushed intervals.icu event id. *Why:* `planned_workouts` remains the owned plan/history source of truth, while delivery is an explicit propose → approve → push workflow with a durable audit trail and no silent trainer writes (Decision #29).
55. **Cadence-critical workout output is flattened into individual steps.** The Batch 12 rail deliberately avoids `IntervalsT`/repeat-block emission in both intervals.icu text and `.ZWO` fallback output. *Why:* validated power and timing were exact, but Zwift overrides cadence on repeated-interval blocks (Decision #32); flat steps preserve our cadence intent until PC Zwift verification proves otherwise.

### 2026-06-21 — LLM backend (auth + cost)
56. **Claude access is the paid Anthropic API (Console `x-api-key`, per-token billing) — not Pro/Max subscription auth, and not free LLM tiers.** Staying on `claude-sonnet-4-6` (not Opus) for the morning/post-workout tasks; revisit cost after a few months (~Sept 2026). The non-dev startup validator now also fails closed when `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` is empty. *Why:* (a) subscription auth (Claude Code / Agent SDK `CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN`) is for interactive use — the analysis runs unattended from APScheduler against the raw Messages API, so powering a deployed backend with a personal subscription is outside intended use and risks the account; (b) free tiers (Gemini free, Groq, OpenRouter `:free`) generally train on / human-review inputs — unacceptable for Mark's personal health data — whereas paid API tiers do not train on data. Cost is ~$2–4/month at this volume, and a provider swap stays low-effort (clean boundary classes, most alternatives OpenAI-compatible). Refines Decision #4.

### 2026-06-21 — Phase 2 Batch 12 closeout (rail-only)
57. **Batch 12 ships the Zwift delivery rail now; the production daily-loop *data* gate is deferred to Batch 18.** Merged and deployed: the delivery rail (intervals.icu push + `.ZWO` fallback, propose→approve→push, migration `007`), the `GARMIN_TOKENSTORE_B64` token-blob auth path, and the Anthropic fail-closed validator (#56). But the strict daily-loop smoke (non-null Garmin daily metrics/sleep + morning analysis for today) **cannot pass**: production has no job that syncs daily metrics/sleep — `GarminSyncService.sync_daily` exists from Batch 2 but has **no caller in `src/`** (the 06:30 job only does weather→analysis; the hourly job only does activities). Anthropic credits + the Garmin token blob were necessary but not sufficient. *Why ship anyway:* the rail is the foundational v2 dependency (#25–29) for executable coaching (Batches 13–16) and is complete and green; blocking it on a separate missing sync would stall all of v2. The daily-metrics/sleep sync and the strict data gate are relocated to **Batch 18** — this adjusts where Batch 12's data-loop acceptance is verified, it does not reverse the gate.

### 2026-06-21 — Phase 2 Batch 18 (production daily-loop data sync)
58. **The Garmin daily metrics/sleep sync is wired *inside* the 06:30 `morning_weather_sync` job, before the analysis loop — not as a separate scheduler job.** `run_morning_weather_sync` now runs weather sync → commit → `_sync_garmin_daily` → commit → morning analysis, all in one ordered pipeline against the same session. *Why:* the acceptance criterion is "before the 06:30 morning analysis runs" (Batch 18.1), and a single job makes that ordering deterministic — a separate cron job firing near 06:30 would race the analysis with no guaranteed happens-before. Sharing the session also means the just-committed `daily_metrics`/`sleep` rows are immediately visible to `MorningAnalysisService` for today's verdict. The fetch is wrapped in `_retry_sync(..., backoff=2.0)` (new exponential-backoff option) so a transient Garmin 429 is survived, and each profile's sync is isolated in its own try/except so one profile's Garmin failure (429/MFA/token) is logged and skipped without blocking the others or the downstream analysis. Closes the data gate deferred in Decision #57.
59. **Production Hive auth resumes from a persisted Cognito refresh token (`HIVE_TOKENSTORE_B64`), not a headless password login.** Mark's Hive account requires AWS Cognito `SMS_MFA`, so `pyhiveapi`'s `Auth.login()` returns an SMS challenge that cannot be answered unattended. `HiveClient` now decodes a base64 `{username, refresh_token}` blob and calls Cognito `REFRESH_TOKEN_AUTH` directly (pyhiveapi's own `Auth.refresh_token()` is broken — a stray trailing comma makes `AuthParameters` a tuple) to mint a fresh id token; full email/password login is kept only as a fallback and rejects SMS_MFA with a pointer to the blob. `scripts/bootstrap_hive_tokenstore.py` mints the blob from a one-time SMS-2FA login. *Why:* the production `morning_weather_sync` / `hive_temperature_poll` jobs run unattended from APScheduler, and the previous full-login client failed *every* poll on the SMS challenge — leaving `thermalState` empty and emitting a scheduler ERROR line, both of which block the Batch 18 strict daily-loop gate (#58). This corrects the earlier "Hive — no 2FA on his account" claim in `AGENTS.md` (the validated spike only ran headlessly by caching the refresh token), and mirrors the Garmin `GARMIN_TOKENSTORE_B64` pattern. Fixed alongside: `logging_config.py` now includes `structlog.processors.format_exc_info`, so scheduler exception tracebacks are no longer dropped — they were serialized as a bare `exc_info=true`, which is what hid this root cause until a Railway log dive.
60. **Daily-loop thermal state hides stale Hive temperatures using the same 45-minute freshness rule as the notification engine; stale rows still expose their last sync timestamp, but not a current temperature value.** The API now nulls `thermalState.latestTemperatureC` and `targetTemperatureC` when the newest `temperature_readings` row is older than the Hive freshness window, while preserving `capturedAtUtc`. *Why:* the Batch 18 strict smoke originally passed because `latestTemperatureC` was merely non-null, even though the live Hive `heating` product's `lastSeen` was stuck at `2026-06-16T15:10:56.874Z`. Surfacing that stale value as "current" made the daily loop look fresher than it was. Aligning the daily-loop surface with the existing stale-source alert rule makes production honesty stronger than the old non-null gate and keeps the UI/API consistent about what counts as fresh thermal data.

### 2026-06-21 — Phase 2 Batch 13 (executable coaching)
61. **The Amber/Red workout adjustment is a deterministic transform on the normalized `%FTP` IR, not a Claude call.** `adjust_ir_for_verdict` (in `services/executable_coaching.py`) operates on the already-flattened Batch 12 IR: **Amber** scales every step to 75% duration (a 25% cut, inside the documented 20-30% band), drops the working intervals by ~one zone (13 FTP points), and caps power at threshold (98%) so no HIT/VO2 survives; **Red** halves duration and caps every step at 60% FTP, which makes a VO2 push structurally impossible; **Green** is pass-through. *Why:* the verdict framework (ARCHITECTURE §4) is a documented rule, and the **Red-never-VO2** guarantee is a safety property that must hold every time — encoding it as inspectable, unit-tested arithmetic is stronger and cheaper than trusting an LLM to obey it, and it keeps regeneration working even when `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`/`INTERVALS_API_KEY` are absent (regeneration only *proposes*; it never pushes). The morning verdict itself is still produced by the Batch 6 engine; Batch 13 only acts on the stored `verdict`.
62. **Executable coaching reuses the existing schema — no new migration.** An Amber regeneration is stored as an ordinary Batch 12 `workout_delivery_proposals` row via a new shared `WorkoutDeliveryService.propose_from_ir`; the adjustment provenance (`origin`, `adjustment`) lives inside the snapshot's `structured_workout_ir` JSONB, and every proposal/push is audited as an `analyses` row with `analysis_type` `workout_proposed` / `workout_pushed` (the Batch 9 notification-audit pattern, idempotent on a per-row `tag`). Auto-push (`auto_push_due`, the `workout_autopush` scheduler job, 07/13/19 local) only ever pushes proposals a human has **already approved** and that fall within `today + 2 days`, so Decision #29 (propose → approve → push, never silent) holds while Decision #31 (the app pushes a couple of days ahead) is automated. *Why:* delivery state already has a durable home (#54) and the audit log already stores date-scoped generated outputs with dedupe; adding columns or a table for origin/verdict would be churn for data that is naturally part of the IR snapshot, and reusing `analyses` keeps Batch 13 migration-free and consistent with how nudges/alerts record evidence.

### 2026-06-21 — Phase 2 Batch 14 (dynamic weekly restructuring)
63. **The weekly restructurer is a deterministic permutation engine over the week's bike sessions, with the no-stack rule as a hard constraint and defer-on-fatigue as a lexicographic objective.** `plan_week_restructure` (in `services/weekly_restructure.py`) reassigns the week's bike workouts among the dates that already hold a bike session (strength/mobility days stay put and act as spacers), enumerates the permutations (capped at `MAX_PERMUTE_SESSIONS`), and picks the lowest-cost feasible arrangement. **Feasibility** = no VO2↔Sweet-Spot pair within `MIN_GAP_DAYS` (same/adjacent days). When **fatigued**, the cost key is `(infeasible?, defer_cost, moves, shift)` so deferring hard sessions later in the week is the primary objective; when fresh it is `(infeasible?, moves, shift, defer_cost)` so a conflict is fixed with minimal disruption and an already-spaced fresh week is a no-op. *Why:* the spacing/fatigue rules are documented coaching constraints (KB `training_plan.constraints`, ARCHITECTURE §6) and a small enumerated search makes them inspectable, deterministic, and unit-testable without a DB or an LLM — the engine is a pure function and the DB service is a thin wrapper. The fatigue signal itself (`assess_recovery_signal`) reads the latest readiness, HRV status, and the morning-verdict trend (a Red, ≥2 Ambers in the window, low readiness, or unbalanced HRV).
64. **Restructures are human-triggered and approval-gated, not auto-applied by the scheduler; the plan is versioned on `planned_workouts` and reuses the Batch 12/13 delivery rail (no new migration).** `apply_for_week` versions only the changed dates (new active version per date, prior deactivated — same pattern as `coaching_state.override_planned_workout`), audits the restructure as an `analyses` row (`analysis_type="weekly_restructure"`, `subject_date=week_start`), and proposes the changed bike workouts via `WorkoutDeliveryService.propose_from_ir` with `origin="weekly_restructure"` — they stay `proposed` until the human approves (Decision #29). It is exposed through `GET/POST /api/v1/restructure/*`, not wired into a scheduler job. *Why:* a scheduler that silently rewrote the plan and queued deliveries would violate the "never silent, mould-it-then-lock" contract (#16/#29); making restructure an explicit human action (preview → apply → approve → push) keeps Mark in control. Versioning per changed date preserves plan history and satisfies the `(user, date, version)` constraint, and reusing the existing proposal/audit homes (#54, #62) keeps Batch 14 migration-free.
65. **The VO2 progression — including Rønnestad 30/15 — is centralized in a shared `services/vo2_progression.py` toolkit used by both the plan seed and the restructurer.** `select_vo2_protocol(week_number, block_type)` returns 30/30 for early build and Rønnestad 30/15 from `RONNESTAD_FROM_WEEK` (7) onward; `build_vo2_structured_workout` emits the `structured_workout` dict carrying the documented constraints (`ergMode="off"`, even-paced 105-110% FTP / 15s easy — Decision #33). `coaching_state._build_templates` now calls the toolkit instead of inlining the VO2 shapes, and when `apply_for_week` defers/moves a late-build VO2 session it regenerates it through the toolkit so the deferred session keeps the 30/15 / ERG-off constraints. *Why:* the seed and the dynamic restructurer must agree on which protocol a given build week uses; a single source removes drift and makes the 30/15 progression independently testable, and it is the natural home for Batch 16's generator to draw VO2 days from later.

### 2026-06-21 — Phase 2 Batch 15 (holiday pause/resume)
66. **A holiday window is treated as a recovery-week equivalent: planned workouts inside the window are versioned as `status='skipped'` with `source='holiday_pause'`, not deleted.** `HolidayPauseService.pause` deactivates the existing `planned_workouts` rows and inserts new versions at `version+1` carrying the skipped status (same versioning pattern as Batches 13/14). *Why:* versioning preserves plan history and audit traceability; the `(user_id, workout_date, version)` uniqueness constraint stays intact; and it mirrors how the weekly restructurer and workout-delivery service handle plan changes — a consistent write pattern across all plan-mutation services.
67. **On return from holiday the 2121 block continuation rule is applied: Build1 pre-holiday → first week back continues as Build2; Build2 pre-holiday → first week back repeats Build1.** `continuation_label`/`continuation_week_number` are pure deterministic helpers — Build1/Build2 is determined by `(sequence_index - 1) % 3 == 0` (Build1) / `== 1` (Build2). `resume` finds the nearest build block that ended before the holiday, resolves the label and week-number, then regenerates the first post-holiday build block's workouts from `_block_templates` via `_regenerate_block`. *Why:* the 13-week 2121 slate is the core training block structure; the holiday pause must not arbitrarily reset to week-1 content when a partial build pair (Build1 or Build2) was in progress before the break — doing so would either repeat identical sessions or skip a progression step. The mirror pattern (came from Build1 → continue to Build2; came from Build2 → redo Build1) gives Mark continuity with minimal lost work and is the coaching-logic equivalent of how the existing slate handles recovery weeks.
68. **Holiday windows are stored as JSONB in the existing `knowledge_base` table at `section='holiday_windows'`; no migration is required.** Content schema: `{"windows": [{startDate, endDate, pausedAtUtc, resumedAtUtc}]}`. A new KB row is versioned (existing deactivated, new active) on each pause and each resume, preserving window history. *Why:* mirrors the Batch 13/14 pattern — using `knowledge_base` for structured operational context avoids table proliferation and any Alembic migration; the JSONB column and versioning semantics already suit append-append history. An active window (no `resumedAtUtc`) is the guard that prevents double-pause.

### 2026-06-22 — Phase 2 Batch 16 (app-generated 13-week blocks)
69. **The 13-week block generator is deterministic, not an LLM call, and reuses the shared `coaching_state` block templates + the Batch 14 `vo2_progression` toolkit.** `generate_block_plan` (in `services/block_generator.py`) maps the fixed `BLOCK_SEQUENCE` (2 build / 1 recovery ×3, wk12 taper, wk13 consolidation) over concrete dates from a start date + FTP, drawing each week's workouts from `_block_templates`; generated VO2 days therefore carry 30/30 early and Rønnestad 30/15 from ~Wk7 automatically. *Why:* the acceptance criteria are all *structural, testable invariants* — the exact 2121 shape, the VO2 progression rule, and refine/lock versioning — and the rest of v2 (Batches 13/14) already chose deterministic engines over LLM calls for plan-shaping safety properties. A deterministic generator makes the shape inspectable and unit-testable, guarantees it without depending on `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, and keeps a single source of truth for VO2 protocol selection shared with the seed and the restructurer (#65). "Conversational/refine" (Decision #16) is delivered as the *iterative refine-then-lock loop* the human drives, not as free-text generation.
70. **The generated block is a refine-then-lock draft stored as JSONB in `knowledge_base` at `section='generated_block'`; only `lock` mutates `planned_workouts`, and no migration is required.** Lifecycle: `generate` (status `draft`) → `refine*` (edit individual days) → `lock` (status `locked`, writes the plan) — each step versions the KB row (max-version + 1, so a discard-then-regenerate never reuses a version number). `generate` returns 409 if an unlocked draft already exists, and `discard` drops an unlocked draft, so refinements are never silently clobbered (Decision #29, "mould it, fix errors"). `lock` writes one versioned `plan_block` per week (block name versioned to avoid colliding with the seed slate) and versions up any active `planned_workout` on each date — the same write pattern as the holiday regenerator — so locking integrates with, rather than duplicates, plan history. Once locked the rows are ordinary active `planned_workouts` with `source='block_generator_lock'`, so they feed the daily loop and the Zwift rail under the existing approve → push gate (16.4) with no extra wiring. Exposed via `GET/POST /api/v1/block-generator/*` (human-driven) and a `/builder` PWA tab. *Why:* mirrors the Batch 15 no-migration JSONB pattern; keeping the draft out of `planned_workouts` until lock means a half-moulded block never leaks into the daily verdict or a delivery proposal, and reusing the existing versioning/delivery homes (#54, #64) keeps Batch 16 migration-free.

### 2026-06-22 — Phase 2 Batch 17 (monitoring + insight)
71. **The three monitoring insights (FTP-drift, early-warning, driver/correlation) are deterministic pure functions in `services/insights.py`, surfaced via human-triggered API and recorded to `analyses` on a `/run` call — no LLM, no new migration, and no scheduler cron.** `detect_ftp_drift` reads the trend in aerobic efficiency (watts-per-heartbeat) over recent rides and flags rising/falling/stable with the evidence window (first/last ride dates + sample count) surfaced; `detect_early_warning` measures the least-squares slope of HRV/sleep/readiness over a short window and fires only when ≥2 trends are degrading **and no Red is yet present** (a Red in the window is reported `already_red`, not "early"); `compute_drivers` ranks candidate movers of sleep/recovery by Pearson correlation over the long history, skipping drivers with <`MIN_CORRELATION_SAMPLES` pairs or zero variance. `InsightsService` is a thin DB wrapper; `run()` records an `analyses` audit row (`ftp_drift` / `early_warning` / `driver_correlation`) only for *findings* — a drift that actually drifted, a warning that fired, drivers with enough history — idempotent per `subject_date`. *Why:* like Batches 13/14/16, the acceptance criteria are testable arithmetic invariants (thresholds, evidence windows, correlation maths) that are stronger as inspectable pure functions than as an LLM call, and they work without `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`. Keeping insight runs human/API-triggered (not a new APScheduler job) follows Decision #64's philosophy — no silent background rewriting — and avoids racing the 06:30 pipeline; a scheduled `/run` can be layered on later without changing the engine.
72. **The experiment tracker reuses the existing `experiments` table for state and `analyses` for the audit trail; the three standing hypotheses seed lazily on first list; status is a validated state machine.** `ExperimentTrackerService` (in `services/experiment_tracker.py`) seeds collagen / recovery-week-disruption / 04:00-waking idempotently (keyed by a `slug` in `success_criteria_json`), and exposes create / pause-resume-conclude / add-observation through `GET/POST /api/v1/experiments/*`. Lifecycle is `active` ⇄ `paused` → `concluded` (terminal); `can_transition` enforces the matrix, concluding requires an outcome in {`supported`,`refuted`,`inconclusive`} (422 otherwise), and a concluded experiment rejects further status changes (409) and new observations (409). Observations append to `observations_json["entries"]`; every change writes an `analyses` row (`analysis_type="experiment_update"`). *Why:* both tables exist from Batch 1, so no migration is needed (mirrors the Batch 13/15/16 no-migration pattern); lazy-seeding the documented KB hypotheses (ARCHITECTURE §3) gives Mark a populated tracker without a one-off script (same approach as the Batch 5 coaching-state seed); and a deterministic transition matrix keeps the lifecycle from landing in an illegal state.

### 2026-06-22 — Auth simplification (passwordless device tokens)

73. **Auth moves to passwordless, revocable device tokens provisioned by a one-time activation link — replacing the inherited display-name + 4-digit-PIN + JWT login (supersedes the `pin_hash` login mechanism in #20; `display_name` stays as the profile label, no longer a credential).** Each device holds a 256-bit opaque token stored only as a SHA-256 hash (reusing the existing `refresh_tokens` table shape); `get_current_user` resolves it to a `Profile` with one indexed lookup instead of decoding an HS256 access/refresh JWT. Provisioning is admin-only and out-of-band: a CLI (`python -m src.activate --profile <name>`) mints a short-lived **single-use activation code**, printed as a `…/activate#code=…` link — the durable token never travels in a shareable link, and the `#fragment` keeps the code out of server logs; the PWA exchanges the code once for the device token, stores it, and Mark never sees a login screen again. Identity stays `token → profile`, so the 1–2-user model (#2) and admin-only provisioning with no public signup (#21) are preserved — only the *mechanism* changes, and two users (Craig + Mark) map to two tokens with `require_admin` still reading `profile.role`. *Why:* the v1+v2 review (`docs/reviews/v1-v2-review.md`) found that the bulk of the auth attack surface and code is the brute-force/reset machinery around a 4-digit PIN — and it is half-built: the DB lockout is **unwired** despite `rate_limit.py` claiming it is "the durable brute-force guard", the PIN-reset token is written to logs, and the production PIN was still the temporary `1234`. A high-entropy device token makes brute-force moot (no lockout/rate-limit needed as a guard), deletes the PIN/reset/change-PIN/refresh-rotation endpoints **and both JWT signing secrets**, and is a net code *reduction*. The one residual exposure — the token lives in `localStorage`, so it is XSS-readable — is closed by shipping the `vercel.json` security-headers/CSP block (review finding P2-1) in the same change.

74. **The cutover is phased, parallel-run, and reversible; platform-level auth (Cloudflare Access, the review's "Option C") is explicitly deferred, not adopted.** Rollout (full file-level plan in `docs/reviews/auth-simplification-plan.md`): (1) add the device-token path *alongside* the existing PIN login — `get_current_user` accepts either — and prove the activation flow on a real phone, nothing deleted; (2) flip the PWA default to device-token auth and hide the login form, PIN endpoints still live as a fallback; (3) once stable, delete the PIN/JWT/reset/lockout code (frontend `LoginPage`/`PinInput`/`ForgotPinPage`/`PinResetPage`; backend login/refresh/logout/change-pin/pin-reset, the bcrypt + HS256 helpers, the auth rate-limit keys) and ship the security headers; (4) drop the now-dead `pin_hash`/`failed_login_count`/`locked_until` columns and the `jwt_access_secret`/`jwt_refresh_secret` settings (the `player_pin_reset` audit enum value stays per #52). Only Phase 3 is destructive, and it lands only after Phase 2 has run cleanly for several days. *Why:* a parallel-run keeps Mark from ever being locked out mid-migration and lets each step be reverted independently. **Cloudflare Access (Option C)** is the more secure end-state — the session would live in an HttpOnly cookie outside JS's reach, and the API could not be reached without Cloudflare's signed JWT — but it requires a **paid custom domain** (Access cannot gate the `*.vercel.app`/`*.railway.app` platform URLs) and adds a fourth party to the auth path, and a domain is itself a renewal/hijack liability on a low-touch personal project. Given Craig owns no domain and the threat model is "keep opportunistic strangers out" (not a targeted adversary), the device-token approach at zero cost plus a CSP header is judged sufficient. Option C is recorded as the documented upgrade to take **if** a domain is later acquired or the `localStorage` residual becomes unacceptable; the `token → profile` identity model in #73 is forward-compatible with it (swap the credential source for Cloudflare's `Cf-Access-Jwt-Assertion`, keep everything downstream).

### 2026-06-22 — Red-never-VO2 at the delivery gate (review fix P1-2)

75. **The Red-never-VO2 guarantee is enforced at the delivery gate, and a Red verdict now regenerates a recovery substitution (extends #61/#62; closes review finding P1-2).** Two layers in `services/executable_coaching.py`: (a) `auto_push_due` re-reads the stored morning verdict for each approved proposal's date and refuses to push a proposal carrying VO2 intensity on a Red day, auditing the skip as an `analyses` row (`analysis_type="workout_push_blocked"`); the check is the pure predicate `blocks_red_vo2(verdict, ir)` — the verdict normalises to Red and any IR step reaches `HIT_FLOOR_PCT` — so the safety property is unit-testable without a DB. (b) `regenerate_for_verdict` now fires on Amber **or** Red, with Red proposing the `red_substitution` easy spin (still only `proposed`, never auto-approved), wiring the previously-dead Red branch of `adjust_ir_for_verdict` into the live 06:30 pipeline. *Why:* the transform-level guarantee (#61) was sound, but the live loop only regenerated on Amber and `push`/`auto_push_due` never re-checked the verdict — so a VO2 session approved ahead of the week (the #31 week-ahead workflow) could auto-push to Zwift on a Red morning. The property held in the unit but not at the delivery boundary; re-checking at the gate makes it hold however a proposal became approved, and keeping the predicate pure mirrors #61's "safety as inspectable arithmetic". No migration — the block audit reuses `analyses`. Shipped on `fix/red-vo2-delivery-gate` (PR #14), CI green.

### 2026-06-22 — Security quick-wins (review P2-1/2/3)

76. **Shipped the three remaining web-hardening quick-wins from the v1+v2 review in one change: a `vercel.json` security-headers/CSP block for the SPA origin (P2-1), a `react-router-dom` 6.30.3→6.30.4 bump for the GHSA-2j2x-hqr9-3h42 open redirect (P2-2), and a `security-audit` CI job running `pnpm audit --prod --audit-level=moderate` + `pip-audit -r requirements.txt` (P2-3).** The CSP is scoped to non-`/api` routes (`source: /((?!api/).*)`) so the proxied API responses keep their own stricter `default-src 'none'` from `middleware.py`. It uses `script-src 'self' 'sha256-…'`: the one inline script in `index.html` (the pre-mount theme-apply block) is allowed by **hash**, not by weakening script-src with `'unsafe-inline'` — so an injected `<script>` still cannot run and read the `localStorage` device token (the residual flagged in #73). `style-src` keeps `'unsafe-inline'` because Radix/shadcn, framer-motion and recharts all set inline `style=` attributes at runtime; script injection is the real XSS risk, inline styles are not. `connect-src 'self' https://*.sentry.io` covers the same-origin API proxy plus Sentry ingest (Supabase is never called from the browser). *Why:* P2-1 is load-bearing for the passwordless-auth plan (#73) — the device token lives in `localStorage`, so the CSP is what closes its XSS-exfiltration residual, and shipping it now puts it in place before Phase 1. The bump and the CI gate are one-liners that stop the same class of advisory recurring silently. **Maintenance gotcha:** the CSP carries a SHA-256 hash of the exact bytes of the inline `<script>` in `apps/web/index.html`. If that script is edited, the hash must be regenerated or the no-flash theme-apply silently breaks in production — the failure is *cosmetic* (a brief dark flash for light-mode users, since the page defaults to `class="dark"`), not a white screen, because the app bundle loads as an external `'self'` module. Regenerate after a build with:
`node -e 'const fs=require("fs"),c=require("crypto");const m=fs.readFileSync("apps/web/dist/index.html","utf8").match(/<script(?![^>]*src=)[^>]*>([\s\S]*?)<\/script>/)[1];console.log("sha256-"+c.createHash("sha256").update(m,"utf8").digest("base64"))'`
Shipped on `chore/security-quick-wins`. The interim PIN rotation (P1-3) remains Craig's to run out-of-band until #73 Phase 3 removes the PIN entirely.

### 2026-06-23 — Auth Phase 1 live + P3 hardening (review closeout)

77. **Auth simplification Phase 1 is implemented, merged, and live — the additive device-token path now runs alongside PIN login (executes the #73–74 plan's step 1; PR #18, migration `008`).** `get_current_user` is dual-path: it decodes the HS256 JWT first and, on an `InvalidTokenError` (a device token is opaque, not a JWT), falls back to a hashed-`token_hash` lookup of an unrevoked/unexpired `refresh_tokens` row with `purpose='device'` — so every `CurrentUser`/`AdminUser` route accepts either credential with no per-route change. `refresh_tokens` gained `purpose` (`refresh`|`device`|`activation`) + `used_at` (migration `008`, additive — existing rows backfill to `refresh`). `POST /api/v1/auth/activate` consumes a single-use code (`used_at` set) and mints a 1-year device token; `python -m src.activate --profile <name>` mints the `…/activate#code=…` link. Web: `/activate` routes the code through `AuthContext.activateDevice()`, and the token layer treats a non-JWT token as a never-expiring device token (no refresh attempts). *Why / gotchas:* nothing is deleted, so PIN login is an untouched fallback and the step is fully reversible (#74). Two production-only fixes proved load-bearing during the live bring-up: **(a)** an unset `VITE_API_URL` must resolve to **same-origin** in production (not `http://localhost:8000`), or the CSP blocks `/api/v1/auth/activate`; **(b)** `/activate` must go through the auth context rather than writing `localStorage` directly, or it navigates before React knows the user is signed in and bounces to `/login`. First deployed via break-glass; now Git-backed on `main` (`/api/v1/health` reports a real SHA again). Phases 2 (hide the PIN form) and 3 (delete PIN/JWT/lockout, drop dead columns — closes review P1-1/P1-3/P3-1/2/3) remain pending.

78. **Shipped the three P3 hardening findings from the v1+v2 review (PR #17).** **P3-7:** `/api/docs`, `/api/redoc`, `/api/openapi.json` are now `None` in production (via a testable `config.docs_urls(environment)` helper), so a private app no longer exposes its full schema anonymously — verified live (`/api/docs` → 404 in prod); dev/staging keep them. Consequence: future `/closeout` route checks must probe routes directly (they 401) rather than read the prod OpenAPI. **P3-5:** the prod secrets validator now also requires `jwt_access_secret`/`jwt_refresh_secret` to be ≥32 chars **and** distinct (not just non-placeholder); the live prod secrets are 64-char + distinct, so it gates startup without affecting the current deploy. **P3-6:** `pg_dump` no longer receives the DB password in its DSN argv (visible to `ps`); the DSN is sanitised and the password is passed via the `PGPASSWORD` subprocess env (URL-decoded). *Why:* all three are low-risk defence-in-depth for a private health-data app; each ships with unit tests. Remaining review items P3-4 (scheduler per-profile isolation) and P3-9 (vestigial `SiteRole`, test warnings) are optional and untouched.

### 2026-06-23 — Auth Phase 2 live (review closeout)

79. **Auth simplification Phase 2 is live — the PWA now leads with device-token activation and hides the PIN form behind a fallback toggle (PR #19; executes the #73–74 plan's step 2).** `LoginPage` defaults to an "Invite only — ask Craig for an activation link" screen; the PIN form (name + PIN + Forgot PIN) is revealed only via a "Use a PIN instead" toggle, with a Back link. Because Phase 1 already made the token layer device-aware (`getAuthToken()` prefers the device token, refresh is skipped for non-JWT tokens, a device-token 401 clears and redirects), the cutover needed **no** `api.ts`/`AuthContext`/routing changes — only the unauthenticated UX. *Two deliberate deviations from the plan's literal Phase-2 steps, kept conservative because Phase 2 is reversible:* the JWT silent-refresh in `api.ts` is **kept** (the still-live PIN fallback needs its 30-day refresh; it's removed in Phase 3), and the explicit `GET /api/v1/me`-on-load is **skipped** (a revoked device token is already caught by the first authenticated fetch's 401 → clear → invite screen). *Why:* device tokens are now the default sign-in path while PIN stays a reachable, reversible fallback (`/login` → "Use a PIN instead"); Mark, already activated in Phase 1, is unaffected. Verified live: the new invite copy is present in the prod Vercel bundle, `/login` 200, no console errors; frontend-only, so `/health` (backend) is unchanged. Phase 3 (delete the PIN/JWT/lockout code + endpoints, drop the dead `pin_hash`/`failed_login_count`/`locked_until` columns and the JWT secrets, remove the refresh logic — closes review P1-1/P1-3/P3-1/2/3 and retires the `1234` PIN) remains, to land after Phase 2 soaks.

### 2026-06-23 — Phase 3 Batch 19 (strength watching-brief)

80. **The strength watching-brief is a deterministic, advisory-only engine that classifies strength sessions via the existing `exclude_from_recovery` flag and computes rolling frequency/volume/load-proxy rollups over two windows (4 weeks, 12 weeks) without a new table, a new migration, or any write to recovery/verdict state.** `is_strength_activity` delegates entirely to `activity.exclude_from_recovery` set at Garmin sync time (Batch 8 wrist-HR detection, Decision #49) — no duplicate type-key logic and no new classification code. `compute_strength_rollup` is a pure function over `StrengthSession` sequences: it computes `WindowStats` (session count, total duration, total load proxy, sessions/week) for both windows, and derives a trend (`increasing` / `stable` / `decreasing` / `insufficient_data`) by comparing the first-half vs second-half rate of the 4-week window. `StrengthBriefService.brief` is a thin DB wrapper that reads `Activity` rows where `exclude_from_recovery=True` within the 12w lookback and calls the pure engine — it never writes. The result (`StrengthBriefResult`) is added to `DailyLoopSnapshot` and exposed via `GET /api/v1/strength-brief`; the daily-loop router serialises it as `strengthBrief` in the existing `{data, meta, errors}` envelope. *Recovery-isolation invariant (#49/#80) explicitly unit-tested:* `StrengthBriefResult` must not carry verdict/recovery fields (tested via `__dataclass_fields__`), and `is_strength_activity` must not mutate `exclude_from_recovery` on any `Activity`. *Why:* mirrors the Batches 13/14/16/17 pattern — deterministic pure-function engines are inspectable, unit-testable without a DB, and don't depend on `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`; the advisory-only design keeps the engine migration-free and the recovery-isolation invariant preserved. No LLM, no new table, no scheduler job.

### 2026-06-23 — Phase 3 Batch 20 (weekly & monthly deep reviews)

81. **The weekly/monthly deep review splits into a *deterministic* rollup packet (DB-free, unit-testable) and a *narrative* generated through the thin Anthropic Messages boundary reused from Batch 6 (#47) — stored in `analyses` under new `analysis_type` values `weekly_review` / `monthly_review`, migration-free.** `compute_review_rollup` (in `services/reviews.py`) is a pure function over plain samples (`ReviewDay` / `ReviewActivity` / `ReviewAdherence` / `ReviewThermalNight`) that aggregates a period's sleep, recovery/HRV/readiness, training load + adherence, morning verdicts and thermal/environment into reproducible averages, counts, by-type load, and first-half-vs-second-half trends. `ReviewService` is the thin DB wrapper: it reads the rows, **reuses** the Batch 19 `StrengthBriefService` and the Batch 17 `InsightsService` (FTP-drift + early-warning) rather than recomputing them, and assembles the packet. The weekly and monthly variants share *all* rollup + boundary machinery, differing only in the calendar window. **Period windows are calendar-aligned** — weekly = ISO week (Mon–Sun) containing `as_of`, monthly = calendar month — so the period start is a stable `subject_date` and `run` is **idempotent per period** (returns the existing review unless `force=True`). Following #71, the engine is **human/API-triggered, not a scheduler cron**: `GET /api/v1/reviews/{period}` previews the packet + latest stored narrative and **never writes**; `POST /api/v1/reviews/{period}/run` generates and records. The data-quality guardrails (no L/R balance, SpO2/HRV reliability window, wrist-HR strength excluded from recovery, ignore the broken Duration column) are carried in the packet and reinforced in the system prompt. A read-only Reviews PWA tab (`/reviews`) renders the deterministic summary cards and the on-demand narrative. *Why:* unlike the deterministic-only engines of Batches 14/16/17/19, a periodic review is inherently *narrative*, so it reuses the inspectable, fakeable-in-tests Anthropic boundary (#47) for the prose while keeping every number deterministic and unit-testable (the v3 boundary rule). Reusing Batch 17/19 outputs avoids duplicating insight maths; calendar-aligned idempotency keeps the audit log a clean one-review-per-period record; and reusing `analyses` keeps the batch migration-free (mirrors #62/#71/#80). The boundary establishes the review machinery that Batches 21 and 23 reuse.

### 2026-06-23 — Phase 3 Batch 21 (year-on-year & seasonal trends)

82. **The year-on-year & seasonal trend engine mirrors the Batch 20 split — a *deterministic* windowing/aggregation half (DB-free, unit-testable) plus an *optional narrative* generated through the Batch 20 Anthropic boundary (#47/#81), reused with a trend-specific system prompt — stored in `analyses` under the new `analysis_type='seasonal_trend'`, migration-free.** `services/trends.py`: `compute_trend_windows` is a pure function over plain `TrendSample` values that buckets daily history into comparable **month** (`2026-07`) or **season** (`2026-summer`, meteorological; December rolls into the next year's winter) windows and computes per-metric summary stats (count/mean/median/min/max) over nine metrics (sleep score/duration, HRV, readiness, resting HR, VO2 max, SpO2, indoor peak, outdoor overnight low). The **SpO2/HRV reliability cutoff (#45)** is honoured *in the aggregation*: rows before `RELIABILITY_START_DATE` (2026-06-11) are dropped from those two gated metrics only and surfaced as an explicit `excludedCount` (the `metric_baselines` provenance pattern, #44) — all other history stays intact. `compute_year_on_year` lines a window up against the same period one calendar year earlier (`prior_year_key`) and computes same-period deltas per metric, requiring **≥`MIN_YOY_SAMPLES` (5)** in *both* the current and prior-year windows; with no qualifying metric the comparison is `insufficient_history` overall (the expected state until ~Mar 2027, since history starts ~24 Mar 2026). `TrendsService` is the thin DB wrapper (reads `daily_metrics` / `sleep` / `weather_daily` / `temperature_readings`, never recomputing other engines). Following #71 the engine is **human/API-triggered**: `GET /api/v1/trends/seasonal`, `GET /api/v1/trends/year-on-year`, and `GET /api/v1/trends/narrative` preview and **never write**; only `POST /api/v1/trends/narrative/run` records. The narrative is **idempotent per window** (`subject_date` = canonical window start) and is disambiguated month-vs-season by a per-bucket `prompt_version` (`trends-month-v1` / `trends-season-v1`), since both can share a start date (e.g. summer and June both start 2026-06-01). **When history is insufficient the run reports `insufficient_history` deterministically and never calls the model.** A read-only Trends PWA tab (`/trends`) renders the YoY deltas, recent windows, and the on-demand narrative. The Batch 20 `AnthropicReviewClient` gained an optional `system_prompt` override (backward-compatible) so Batches 21/23 reuse the boundary with their own prompt. *Why:* the seasonal lens is inherently *narrative* like Batch 20, so it reuses the inspectable, fakeable-in-tests boundary for prose while every number stays deterministic and unit-testable (the v3 boundary rule); honouring #45 in the aggregation and surfacing sample/excluded counts keeps comparisons trustworthy; graceful insufficient-history (never inventing a prior-year number) matches #71's sample-size gates; and reusing `analyses` keeps the batch migration-free (mirrors #62/#71/#80/#81).

### 2026-06-23 — Phase 3 Batch 22 (hypothesis evaluation)

83. **Hypothesis evaluation is a *deterministic, advisory* engine that reuses the Batch 17 insights math (`_slope`/`pearson`/`compute_drivers`) to recommend a conclusion per experiment, but never changes status — concluding stays the human-gated, terminal `POST /…/status` action (#72). No LLM, no migration; reuses `experiments`/`analyses`.** `services/experiment_evaluation.py` dispatches on the experiment's `slug` (set by the Batch 17 tracker) to one of three pure, DB-free evaluators, each surfacing its evidence window and reasons: **gate** (`collagen`) — counts the current run of *calendar-consecutive* nights at/above the age-adjusted sleep floor (`Sleep.age_adjusted_score`, falling back to `score`); a met gate (≥`gateNights`) recommends `supported`, else `inconclusive`. **correlation** (`early_waking_0400`) — Pearson-ranks the *measured* candidate drivers (overnight low °C from `weather_daily`, sleep stress) against an overnight-disruption proxy (`awake_sleep_sec`→minutes) via `compute_drivers`; |r|≥0.5 → `supported` (identifiable trigger), ≥0.3 → `inconclusive`, otherwise `refuted` (no measured trigger); drivers the hypothesis names but we don't capture (alcohol, late snack) are surfaced as a coverage gap, not silently dropped. **group_compare** (`recovery_week_disruption`) — before/after comparison of mean age-adjusted sleep on recovery-week vs build-week nights, labelled from the containing `plan_blocks.block_type`; recovery worse by ≥3 points → `supported`, better → `refuted`, inside the band → `inconclusive`. Every evaluator **skips with an explicit reason** below its sample gate (#71): gate needs ≥5 scored nights, correlation ≥8 paired nights, group compare ≥4 per group. User-created experiments fall back to the correlation evaluator when they declare `candidateDrivers`, else report `no_evaluator` ("conclude manually"). The recommendation maps onto the tracker's outcome vocabulary (`supported`/`refuted`/`inconclusive`) so **accepting it flows through the existing conclude path** unchanged. Following #71 the surface is human/API-triggered: `GET /api/v1/experiments/{id}/evaluate` previews and **never writes**; `POST /api/v1/experiments/{id}/evaluate/run` records an audit row in `analyses` (`analysis_type='experiment_evaluation'`, `prompt_version='experiment-eval:v1'`), **idempotent per (experiment, subject date)** (a row already present for that date is reused unless `force=True`; idempotency is keyed on `context_packet.experimentId` since many experiments share a date). The router exposes `canConclude` (true only on a non-concluded experiment with an actionable recommendation) so the PWA only offers the terminal action when it's legal. A new read-only Experiments PWA tab (`/experiments`, "Tests") lists the hypotheses and, per card, evaluates the evidence and offers "Conclude as <recommendation>" wired to `POST /…/status`. *Why:* unlike the narrative batches (20/21), evaluation is a *safety/accuracy* judgement, so — like Batches 13/14/16/17/19 — it's inspectable, unit-testable arithmetic that works without `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`; reusing the Batch 17 slope/Pearson math avoids a second copy of the insight stats; the never-auto-conclude guard (no status write anywhere in the engine or `/evaluate`) is explicitly unit-tested, keeping `concluded` human-gated and terminal (#72); and reusing `experiments`/`analyses` keeps the batch migration-free (mirrors #62/#71/#72/#80/#81/#82). The standing hypotheses' alcohol/late-snack triggers aren't captured by any synced source, so the correlation evaluator reports them as an unmeasured-coverage gap rather than pretending to rule them out.

### 2026-06-23 — Phase 3 Batch 23 (auto-generated handover-doc export — v3 capstone)

84. **The handover export splits into a *deterministic* assembler + markdown render (DB-free, unit-testable, always available) and an *optional narrative* generated through the Batch 20 Anthropic boundary (#47/#81/#82) — stored in `analyses` under the new `analysis_type='handover_export'`, migration-free.** This is the #13 capstone: the app generates the "handover doc" Mark used to hand-write to brief an AI, by pulling all retained state into one portable export. `services/handover.py`: `build_handover_packet` is a pure function over plain values that composes the full living state — the knowledge base (only the six known sections: `profile`, `data_quality_rules`, `age_adjustment`, `sleep_protocol`, `training_plan`, `active_hypotheses`, in hand-doc order; arbitrary sections are dropped so the shape is deterministic), the current plan/block + upcoming active workouts, `metric_baselines`, the most recent weekly + monthly reviews (Batch 20), the seasonal year-on-year comparison (Batch 21, reused via `TrendsService`), the experiments + their latest deterministic evaluation (Batch 22, reused via `ExperimentEvaluationService`), and the strength watching-brief (Batch 19). The data-quality rules ride in `knowledgeBase.data_quality_rules` **and** are echoed under `dataQualityGuardrails` so a consumer cannot miss them. `render_handover_markdown` is a second pure function that renders the packet into a portable markdown handover doc **deterministically — no model, no API key** — so the export always works and faithfully reflects current retained state (the round-trip guarantee, 23.4); it surfaces left/right power balance only as a *rule to obey*, never as advice (explicitly tested: the phrase appears exactly once, inside the rules section). `HandoverService.run` polishes the doc through the thin Anthropic boundary reused with a handover-specific `HANDOVER_SYSTEM_PROMPT`, stored with `prompt_version='handover-v1-2026-06-23'` / `model_name` / raw response, **idempotent per day** (`subject_date` = the as-of date); fakeable in tests without `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`. Following #71 the surface is human/API-triggered: `GET /api/v1/handover` previews the packet + deterministic markdown + latest stored narrative and **never writes** (experiments are listed with `seed=False` so even the lazy-seed can't fire on a GET — the standing hypotheses still appear via the KB `active_hypotheses` section, keeping the handover faithful pre-seed); `POST /api/v1/handover/run` generates + records; `GET /api/v1/handover/export` downloads the deterministic markdown as a `text/markdown` attachment. A new read-only Handover PWA tab (`/handover`) shows the deterministic export preview, a "Download .md" button (client-side Blob from the already-returned markdown — no extra round-trip), and a "Generate narrative" button wired to `/run`. *Why:* like the narrative batches (20/21) the prose is inherently *narrative*, so it reuses the inspectable, fakeable-in-tests boundary; but a handover **must not depend on the model being reachable**, so the deterministic packet→markdown render is the floor that always reflects retained state (the #13 round-trip), with the LLM narrative an optional polish on top. Reusing every prior batch's service (no recomputation) keeps the capstone a thin integrator; reusing `analyses` keeps it migration-free (mirrors #62/#71/#80/#81/#82/#83).

### 2026-06-24 — Historical Garmin backfill (operate/soak)

85. **Historical data is loaded by a standalone *resumable* backfill CLI that re-drives the existing daily sync over past dates — not a new sync path, not a migration, and (for history) activity *summaries* only.** `apps/api/src/garmin_history_backfill.py` walks a `--start`/`--end` range and, per day, calls the same `GarminConnectClient.fetch_daily_payloads` + `GarminSyncService.sync_daily` the 06:30 job uses, plus monthly-chunked `sync_activities`. It commits per-day and skips days that already have a `daily_metrics` row (`--skip-existing`, default), wraps each fetch in exponential backoff, paces with `--throttle`, isolates per-day failures, and previews with `--dry-run`; `--no-activity-details` keeps a year-long pull to activity summaries only. Run via `railway run --service api` so the prod `GARMIN_TOKENSTORE_B64` + `DATABASE_URL` are injected and rows land in prod Supabase. Used 2026-06-24 to load a gapless 2025-06-24 → 2026-06-24 year for Mark (366 days metrics+sleep, 673 activity summaries; PR #27). *Why:* the sync layer was already date-parametrized and idempotent, so a backfill is a thin driver over it, not new logic — and reusing it guarantees backfilled rows are shaped exactly like live-synced rows. Resumability (per-day commit + skip-existing) was essential because the agent sandbox reaps background jobs at turn boundaries; the run still reached full coverage across several restarts, and re-running is always safe. Summaries-only for history was a deliberate cost trade: the dry-run showed ~1,500 activities/yr, so per-second time-series would mean ~1,500 extra detail calls + hundreds of thousands of `activity_timeseries` rows for little marginal value to the v3 trend/review engines (which read summaries) — re-runnable without the flag for a window if deep per-ride analysis is ever needed. The goal was to mature the v3 long-horizon engines (#82) on real data now rather than waiting until ~Mar 2027; verified directly against prod (5 season windows; a real June-over-June year-on-year), with the #45 SpO2/HRV reliability cutoff honoured in the aggregation and the un-backfillable Hive indoor-temperature history (no historical API) both surfacing as honest gaps rather than bad numbers.

### 2026-06-24 — Scheduler reliability (Hive feed stall)

86. **The in-process APScheduler is treated as best-effort, not the source of truth for scheduled work: jobs are made runnable standalone (`python -m src.run_scheduled <job>`) so an external scheduler can drive them, and interval jobs are seeded to fire shortly after startup.** Root cause of the stalled Hive feed (only 2 readings ever, both manual): every scheduled job runs in-process inside the web container (`main.py` lifespan → `create_scheduler`), which is only reliable if the container runs continuously — and in prod it does not (frequent restarts / idle-cycling), so the plain 15-minute Hive interval rarely reached its first fire (start + 15 min) while the +5-minute-seeded activity poll occasionally did, and the wall-clock jobs (06:30 morning sync, evening nudges) only fired if the container happened to be awake. The poll itself is healthy: a manual run writes a reading immediately, and the token / profile / Hive API all work. Fix is two-part: (1) **band-aid** — seed the Hive poll with `next_run_time = now + 2 min` (mirroring the activity poll) so a freshly started container polls within ~2 min instead of waiting a full interval (the test asserts both interval jobs are seeded); (2) **durable** — a new `src/run_scheduled.py` runs any single named job to completion and exits, mapping job names to the existing `run_*` coroutines (identical behaviour, no duplicated logic), so jobs can be driven by Railway Cron / GitHub Actions / a manual `railway run` independent of the web container's lifecycle; `docs/runbooks/scheduled-jobs-cron.md` documents the schedules and the cutover (`SCHEDULER_ENABLED=false` once external cron is verified, since the jobs are idempotent and can overlap briefly). *Why:* binding all scheduling to a single web container's uptime is the actual defect; decoupling execution from that container — via a standalone runner that reuses the scheduler functions — makes scheduled work survive restarts/idle-cycling, and the band-aid ships immediate relief without waiting for the cron wiring. **DST caveat:** Railway cron is UTC and does not track Europe/London BST↔GMT, so the timezone-agnostic interval jobs (`hive-poll`/`activity-poll`/`backup`) move to cron cleanly, but the wall-clock jobs are best kept on in-process APScheduler (which handles DST via `timezone=Europe/London`) with the container made always-on — or accept ±1h drift. **Open:** whether to fully retire in-process APScheduler or run a hybrid is deferred until external cron is wired and the always-on / Railway "App Sleeping" question is settled in the dashboard.

**Correction (2026-06-24, same day):** after Railway **App Sleeping was disabled** (the container now stays up — confirmed: the +5-min activity poll fired at 12:52 and the 15-min Hive interval fired *on schedule* at 13:02), the Hive poll's *real* prod failure finally surfaced in the logs: `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'pyhiveapi'`. **`pyhiveapi` was missing from `apps/api/requirements.txt`** (the Dockerfile installs only that file), so the poll fired in prod but raised immediately — and every earlier "a manual run writes a reading" check passed *only* because `railway run` executes against the **local venv**, which had `pyhiveapi` installed ad-hoc and never tracked. So the primary Hive-specific blocker was the **missing dependency**, not the scheduler; fixed by adding `pyhiveapi>=0.5.16` to `requirements.txt`. Disabling App Sleeping was still necessary (it makes the container stay up so the scheduler fires at all), and the seed / `run_scheduled` changes remain valid resilience. **Lesson:** `railway run` validates code against the *local* venv, not the deployed image — verify dependency-sensitive prod behaviour from the container logs, not a local invocation.

### 2026-06-24 — Wake-triggered morning verdict

87. **The morning run fires when Mark *actually wakes* (detected from his Garmin `sleepEnd`), not on a fixed 06:30 cron — in-process via a `wake_check` interval job that polls sleep every ~15 min and triggers the *unchanged* `run_morning_weather_sync` once his wake is stable, with a 09:30 backstop.** The backfill made the case quantitative: across 363 nights his median wake is **08:22** (range 03:45–09:24) and he wakes after 06:30 on **98.6 %** of mornings, so the legacy 06:30 cron fired ~2 h before he woke almost every day — reading a pre-dawn placeholder for time-of-day-live Training Readiness and an unfinalized sleep score. **Mechanism:** a new pure decision core `services/wake_detection.py::is_morning_ready(today, sleep, *, prev_sleep_end, now, backstop, duration_floor_min, settle_min) → WakeDecision{fire|wait|nap_ignored, sleep_end_to_persist, reason}` (no I/O, exhaustively unit-tested), driven by `scheduler.run_wake_check()`. Per poll, per active profile, within the window (03:30–10:00 Europe/London): short-circuit if today's morning analysis already exists (cheap `analyses` read, no Garmin call — stops polling for the rest of the day); else a **light sleep-only Garmin poll** (new `GarminConnectClient.fetch_sleep` = the single `get_sleep_data` call, not the ~10-call `fetch_daily_payloads`); apply the **back-to-sleep stability guard**; persist the current `sleepEnd` as a `wake_check` audit row for the next poll's comparison; if ready, run `run_morning_weather_sync` once. **The stability guard is the key correctness point:** Garmin records one consolidated overnight session (brief awakenings are awake epochs *inside* it), but a genuine two-block night can close the first session early — so we never fire on first detection. Fire only once today's `sleepEnd` (a) equals the value persisted on the previous poll (unchanged ≈ stable across two consecutive ~15-min polls) **and** (b) sits ≥ `settle_min` (20 min) in the past **and** (c) the session clears a `duration_floor_min` (180 min) that excludes naps. A *later* `sleepEnd` than last poll means he drifted back to sleep → keep waiting and persist the later value until it settles at his true get-up. Cost: the verdict lands ~15–20 min after wake rather than instantly — a fair trade for never building it on a half-night. **Backstop (belt-and-suspenders):** a dedicated `morning_backstop` cron at 09:30 Europe/London runs `run_morning_weather_sync` directly, **and** `is_morning_ready` fires on `now ≥ backstop` regardless of the data, so a verdict is guaranteed even if wake was never detected (watch not worn / never synced / container down through the window) whether the in-process scheduler or external cron drives it. **State is migration-free** — the last-seen `sleepEnd` + idempotency live in the existing `analyses` table (`analysis_type='wake_check'`, one row per (user, day), updated in place; `context_packet.sleepEndUtc` carries the value), and the verdict's once-per-day guarantee reuses the existing morning-analysis idempotency (`generate_and_store` short-circuits per `subject_date`). **Wiring:** replaces the 06:30 `morning_weather_sync` cron in `create_scheduler()` with the `wake_check` interval job (15 min, seeded `next_run_time = now + 3 min`) + the `morning_backstop` cron; adds `wake-check` to `run_scheduled.JOBS` so an external cron can drive it too. *Why now:* settled by DECISIONS #86 — App Sleeping is off so the container is always-on and in-process APScheduler fires reliably and handles BST↔GMT via `timezone=Europe/London` (a UTC external cron would drift ±1 h on the window/backstop bounds, so wake detection stays in-process; the `run_scheduled` entry is resilience, not the primary path). *Why reuse `run_morning_weather_sync` unchanged:* only the **trigger** changes, not the verdict — the sync/analysis/Amber-regen pipeline and its per-profile idempotency are untouched, so this is a thin integrator over proven code. **Known single-subject simplification:** `run_morning_weather_sync` serves *all* active profiles, so when any one profile is ready the whole sync fires; for a 2nd user who has not yet woken that means a verdict on whatever data exists today (and the morning-idempotency then blocks a later fresh one). Acceptable for this 1–2 user app (effectively just Mark); a per-profile trigger would require changing `run_morning_weather_sync`, which the design deliberately keeps unchanged. **Calibration constants** (`WINDOW_START/END`, `BACKSTOP`, `DURATION_FLOOR_MIN`, `SETTLE_MIN`) are tuned to Mark's distribution and live in `wake_detection.py`; retune there if his schedule shifts. Full design + decision matrix in `docs/designs/wake-triggered-morning.md`.

### 2026-06-24 — Metric baselines from DB history

88. **`metric_baselines` is (re)computed from the stored `daily_metrics` + `sleep` history, not the 84-night xlsx, via a small admin CLI that reuses the xlsx importer's statistical core under a distinct `db_history` source.** Context: the year-history backfill (#85) loaded a gapless 366 nights into prod but **left `metric_baselines` empty for Mark** (the xlsx import — Batch 4, the only thing that ever wrote baselines — was never applied to prod), so the morning "Metrics vs Baselines" read (ARCHITECTURE §4) was silently falling back to the static knowledge-base profile bands instead of history-derived stats.
