Rather than belatedly run the xlsx (84 stale nights, 24 Mar–15 Jun) I derived the baselines from the *real* DB history we now hold. **Mechanism:** the per-metric statistics in `services/sleep_history.py` were extracted into a pure, source-parametrized core `compute_metric_baselines(samples: Sequence[BaselineSample], *, source) → list[dict]` (mean/median/min/max/quartiles/stddev, the #45 SpO2/HRV reliability cutoff applied as before — pre-2026-06-11 SpO2/HRV dropped from those two metrics only and surfaced as `excluded_sample_count` with `reliability_start_date` recorded); the xlsx path (`build_metric_baselines`) is now a thin wrapper that feeds `SleepHistoryRow`s through that core, so its output is identical and its tests are unchanged. A new `services/metric_baselines.py::MetricBaselineBackfillService.rebuild` reads `sleep` + `daily_metrics`, joins them per calendar day into `BaselineSample`s **using the exact column mapping of `morning_analysis._metrics_vs_baselines` `current_values`** (so the persisted baseline and the live "current" value are drawn from the same fields — RHR coalesces the daily-metric reading over the sleep reading), computes over a configurable trailing window, and upserts idempotently (dry-run supported). The CLI is `python -m src.metric_baselines_backfill` (run via `railway run --service api`, DB-only — no Garmin/Hive egress), mirroring the #85 backfill runner. **Window = trailing 84 nights by default** (`--window-days`, `--all`, `--as-of` to override): matches the §5 "84-night summary stats" design and the sports-science norm that a *current* personal baseline tracks recent fitness/seasonal state rather than a full year that would blend winter and summer — though the #45 cutoff independently caps SpO2/HRV to post-2026-06-11 regardless of window. **Distinct `db_history` source** keeps provenance honest (#44) and means these rows never collide with the xlsx `(user_id, metric_key, source)` unique key; the morning read consumes **all** baselines for a user irrespective of source, and an empty table remains the graceful KB-band fallback (structural — `_metrics_vs_baselines` emits one row per existing baseline), so this change only ever *adds* the richer read, never breaks the floor. *Why a CLI over a scheduler job:* baselines drift slowly and recomputation is cheap + idempotent, so like #71/#85 this stays human/API-triggered, not a new cron — re-run it periodically (e.g. as more reliable HRV/SpO2 nights accumulate past the cutoff) to refresh. **No deploy was required for prod to benefit:** the morning read path was already live, so persisting the rows lit up the table immediately; the code only needs to land on `main` for the recomputation to be reproducible. Applied to prod 2026-06-24 (default 84-night window 2026-04-02 → 2026-06-24): 7 baselines written under `db_history` — e.g. sleep_score median 74 (IQR 68–80, n=81), RHR median 44 (n=84), and SpO2 n=11/excluded=69, HRV n=14/excluded=70 with `reliability_start_date=2026-06-11` — and `_metrics_vs_baselines` verified to return 7 populated rows (was 0).

### 2026-06-25 — Brand name

89. **The app's brand name is "CheckMark", with a checkmark (✓) as the logo mark — superseding the Phase-0 placeholder "GARMIN / COACH" text wordmark (#23).** *Why:* the name pulls triple duty — (a) the product's headline output is a daily morning Green/Amber/Red verdict (#14, ARCHITECTURE §4), and a ✓ reads as "approved / all-clear / good to go", so the mark literally *describes the core feature*; (b) "Mark" is the sole user, so the name is quietly personal to exactly the audience that matters; (c) a checkmark is a trivial, instantly-recognisable glyph that doubles as the PWA icon, favicon, and push-notification mark for free. Trademark collision is irrelevant — 1–2 private users, no public sign-up (#2/#21). **Rejected:** "Harminy" (a Hive+Garmin portmanteau) — it reads as a misspelling of "harmony" (a permanent spoken/typed-spelling tax) and the Hive half barely survives the blend, so the "mix of both sources" story never lands. **Status: name chosen; app icon + PWA manifest implemented 2026-06-25.** The icon set is the ECG-checkmark mark (a bold white checkmark that doubles as a heartbeat trace) on a deep-teal→fresh-green tile with a faint Green/Amber/Red verdict-gauge arc behind it — all regenerated deterministically from `apps/web/generate-icons.mjs` (master art in code → `@resvg/resvg-js` → favicon/SVG/PNG/maskable/Apple set), replacing the inherited Calcio target-ball assets. The home-screen name, favicon, Apple-touch + maskable icons, and social meta now read "CheckMark" (`vite.config.ts` manifest + `index.html`). **In-app wordmark + theme shift also implemented 2026-06-25 (same day):** the splash/header wordmark is now the two-line "Check / Mark" lockup (the `brand` tokens in `theme/tokens.ts`; the inherited brass-gold `--wordmark-gradient` rethemed to a teal→green that echoes the icon), and every user-facing "Garmin Coach" string (login, activation, onboarding, install, unlock) now reads "CheckMark". The dark theme shifted off the inherited cool-navy-graphite surfaces to a **deep teal-graphite** ramp (`--bg #0A1112` … `--border-strong #345355`, mirrored in `tokens.ts`) so the chrome harmonizes with the icon, and the PWA `theme-color` / manifest `theme_color`+`background_color` moved from the *mismatched* navy `#071A3D` to `#0A1112` (it now matches the app background). Because that status-bar hex lives inside the CSP-pinned inline theme-apply script, the `vercel.json` `script-src` hash was regenerated to `sha256-QY4bpzMUdH+mk0/4LkojnHpgTlsQqmT5edgIsAQV3r0=` (the #76 maintenance gotcha). **Deliberately left as-is:** the primary brand was already emerald green (`--primary #10B981`) so it is unchanged; the **gold `--accent`** (used by the button/badge `accent` variants) is kept as a warm secondary (green+gold+teal reads premium, and the on-accent AA contrast was verified for gold); light mode stays neutral off-white. Verified live on the Node-20 dev preview — the login splash renders the teal "Check/Mark" wordmark on the `#0A1112` bg with `theme-color` matching and no console errors. The in-app identity now matches the icon; revisit only if a public-facing identity is ever needed (it isn't, for a private app).

### 2026-06-26 — World-class UI/UX redesign

90. **The PWA was redesigned screen-by-screen for "professional + simple for Mark + serves his original requirements", treating the finished v1→v3 feature set as the input and changing only the presentation layer — no backend coaching logic, no DB migration.** Context: with all functionality shipped and soaking, the app still *read* as a developer's dashboard rather than a coach for a 57-year-old. Reviewing against Mark's own docs (`~/Downloads/Dad Fitness/` — App Optimisations wishlist, Handover Document, AI Daily Check-in; captured in memory `reference_dad_requirements_docs`) surfaced five gaps that each map to an explicit ask: (a) the AI output was dumped into `whitespace-pre-wrap` divs with **no markdown renderer**, so his "**put each point's headline in bold**" request rendered as literal `**asterisks**` and any table as raw `| pipes |`; (b) the **Metrics-vs-Baselines table** he specifically wanted (the Copilot "Metric | Last night | Baseline | Status ✔/⚠" grid) was *computed server-side and then hidden* — `morning_analysis._metrics_vs_baselines` builds it into `analysis.context_packet["metricsVsBaselines"]` but the daily-loop serializer never returned it; (c) navigation was a 10-tab mobile bottom bar (10px text, unusable on a phone) while the desktop top-nav exposed only 3 of those 10 routes (7 unreachable); (d) Home was a 774-line kitchen-sink mixing the read (verdict/sleep/metrics) with two big write forms (manual check-in + per-workout adherence); (e) engineer-speak throughout ("Daily Loop", "adherence", "propose→approve→push", "hypothesis evaluation"). **Decisions taken (with the user, in plan mode):** full redesign (not audit-only or targeted), simplify nav for Mark (primary tabs + tuck admin tools), verify with live before/after screenshots. **Approach & key choices:** (1) add `react-markdown`+`remark-gfm` behind a themed `components/Markdown.tsx` (XSS-safe — no raw HTML) and route all five AI-output surfaces through it; (2) surface the *already-computed* `metricsVsBaselines` additively (`routers/daily_loop.py` `AnalysisOut` + shared `dailyLoopAnalysisSchema`, **no migration**) and render it in `components/MetricsBaselineTable.tsx` with direction-aware ✔/⚠ status derived from the trailing-window quartile band (higher-is-better vs lower-is-better per metric) — chosen over relying on the model to format a markdown table each day so the table is reliable and matches his Copilot example exactly; (3) IA = **Home · Plan · Trends · More** with the secondary/admin destinations (Plan builder, Holiday, Tests, Coach state, Handover, Settings) behind a `MoreMenu` sheet (mobile) / dropdown (desktop), single-sourced in `lib/navConfig.ts`; (4) Home rebuilt read-first (verdict hero → last night's sleep w/ age-band REM context → baselines table → today's training incl. strength green-lit → the rendered coach read → post-workout → thermal) with the check-in + adherence forms moved to a focused `pages/CheckInPage.tsx` behind a primary CTA; (5) **Plan** shows Mark's *whole* fixed week Mon–Sun incl. strength/flexibility (today lit by the daily-loop verdict) above the de-jargoned Zwift delivery — the week is a **frontend const of his documented, fixed structure, NOT a new endpoint**, because the existing `workout_delivery.list_week_ahead` is bike-only *by design* (Decision #31) and widening it would re-litigate a settled decision and risk the delivery contract; (6) Trends gets real **recharts** line charts (the dep was installed but unused). **Gotcha recorded:** recharts does **not** resolve CSS `var(--x)` in SVG stroke *attributes* (only in `style`/`fill` objects), so chart strokes pass concrete hex (imported from `theme/tokens`), and trend windows must be sorted oldest→newest for the line to read left-to-right. **Verification:** because the auth gate (`AuthContext`/`ProtectedRoute`) only reads `localStorage` with no server validation, the live walkthrough was done **prod-free** via a temporary Vite `configureServer` mock-API middleware + a localStorage session — minting a real prod device token via `railway run … src.activate` is blocked by the auto-mode safety classifier as a production write, so the mock path is preferred and needs no token; the temp config was reverted before commit (memory `ui-walkthrough-method` updated). Web typecheck + lint (0 errors) + 28 vitest (6 new: Markdown, MetricsBaselineTable, CheckInPage) + vite build; shared 7; backend ruff + mypy; full CI green on PR #35; prod smoke confirmed (`/api/v1/health` sha=`dea04da`, web 200, daily-loop 401). **Deliberately out of scope:** no change to the Anthropic morning/post-workout prompts (they already ask for bold headlines + the table — only the *rendering* was broken), no new endpoints, no auth Phase 3.

### 2026-06-27 — Batch 25 same-day workout delivery

91. **Same-day approval from Home supersedes the old two-day-ahead auto-push default (#31); the canonical path is now wake verdict → accept or manually override → approve and push immediately.** Mechanism: `POST /api/v1/workout-delivery/planned-workouts/{id}/send-today` is keyed by today's planned workout, reuses the existing `workout_delivery_proposals` table (#54), builds from the verdict-adjusted IR (`adjust_ir_for_verdict`, #61), optionally applies Mark's manual duration/intensity dials as a fresh `manual_override` IR, approves the proposal, and calls the existing intervals.icu rail in the same explicit action. The existing propose → approve → push rule (#29) is preserved as state transitions and audit rows (`workout_proposed` / `workout_pushed`); Red-never-VO2 is re-checked at this same-day gate before intervals.icu is called. `DEFAULT_LEAD_DAYS` is now `0`, so background auto-push only catches already-approved workouts due today rather than pre-sending future sessions. *Why:* after the Batch 24 daily-flow redesign, the product wants the morning's sleep-adjusted session to feel like a live coaching decision, not a plan that was silently staged days ahead. A direct same-day endpoint keeps the trainer write visibly under Mark's control and makes the exact pushed IR inspectable. **25.0 caveat:** this session did not perform a fresh manual Zwift latency check; the prior throwaway spike already proved intervals.icu API event creation and manual Zwift visibility, but same-day end-to-end latency still needs one live observation before `/closeout` should claim it as verified. The implementation chooses the direct live-push path; if that observation fails, the fallback is to pre-stage the base session overnight and push a same-day replacement/adjustment from the same proposal model.

### 2026-06-27 — Batch 26 post-ride check-in

92. **Post-ride subjective input reuses `manual_entries` with a nullable `activity_id`, rather than adding a new check-in table.** The morning manual entry stays the date-level row (`planned_workout_id IS NULL AND activity_id IS NULL`), planned-workout adherence stays linked to `planned_workout_id`, and after-ride RPE / legs / feel / niggles are stored as a third row shape linked to the Garmin `activities.id` (migration `009`). `PostWorkoutAnalysisService` includes the latest activity-linked check-in as `postRideCheckIn` in the context packet and considers an existing post-workout analysis stale when it does not cover the latest check-in, so the next post-workout generation incorporates Mark's felt experience without duplicating storage or requiring a second analysis table. *Why:* this mirrors Decision #48's "manual_entries is the daily subjective/adherence home" while giving Batch 8's activity-scoped analysis a precise FK. It also prevents late post-ride subjective scores from accidentally influencing the same day's morning verdict, because morning analysis now filters to the date-level manual entry only.

### 2026-06-28 — detailed per-ride/walk time-series backfill + bounded storage

93. **Per-second activity time-series is backfilled only for the types whose channels we actually analyse (cycling + walking), and the redundant `raw_metrics` JSON blob is dropped on write for the high-volume types to keep the free-tier DB under its cap.** Context: the #85 year backfill loaded activity *summaries* only (`--no-activity-details`), explicitly leaving the per-second `activity_timeseries` (power / HR / cadence / performance-condition / available+potential stamina / speed) for "a window if deep per-ride analysis is ever needed" (ARCHITECTURE §4 post-workout). This session loaded that detail for Mark's full history. **Scope = cycling + walking, not all types**, decided against the Supabase **free-tier 500 MB cap** (the project is shared with the movie app, #34): an all-types load projected to ~620 MB, and breathwork/strength/yoga per-second data has ~no coaching value. **Mechanism (CLI):** `garmin_history_backfill.py` gained a `--detail-types indoor_cycling,road_biking,cycling,walking` filter (threaded into `GarminConnectClient.fetch_activity_payloads`) that scopes the costly one-per-activity `get_activity_details` call to the named `activityType.typeKey`s — summaries are still backfilled for every type, only the details are filtered. Run via `railway run` over 2025-06-24 → 2026-06-27; all 13 month-chunks succeeded with no 429s, giving 203 rides + 387 walks per-second coverage (verified: power/HR/cadence/stamina populated, outdoor GPS preserved). **The cap bit anyway:** the re-sync also pulled in ~260 activity summaries the original run had missed (Garmin had backfilled more auto-tracked walks/breathwork since), and per-activity sample density ran higher than the pre-run estimate, so the load overshot to ~625 MB and the **physical disk filled** — at which point `VACUUM FULL` cannot run (no room to write the compacted copy). **Storage decision:** `activity_timeseries.raw_metrics` is a JSONB copy of the full Garmin sample map, but **every channel the analysis uses is already in a typed column and nothing in the codebase reads `raw_metrics`** (grep-verified) — its only non-redundant content is GPS lat/long + elevation on outdoor rides (the L/R pedal-balance channels it also carries are exactly the single-sided-meter data the data-quality rules forbid using — ARCHITECTURE §3). So `raw_metrics` is emptied for the two high-volume types: historically via `UPDATE … = '{}'` then a **dump → `TRUNCATE` → reload** (the only table shrink that needs no free space when the disk is already full — `VACUUM FULL`/`CLUSTER`/CTAS all need ~the new copy's size free; 508,293 rows round-tripped with zero loss, DB 625 → 248 MB), and going forward via `STRIP_RAW_METRICS_TYPES = {indoor_cycling, walking}` in `GarminSyncService.sync_activities`, so new live-poll rows of those types persist `{}`. **Outdoor rides (`road_biking`, `cycling`) keep `raw_metrics`** so their GPS/elevation survive. *Why:* the typed columns are the analysis contract; the JSON blob is pure storage cost on a hard-capped shared free tier, and stripping it on write makes the cleanup durable instead of a recurring chore. **Lessons:** size-project per-type from a real sample before any large free-tier load, and remember the disk-full ⇒ can't-`VACUUM FULL` trap — dump→`TRUNCATE`→reload is the escape hatch. The `--detail-types` filter + tests were already committed; the live-sync strip + this record land together. The live-sync strip only takes effect once merged to `main` (Railway auto-deploy).

### 2026-06-28 — surface already-captured Garmin load/activity context into the morning packet

94. **Garmin training-load + daily-activity signals that the sync already stores in `daily_metrics.raw_payload` are surfaced into the morning context packet — additive, no new Garmin fetch, no migration.** An audit of the validated sample shapes (`~/garmin-spike/out/`) confirmed the high-value load/activity data is *already pulled daily and stored* — the `fetch_daily_payloads` call keeps the full `training_status` + `stats` responses in `raw_payload`, but `_daily_metric_packet` only promoted ~18 fields, so the rest never reached Claude. `_training_and_activity_fields(raw_payload)` now reads, with safe nested navigation: **chronic training load** (`mostRecentTrainingStatus.latestTrainingStatusData.{device}.acuteTrainingLoadDTO.dailyTrainingLoadChronic`) → an **acute:chronic load ratio (ACWR)** computed against the already-promoted acute load; the **training-load balance** phrase (`mostRecentTrainingLoadBalance…trainingBalanceFeedbackPhrase`); and **steps + intensity minutes** (moderate+vigorous) from `stats`. These merge into `_daily_metric_packet`, and `SYSTEM_PROMPT` now tells Claude to use ACWR / chronic load / balance / intensity minutes as *supporting context*. **The deterministic Green/Amber/Red verdict (`_morning_verdict`) is unchanged** — it never consumed the packet dict, so this enriches the model's narrative/rationale only, not the rule output. *Why:* surfacing already-stored data is ~zero cost (no Garmin call, no storage, no migration) and gives the morning read real load-management context (ramp-rate / ACWR strain, aerobic balance, non-structured daily load). **Deliberately not fetched** (the "should we pull more from Garmin?" question): all-day HR/SpO2/respiration are the intraday volume trap on the free-tier cap (#93); `user_summary` duplicates `stats`; `body_composition` is empty for Mark (basic scale → `weigh_ins` only); and per-activity HR-zones/laps are derivable from the #93 per-second time-series rather than re-fetched. Held for later (lean first cut): the intraday stress + body-battery curves (`stressValuesArray`/`bodyBatteryValuesArray`, also already in `raw_payload`) and stress-duration split.

### 2026-06-28 — Batch 27.0 Dreo fan spike (direct-cloud control)

95. **The bedroom fan is driven over the *direct Dreo cloud* path via `pydreo_community` (no Home Assistant fallback needed), and the device is a `DR-HPF008S` "Air Circulator" — not the 508S the plan named.** The throwaway 27.0 spike (`~/dreo-spike/`, outside the repo like `~/garmin-spike`) proved the full control surface end-to-end against Mark's real fan: `login()` → `load_devices()` → **`start_transport()`** → power on/off, preset-mode, speed, oscillate, and a state read — every step physically confirmed by eye. **Device truth:** the only device on Mark's Dreo account is a `DR-HPF008S` (name "Air Circulator", `class=PyDreoAirCirculator`, `sn=1813458665562238978-b9d060fcd119e249:001:0000000000s`, `speed_range=(1, 9)`, `preset_modes=['normal','auto','sleep','natural','turbo']`), and Mark confirmed it *is* the bedroom fan — the "508S" in the plan/STATUS was simply a wrong label, so 27.1 targets this model + serial. **Chosen path = direct cloud:** `pydreo_community` 1.9.22 (imports as `pydreo`; the standalone PyPI lib the official `dreo-team/hass-dreoverse` wraps) talks straight to the Dreo cloud, so the HA-OS-hub fallback in the 27.0 plan is not needed (no extra home hardware). **Lifecycle the 27.1 wrapper must follow:** `PyDreo(user, pass)` → `login()` → `load_devices()` → `start_transport()` — which opens the command WebSocket on a background daemon thread; control setters raise `RuntimeError: Command transport disabled. Run start_transport first.` until it is up, and because the socket connects asynchronously the wrapper must wait for it to be ready before the first command — then drive the device via attribute setters (each send blocks on a device `control-report` ack, ~2 s timeout with retries) → `stop_transport()`. **Region auto-detects to EU, no config:** the `PyDreo(region=…)` constructor arg is cosmetic (it rejects lowercase `'eu'`, defaults to `NA`, warns), but `login()` reads the user's real region from the auth response and sets `auth_region`/`api_server_region=EU`, which builds the `wss://wsb-eu.dreo-tech.com/…` URL — login self-corrects; pass uppercase `'EU'` or omit to silence the warning. **Load-bearing control rule — mode-before-speed:** the `fan_speed` setter sends only the `WINDLEVEL` (1–9) and does not change the wind-*type*, so while any preset (`turbo`/`auto`/`sleep`/`natural`) is active the motor ignores the windlevel — the cloud echoes the new `fan_speed` in state but the fan does not physically change. Proven in the spike: speed 1→3 did nothing in `turbo`, then worked the instant `preset_mode` was set to `normal`; **so 27.2's "set speed to N" must send `preset_mode='normal'` then `fan_speed=N`.** **Auth/secrets:** the account creds (`DREO_USERNAME`/`DREO_PASSWORD`) authenticate and `login()` returns a 36-char token, so 27.1 mirrors the Hive/Garmin boundary — env creds plus a `DREO_TOKENSTORE_B64`-style cached-token path, held server-side, never frontend-exposed. **Open (not yet proven):** *token-resume* — every spike run logged in with username+password; resuming from a cached token without a password was not tested, so 27.1 should implement the token-store **with a password fallback**, and a ~2-minute follow-up spike can confirm pure resume. **Bonus:** the device reports a `temperature` attribute (≈70–79 across runs, looks like °F ambient) — a possible second indoor-temp source alongside Hive, noted not adopted. **Dependency gotcha (#86):** `pydreo_community` must be added to `apps/api/requirements.txt` (the Dockerfile installs only that file) or the prod control loop will `ModuleNotFoundError` exactly as the missing `pyhiveapi` silently broke the Hive poll.

### 2026-06-28 — Batch 27.2 overnight fan control loop

96. **The bedroom fan is driven by a stateless, idempotent overnight control loop: a pure decision core maps the live indoor temperature onto a bounded fan target (off, or on at a ladder speed) against the Batch 9 sleep-disruption thresholds, and a thin scheduler integrator reconciles only the difference through the 27.1 `DreoFanClient`.** Mirrors the #87 wake-detection split: `services/fan_control.py` is pure / no-I/O and exhaustively unit-tested — `loop_phase(now)` classifies the profile-local time into `control` / `winddown` / `idle`, and `decide_fan_action(phase, temperature_c, fan_state) → FanDecision(action, target_on, target_speed)`. `scheduler.run_fan_control()` is the integrator (a 15-min interval job seeded +4 min, plus a `fan-control` entry in `run_scheduled.JOBS` for external cron). **Temp→airflow mapping (the air-circulator is not a thermostat — it moves air, it cannot hold a setpoint):** turn on at `ON_THRESHOLD_C=19.5` (the Batch 9 warning line from `nudge_alerts.evaluate_thermal_alert`); a fixed, bounded speed ladder 19.5→3 / 20.0→5 / 21.0→7 capped at `MAX_SPEED=7` (never the device max of 9, so overnight airflow stays unobtrusive). **Hysteresis** prevents flapping: once running the fan stays on until the room falls below `OFF_THRESHOLD_C=19.0`. **Idempotency without persistent state:** each run reads the *current* fan state (a cheap cloud connect) and the core returns `action="hold"` when the fan already matches the target, so only genuine changes issue a command — no DB row, no migration. **Overnight only:** the control window is profile-local 21:30→08:30 (calibrated to Mark's #87 wake distribution, median 08:22); a short wind-down 08:30→09:00 forces the fan **off** so it is never left running into the day; outside both the loop is `idle` and makes **no cloud call at all** (so daytime manual use is not fought and cloud traffic is bounded to the night). **Graceful degradation** at every edge: no Dreo creds → skip; no active profile → skip; **no fresh indoor temperature (>45 min old) → `no_data`, hold** (never actuate blind); the fan/cloud unreachable → log a warning and return (the loop never raises, so a fan outage cannot break the scheduler). **DST-safe** like the other interval jobs (#86): the job fires on a timezone-agnostic 15-min interval but the window is evaluated in the profile's IANA zone via `_profile_now`, so BST↔GMT needs no special handling. Speed changes go through `DreoFanClient.set_speed`, which applies the #95 **mode-before-speed** rule (forces `normal` before `WINDLEVEL`). **Single fan / single bedroom simplification** (like #87): the app has one Dreo account (global env creds) and the loop manages the fan against the first active profile's freshest Hive reading — effectively Mark; a per-profile fan mapping would need a device↔profile link, deferred until a real 2nd fan exists. **Calibration constants** (window bounds, thresholds, ladder, max speed) live at the top of `fan_control.py`; retune there if Mark's schedule or comfort band shifts. **Deliberately deferred to 27.3:** a manual override + preferences + surfacing the fan state and the temp it is responding to in the evening Home state — until then the loop *fully owns* the fan overnight and the morning wind-down unconditionally turns it off (so daytime manual use, and keeping it on past 08:30, both wait on the 27.3 override). Tests: 34 (pure core — phases, thresholds, ladder bounds, hysteresis, idempotency; integrator — graceful degradation, on/off+speed wiring, freshness gate); ruff + strict mypy + full backend suite green (330 passed).

### 2026-06-28 — Batch 27.3 manual override + evening "Bedroom — Auto" surface

97. **The fan autopilot is gated by a single `Profile.fan_auto_enabled` boolean (master switch), and the UI shows the loop's *computed intent* — not a live device read — so the daily-loop payload stays cloud-free.** Resolves the three 27.3 design forks left open in #96. **(a) Override = one boolean column, not a table** (migration `010`, `server_default=true`): a single-fan/single-user simplification consistent with #96/#87, so no per-command history or schedule model. It gates the loop at the top of `run_fan_control` — `if not profile.fan_auto_enabled: return` *before* any cloud call — so when the user takes manual control the overnight loop (and its unconditional morning wind-down) no-ops entirely, fixing the #96 "the loop fully owns the fan overnight" gap. **(b) Exposing fan state without a per-request cloud connect:** rejected both forked options (persist the loop's last decision in a row vs. an on-demand device read on every `GET /daily-loop`) in favour of a *third* path — a pure `describe_fan_intent(now, temperature_c, *, auto_enabled)` that recomputes what the loop *would* do right now from the profile-local time + the freshest Hive temp + the auto flag, reusing `loop_phase` + `decide_fan_action` against an off baseline. It surfaces on the existing payload as `thermalState.fan` `{autoEnabled, mode, isOn, speed, respondingToC}` with `isOn=null` when unknown (manual mode, or no fresh temp). So the read path adds **no DB row, no migration beyond the flag, and no cloud I/O** — the daily-loop GET stays a pure DB read, and the card shows "responding to 20.1°C" honestly without touching the fan. **(c) Manual control:** a new `routers/fan.py` with `PUT /api/v1/fan/auto` (the preference) and `POST /api/v1/fan/command` (`{power?, speed?}`, drives the Dreo cloud off the request thread via `asyncio.to_thread`). **A manual command takes control by turning the autopilot off — but only after the command succeeds:** the order is drive-then-disable, so a transient cloud failure returns 502 with the autopilot **left intact** (driving-then-failing must never silently strand the room with auto off and the fan unchanged). 400 if neither power nor speed is given. **Frontend:** the `/bedroom` detail page gains a fan card — an Auto `Toggle` (the preference) plus manual `Off / Low / Medium / High` presets (speeds 3/5/7, mirroring the overnight ladder) — and the evening/post-ride Home `BedroomSummaryCard` shows a read-only fan status line (`fanStatusText`) so the state + the temp it is responding to are visible where Mark actually is at night, with the controls one tap away on the detail page (read-first Home, per Batch 24). Tests: +8 pure (`describe_fan_intent` matrix, `run_fan_control` auto-off gate) and +5 DB-backed (router auto-persist / command-drives-and-takes-control / 400 / 502-keeps-autopilot, daily-loop fan intent); ruff + strict mypy + full backend suite green (338 passed / 93 skipped locally — the 5 new DB-backed tests run in CI), shared + web green (41 vitest, lint 0 errors, build incl. tsc). **Not yet done:** live token-resume confirmation (#95), a real authenticated prod smoke of the two fan routes, and a physical end-to-end of `POST /command` against the real fan (deliberately not driven from a dev preview, which proxies to prod).

### 2026-06-28 — "Compared to the average for your age" home surface

98. **A second reference axis sits alongside the #44/#45 "vs your own baseline" read: each morning the home screen now shows where Mark sits against the *general population average for his age* — Garmin's own fitness age as the headline, plus VO₂max / resting HR / overnight HRV vs published age-band norms.** Mark asked for both the red/green "vs my normal" comparison *and* "how do I compare to the average for my age"; this ships the age axis. **Two sources, deliberately separated.** (a) **Fitness age** is Garmin's VO₂max-derived age-equivalent and is the most credible single "vs your age" number because Garmin computes it against its own population model — it is **already synced** inside `daily_metrics.raw_payload['max_metrics_vo2'][0].generic.fitnessAge` (the same payload #94's VO₂max read uses), so `_extract_fitness_age` pulls it with **no new column, no migration, no extra Garmin call** (chosen over a typed `fitness_age` column: YAGNI until we want fitness-age *trends* — revisit then). (b) **Population norms** for VO₂max, resting HR and overnight HRV are *not* available from Garmin's API as population means, so they are encoded as **static reference tables** (`services/age_norms.py`) by sex + decade band — coarse general-population ~50th-percentile guides (VO₂max ≈ ACSM/Cooper percentile norms; resting HR ≈ AHA-range mean ~70 bpm, roughly age-flat; HRV ≈ age-declining RMSSD per Nunan 2010), **privacy-safe** (no external call, no data leaves the app). **The comparison is pure + direction-aware:** `build_age_comparison(...)` classifies each metric against its age-band average into an outcome tier (`good`/`neutral`/`warn` + descriptor), with the gap signed so "better than average" is green **regardless of direction** — a resting HR *below* the average reads green (lower is better), the exact trap a naive red/green would hit. **Architecture mirrors `metricsVsBaselines` exactly:** computed once at analysis-generation time in `assemble_context_packet`, stored on `analysis.context_packet['ageComparison']`, re-served verbatim by `daily_loop._serialize_analysis` (so the GET stays a pure DB read), and rendered by a new `AgeComparisonCard` (fitness-age headline tile + per-metric tone-tinted tiles, reusing the `MetricsBaselineTable` tone/icon vocabulary) on the pre-ride + rest-day Home phases. The card is **framed honestly** — "general-population averages for your age — a rough guide, not medical advice" — because "the average 57-year-old" is a deliberately blunt, low bar (a fit man clears it easily; fitness age says the same thing more credibly). `sex` was added to the seeded KB profile (`male`), defaulting to male in code when absent so an unseeded/legacy profile still works. **Not Claude-gated:** the data is added to the context packet (Claude *may* reference it) but the verdict rules (`_morning_verdict`) are untouched — this is a deterministic UI surface, like the baselines table. Tests: +9 backend pure (`test_age_norms` — band selection, direction-aware tiers, fitness-age delta/tone, graceful degradation, camelCase shape) and +4 web (`AgeComparisonCard` + a DashboardPage integration assertion); ruff + strict mypy green, backend 347 passed / 93 skipped locally, web build (tsc+vite) + 18 affected vitest green. **Snapshot caveat (same as `metricsVsBaselines`):** the `ageComparison` block only appears on analyses generated *after* this deploys — today's already-generated analysis serves an empty block (the card shows its "shows up once … synced" fallback) until the next morning generation. **Refined before ship (2026-06-28):** Mark then asked to see everything on *one* table — last night's value, the diff vs his own baseline, and the diff vs his age-group average, on each row. The two reads are therefore **merged in the UI** into a single `MetricComparisonTable` (Home pre-ride + rest-day): a 4-column table (`Metric | Last night | vs your normal | vs your age`) with the fitness-age banner on top, joining `metricsVsBaselines` ⋈ `ageComparison` by metric (resting HR on an exact key, HRV bridged `hrv_7_day_avg_ms` ⟷ `hrv_overnight_ms`, VO₂max appended as an age-only row). Because the two frames cover different metrics — **only resting HR and HRV have both** a personal baseline and a population norm; sleep/SpO₂/respiration/body-battery are baseline-only, VO₂max is age-only — cells without a yardstick render `—` (chosen over hiding rows or a two-section card, so each metric stays one row). **Done as a frontend join, not a backend assembler:** both payloads already reach the client and `metricsVsBaselines` is independently needed by the `/baselines` detail route, so the merge is pure presentation — `age_norms.py` and `_metrics_vs_baselines` stay untouched and independently tested, and the backend is unchanged. `AgeComparisonCard` was removed; `/baselines` keeps `MetricsBaselineTable`. The personal-baseline ✔/⚠ status is no longer a separate column: *Last night* is the plain absolute anchor and the two comparison columns are **difference-forward**, each stating the verdict as a tone-tinted, direction-resolved difference (`in range` / `N above` / `N below` / `about average`) — so the comparison itself is what you read rather than a raw range or a bare tinted average. (The first draft tinted the age *average* value, hiding the judgment on mobile where the hover descriptor is invisible — a resting HR below average should read green without the user doing the mental flip.) 4 columns keep it mobile-safe after the #90 clip lesson. Tests: −4 (`AgeComparisonCard`) +6 (`MetricComparisonTable`); web lint 0 errors, build (tsc+vite) + **47 vitest** green; backend untouched. **Final placement (2026-06-28):** Mark then asked to drop the fitness-age banner and the standalone card title and have this *replace* the "Last night's sleep" card. So `MetricComparisonTable` became a **bare table** rendered *inside* that card: the card keeps its bed-icon title, the sleep duration·quality headline, and the **/brief + /baselines detail links — the only Home entry point to those routes** — while its REM/Deep/SpO₂/coach-read stat grid is dropped (that detail lives on /brief; the table already carries score/SpO₂/RHR with comparisons). Fitness age is still computed + serialized but no longer surfaced in the UI.

### 2026-06-29 — Batch 29 — Today-card actions + push-on-plan-set delivery (shipped)

99. **The Home "Today" card becomes the single place Mark acts on his day: it shows whatever workout is next *regardless of type*, in one of two data-driven states, and — the structural change — workouts are delivered to Zwift *when the plan is set* (days ahead) rather than on morning approval, so the morning is review-only and every card action is a re-sync of an already-delivered event.** Designed with Craig on 2026-06-29; full spec in `docs/designs/today-card-actions.md`. **Two states off an existing signal:** `adjust_ir_for_verdict` (#30) already tags the IR `adjustment.changed` — `false` on Green (`as_planned`), `true` on Amber/Red — so the card needs no new flag. `changed == false` → **no-changes** (Edit / Swap day / Skip); `changed == true` → **changes** (Approve & upload / Ignore suggestions / Manual edit / Swap day / Skip) with `planAdjustments` shown inline as the thing being approved, not a passive banner. A non-bike session shows the same card with Edit/Swap/Skip but **no Zwift upload**. **Delivery decision (supersedes #31 lead-days=2 *and* #91 same-day-on-approval):** push each workout to Zwift as soon as it is in the plan. Because events then live in Zwift for days, the actions map to event mutations — plan-set/restructure → **create**; Edit / Approve → **replace** (with the manual or adjusted IR); Swap day → **move** both affected events; Skip → **delete**; Ignore → **no-op** (the original is already there, so "ignore" is a pure client-side dismiss). The intervals.icu rail today is only create+delete (Batch 12); Batch 29 adds **replace** + **move**, keyed idempotently to `planned_workout_id`+`version` so re-syncs never duplicate. **Four forks settled this session:** (a) **Swap = unified move-or-swap** — pick a target day; empty → move, occupied → swap (Mark was happy with either, one control does both); (b) **Ignore = pure dismiss**, no backend call; (c) **Skip = mark-only** — a `planned → skipped` transition on the already-free `planned_workouts.status String(50)` (**no migration**) plus the Zwift delete, no reshuffle "for now" (reshuffling stays the separate `/restructure` tool); (d) **Universal card** — change `useDailyPhase` so any planned workout (not just bike) leads the card, `rest_day` only when nothing is planned. **Policy reversal recorded here:** push-on-plan-set delivers the *as-planned* baseline **without per-workout human approval**, deliberately reversing #29/#30's "nothing delivered silently" for the baseline — approval now gates **only the morning adjustment**. **Invariants preserved:** Red-never-VO2 (`blocks_red_vo2`, #30) still gates Approve; every mutation is audited as an `analyses` row (Batch 13 pattern); a failed Zwift re-sync must leave local state honest (#97 drive-then-disable). **Implementation status:** shipped in PR #44 (`8b5a71e`) on 2026-06-29 using true intervals.icu update-in-place for replace/move, exposed through the Today-card action routes and the daily-loop delivery state. Tier 🔴 High (delivery-rail edge cases + the delivery-policy change).

### 2026-06-30 — Batch 30 — Home day controls + rearrangeable week plan (shipped)

100. **Plan flexibility is implemented as direct, append/version actions over real `planned_workouts` rows — not fake rest rows, not a separate day-state table, and not implicit weekly restructuring — with delivery state keyed to the workout before falling back to date-only legacy rows.** Designed from the 2026-06-29 live-plan inspection and implemented on `feat/batch-30-home-day-controls`; full spec in `docs/designs/home-day-controls-week-plan.md`. **Day state remains derived, not stored:** rest is the absence of active workouts; cycle / weights / flexibility are inferred from workout types (`mobility` maps to flexibility); mixed days are any date with multiple categories. This matches the persisted model (workout rows, not day enums), lets the UI support the simple visible states Craig asked for, and avoids a migration. **New action boundary:** `/api/v1/plan-actions/schedule` returns the grouped live schedule including rest days; `/days/{date}/workouts` appends an active workout, `/days/{target_date}/swap-in` moves an existing workout into that date, `/days/{date}/skip` skips every active workout on the day, and `/days/{date}/actual` records an unplanned `ManualEntry` for "I did something else." Bike additions get a simple default endurance IR and reconcile through the Batch 29 push-on-plan-set rail; weights/flexibility additions are local plan rows with no Zwift upload. **Home + Plan split:** Home shows the day label and practical day-level controls, but every same-day workout still renders through the Batch 29 Today card so delivery actions stay per-workout. The Plan page is the rearrangeable week view over the same API, replacing the hard-coded weekly shape with add/skip/move/rest-day swap-in controls. **Mixed-day safety:** delivery lookups in `workout_delivery`, `daily_loop`, and executable resync paths prefer `planned_workout_id`; date-only lookup remains only as a compatibility fallback for older rows. Reslotting no longer deactivates every active workout already on the target date, so moving one workout into a mixed day preserves the other workouts. *Why:* the live plan currently has one workout per workout day, but the database and daily-loop payload already support a list; using real workout rows keeps future mixed-day behavior honest, makes rest-day add and rest-day swap separate actions as requested, and avoids hiding plan mutations behind a broad weekly restructure. **Implementation status:** shipped in PR #45 (`263460f`) on 2026-06-30 after green CI and production smoke.

### 2026-06-30 — Batch 31 — Overnight temperature × fan × sleep chart

101. **The fan autopilot is made legible by *persisting what it did* (a new `fan_state_readings` time series) and *joining it for read* (a pure `GET /api/v1/bedroom/overnight`), with the fan decision logic, thresholds, and graceful degradation left exactly as Batch 27 shipped them — this batch only adds a write and a read.** Designed with Craig on 2026-06-30; full spec in `docs/designs/bedroom-overnight-chart.md`. **De-risk (31.0) settled two things against the canonical `~/garmin-spike/out/sleep.json`:** (a) the per-interval hypnogram **is** available — `sleep.raw_payload['sleepLevels']` is `[{startGMT,endGMT,activityLevel}]` (0=deep/1=light/2=rem/3=awake) and `parse_sleep_fields` stores the whole sleep dict as `raw_payload`, so it survives the sync → render it as a faint background band, not just a sleep-window box; (b) the Hive poll (seeded +2 min) and `run_fan_control` (seeded +4 min) are separate 15-min jobs at different offsets, so temp and fan never share a timestamp → a **nearest-time** read alignment (the chart unions both onto one numeric time axis and the temp line bridges fan-only times with `connectNulls`), not exact-timestamp. **Why a dedicated table, not `analyses` (the #71 default):** this is a genuine 15-min time series like `temperature_readings`/`activity_timeseries`, not a narrative/audit artifact; `analyses` is one row per `(type, subject_date)` and would force ~44 rows/day or a JSON blob, both worse to query/join. **Rejected** adding `fan_*` columns to `temperature_readings` — the two jobs fire at different offsets, so co-locating would falsely imply simultaneity; keep them separate and join by nearest-time at read. **Persistence shape:** `fan_state_readings` (migration `011`, mirrors `temperature_readings`) records, per within-window fire, `phase`/`auto_enabled`/`observed_temp_c`/`fan_on`/`fan_speed`/`action`/`reason`, unique on `(user_id, captured_at_utc)`. The key change to the loop is structural only: `_apply_fan_control` now **returns** a `FanControlResult` (so the cloud I/O stays outside the DB session as before) and `run_fan_control` reorders the pure `loop_phase` check *before* the `fan_auto_enabled` gate so it can record a tick on **every within-window fire, including the early-return branches** — `auto_off` (autopilot off, **no cloud read**, `fan_on=null`), `no_data` (no fresh temp), `unreachable` (cloud connect/command failed) — so a gap on the chart is *explained* ("autopilot off" vs "cloud unreachable" vs "off because cold") rather than blank; `idle` (daytime) still writes nothing. **Idempotency without changing job semantics:** the tick timestamp is floored to the 15-min slot (`fan_control.INTERVAL_MIN`, now the single source of the interval) and written via `INSERT … ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`, so a coalesced double-fire upserts to one row. **`action` is a superset of `FanDecision.action`:** it folds in the scheduler-resolved outcomes (`auto_off`/`unreachable`/`winddown`) and `winddown` is its own label so the morning shut-off reads distinctly from a cold-room off. **Secret-safe:** the persisted `reason` for failures is a fixed string (`"cloud unreachable"` / `"command failed"`), never the exception text, and no creds touch the table. **Read path:** new `routers/bedroom.py` `GET /api/v1/bedroom/overnight` is a **pure DB read** (never writes) that night-windows `[21:30 → 09:00]` profile-local (reusing the `fan_control` window constants so chart and autopilot can't disagree), joins `temperature_readings` + `fan_state_readings` + the night's `sleep` row (keyed by the wake morning, `night+1`), defaults to the last completed night, and returns a `nights[]` pager; all windowing/hypnogram/summary logic lives in a pure `services/bedroom_overnight.py`. **Kept off `/api/v1/daily-loop`** deliberately (Batch 24/28 ethos — lean daily-loop, heavy reads on detail routes); the Home one-line glance ("Last night: 19→21 °C, fan ran 3.5 h (peak speed 5)") fetches the same endpoint (shared query cache) only on the evening/post-ride phases and renders a server-computed `summary`. **Frontend:** a recharts `ComposedChart` `BedroomOvernightChart` (temp line on the left axis, fan-speed step area on the right, `ReferenceLine`s at 19.5/20.0 °C, the hypnogram/sleep window as faint `ReferenceArea`s, muted `ReferenceArea`s for `auto_off`/`unreachable` runs) below the existing `/bedroom` fan card, with a night pager and an empty state; concrete hex strokes from `theme/tokens` per the #90 recharts-CSS-var gotcha. **Non-goals:** no change to fan behaviour/thresholds; no back-fill (the fan series starts at the `011` deploy, so early nights show temp+sleep with an empty fan track — the empty state says so); not wiring the `early_waking_0400` experiment (this *produces* the series a later Batch-22 evaluation could consume). **Tests:** 14 backend pure (`test_bedroom_overnight` — windowing/default-night/bucketing/hypnogram/summary), 8 DB-backed `run_fan_control` branch+idempotency ticks (`test_scheduler`) + 3 endpoint join/default/400 (`test_bedroom`) (run in CI — no local Postgres), 7 web pure (`bedroomChart` merge/muted/glance) + 4 chart component + Home/detail render assertions; backend ruff + `ruff format --check` + mypy(75) green, full suite 362 passed/129 skipped locally, Alembic single head `011`; web build + lint(0 err) + 63 vitest, shared 7. **Deferred to post-deploy:** live visual confirmation against real prod data — `fan_state_readings` only exists after `011` ships and the dev-preview proxies `/api` to prod, so it cannot be exercised pre-deploy (verified instead by build + tsc + vitest mount tests, which catch a recharts runtime crash). Tier 🔴 High (new table + scheduler write-path refactor + dual-axis chart).

### 2026-07-01 — Plan out-of-sync fix + training-plan importer

102. **Mark's real hand-built training plan was never loaded into the app; the schedule he'd been shown since setup was the Batch 5 *generic* 2121 seed, anchored to the setup week — so the app was ~10 weeks behind reality. Fixed by (a) correcting the current week's rows directly and (b) adding a reviewed-JSON → DB importer and loading his "Plan No. 2" as the real owned plan.** Reported 2026-07-01 from Mark: "today should be Week 13 Consolidation Wednesday" while the app showed something else. **Diagnosis (prod, read-only):** the plan is DB state — `plan_blocks` (13-week 2121, absolute `start_date`/`end_date`, `block_type`) + `planned_workouts` (each pinned to an absolute `workout_date`), and `daily_loop._planned_workouts` selects "today" by a pure `workout_date == local_today AND is_active` match (no relative offset). Mark's active blocks were `batch_5_seed` with **Week 01 Build = Mon 2026-06-15** (the app-generated `next_cycle_start(date.today())` at first-run), so **today (Wed 1 Jul) resolved to Week 03 Recovery** while his real progression had him in **Week 13 Consolidation** — a **70-day / exactly-10-week anchor drift** (his real Week 1 ≈ Mon 6 Apr). Three compounding mismatches, not just the date: (1) wrong week (anchor drift); (2) wrong weekly *shape* — the seed rides Tue/Thu/Sat with strength Mon+Sun and **no Wednesday**, whereas Mark rests Mon/Fri and rides **Tue/Wed/Thu/Sat/Sun**, so the seed's own Week-13 Wednesday was empty; (3) wrong *content* — generic placeholder sessions, not his authored prescriptions. Root cause: **nothing imports a real plan — the Batch 5 seed is a placeholder that was never replaced** (it only fires for a user with no retained state, so it won't re-clobber now). **Fixes applied to prod data (each dry-run-previewed, then applied; a full snapshot of Mark's plan rows was written before the destructive replace):** (1) **today (1 Jul)** — collapsed three duplicate `plan_action_add` "Endurance ride" rows to a single correct Week-13 Wednesday **"Outdoor Zone 2"** (70 min, WU 10′ 50–60% / main 55′ 60–70% / CD 5′ 50–55%), duplicates deactivated (`is_active=false`, reversible), the added Flexibility left intact; (2) **rest of this week (Thu 2 / Sat 4 / Sun 5 Jul)** — set to his Plan No. 1 Week-13 sessions (Sweet Spot Touch 55′, Light Aerobic Spin 45′, final Outdoor Endurance Ride ~80′), Friday left as rest, stray hand-added rows deactivated; (3) **from Mon 6 Jul** — loaded his **"13 Wk 2121 Plan No. 2 – Scheduled Start 06.07.26"** as the owned plan (13 blocks + 78 workouts, 2026-07-06 → 2026-10-04), replacing the forward seed while leaving 1–5 Jul intact; and (4) **relabelled the three leftover seed blocks** (15 Jun–5 Jul) to his real Plan No. 1 weeks — **Week 11 Build / Week 12 Taper / Week 13 Consolidation** — so the current week reads "Week 13 Consolidation" rather than the seed's mislabelled "Week 03 Recovery" (block metadata only — `name`/`block_type`/`sequence_index`/`raw_plan`; ordering is by `start_date` so the reused sequence numbers are harmless). **Durable capability (this commit):** `services/plan_import.py` — a pure, unit-tested `build_plan_rows(plan, start_date)` (maps a reviewed plan dict → Monday-anchored `BlockRow`/`WorkoutRow`s; rejects a non-Monday start) plus `import_plan(session, user_id, plan, *, dry_run)` which **replaces the forward schedule from the plan's Monday start** (earlier, in-progress weeks untouched) and is **idempotent for its own prior import** (matched by `source` + the `PN2 ` block-name prefix); a thin `src/plan_import.py` runner mirroring the other backfills (`--dry-run`, Profile lookup by `--display-name`); and the reviewed `data/plans/plan_no2.json` as the committed source of truth. **Why reviewed-JSON → loader rather than parse-the-`.docx`-live:** the JSON is a committed, human-reviewed artifact that is deterministic and testable, decoupled from `textutil`/docx quirks, and reproducible (`python -m src.plan_import …`). **Modeling notes:** the two Peak-VO₂ weeks map to `block_type="build"` (load-equivalent, so the recovery-vs-build experiment grouping in #83 stays honest) with the descriptive label preserved in the block `name`; `source="plan_no2_import"`. **No schema change, no migration, no new cron** — data + a script only. **Follow-up (not done here):** the Batch 5 auto-seed still fires for a stateless user and silently anchors a fictional plan to the setup week — it should be replaced by an explicit "no plan yet" empty state or an onboarding import step so this can't recur. **Verification:** pure importer suite `test_plan_import.py` (6 tests: 13 Monday-anchored blocks, block-type structure, weekly shape / Friday-rest, field bounds, Monday-start guard, override re-anchor) green; ruff + `ruff format --check` + mypy clean on the new files; prod verified by read-back — blocks now `PN2 W01…W13` (6 Jul → 4 Oct), today shows the single Outdoor Zone 2, and the 5 Jul → 6 Jul seam is clean (Fri 10 Jul correctly blank).

103. **The Plan page should use one mobile-first tap-to-move gesture, not split move controls or drag-and-drop: every workout opens a reusable bottom-sheet day picker over a 14-day visible window, and the existing `swap` route remains the single mutation path.** Designed with Craig on 2026-07-01 and implemented on `feat/batch-32-plan-day-picker`. The prior `/delivery` UI had two fragmented relocation affordances: each workout rendered three forward-only `Move <date>` buttons, while rest days rendered a separate "swap a workout into this rest day" list. That made rescheduling asymmetric, hid backwards moves, and pushed a touch-heavy interaction onto Mark's phone flow. **Rejected:** drag-and-drop across the vertically scrolling day list; it is too fiddly on mobile for the primary user. **Chosen interaction:** one `Move` button per workout opens a reusable `MoveWorkoutSheet`, built on the existing bottom-sheet component, listing exactly the currently fetched plan window with weekday/date, current contents (`title(s)` or `Rest`), a Today marker, and the workout's current day disabled. The plan window widens from `days=7` to `days=14` so "push it into next week" works without a separate calendar. **No backend change:** both old controls already converged on the same move-or-swap behavior (`ExecutableCoachingService.swap_day` via the workout-delivery `swap` route), so the page now calls only `POST /api/v1/workout-delivery/planned-workouts/{id}/swap` with `targetDate` and lets the existing backend resolve empty-target move vs occupied-target swap (#97/#99). The page-local `swapIntoMutation` and the rest-day swap-in block are removed; the `/plan-actions/days/{date}/swap-in` route stays available for any future caller. **Why reusable:** Home's Today-card swap can adopt the same sheet later, so the interaction is now a shareable component rather than a page-only button trio. **Verification:** targeted vitest for `WeekAheadPage`, web lint, and production build (`tsc` + Vite) green. No schema change, no migration, frontend-only.

104. **The overnight bedroom read should reuse the existing 19.5 °C / 20.0 °C thermal thresholds to classify each night into a simple Green/Amber/Red room verdict, carried on the existing summary payload and shown as a badge on Home and `/bedroom`, with one named red cutoff (`RED_CRITICAL_MINUTES=60`) and no fan-loop change.** Designed with Craig on 2026-07-01 and implemented on `feat/batch-33-bedroom-verdict`. Batch 31 already surfaced the overnight chart, but reading the chart still took a moment; Mark wanted a one-glance answer to "did the room cost me sleep last night?" without adding a new route, table, or settings surface. **Chosen derivation:** `services/bedroom_overnight.py` now counts `warning_minutes` from readings `>= THRESHOLD_ON_C` (19.5 °C) and `critical_minutes` from readings `>= THRESHOLD_CRITICAL_C` (20.0 °C) using the same reading-count × poll-interval rollup as `fan_ran_minutes`, then runs a pure `room_verdict(warning_minutes, critical_minutes)` classifier: `green` when warning minutes are zero, `amber` when the room crossed the warning line but `critical_minutes < RED_CRITICAL_MINUTES`, and `red` at or above `RED_CRITICAL_MINUTES=60`. **Why a single constant:** the warning/critical temperature lines were already settled by Batch 9 / Batch 31, but the "how long at 20+ °C is genuinely disruptive?" call is product judgment rather than a derived physical threshold; keeping it as one named constant beside the existing thermal constants makes future tuning easy without burying magic numbers in logic. **API/UI shape:** the existing `GET /api/v1/bedroom/overnight` summary and `bedroomOvernightEnvelopeSchema` now carry `warningMinutes`, `criticalMinutes`, and `roomVerdict`; Home's overnight glance and the `/bedroom` chart header render a badge using the shared verdict colour mapping, but with room-appropriate labels (`Green` / `Amber` / `Red`) rather than the coaching copy ("Good to go", etc.). *Why:* the colour system should feel like the rest of the app, but the bedroom is not itself a training recommendation. **Explicit non-changes:** no migration, no new endpoint, no new cloud call, no new per-user setting, and no change to `fan_control.py` thresholds or scheduler behaviour — this batch only classifies data the chart already reads. **Verification:** backend pure tests cover the new boundary cases; the endpoint contract and Home/detail UI tests were updated; backend pytest/mypy/ruff on the touched path, frontend targeted vitest, lint, and production build all green.

### 2026-07-01 — Batch 34 — Bedroom temperature × sleep correlation

105. **Bedroom climate evidence should be treated as advisory driver-correlation input, not as an automatic fan-threshold tuner: the Batch 31 temperature/fan time series now feeds the existing Batch 17 driver-ranking engine and the Batch 22 `early_waking_0400` evaluator, while `fan_control.py` thresholds remain human-reviewed code.** Designed with Craig on 2026-07-01 and implemented on `feat/batch-34-bedroom-sleep-correlation`; full spec in `docs/designs/bedroom-temperature-sleep-correlation.md`. **Chosen data join:** bedroom drivers are derived on read from the existing `temperature_readings` + `fan_state_readings` night window, keyed by Garmin's wake-morning sleep date (`night + 1`) so they line up with `sleep.calendar_date`: `bedroom_warning_minutes` (minutes at/above 19.5 °C), `bedroom_critical_minutes` (minutes at/above 20.0 °C), `bedroom_fan_ran_minutes`, and `bedroom_peak_fan_speed`. Missing bedroom series degrade to `None`, not zero, so early live nights and pre-series history cannot create false cool-room or fan-off evidence. **Reuse over reinvention:** the four keys are added to `insights.DRIVER_KEYS` and to `EARLY_WAKING_DRIVERS`; both surfaces still use the existing `compute_drivers` / Pearson / sample-gate path, with no new statistics, table, endpoint, migration, cron, or cloud call. **Plain-language layer:** bedroom correlations also carry a deterministic grouped-mean sentence (for example, "Nights with 60+ min above 20C average 6 points lower sleep score") on the driver item / audit packet and, for experiment evaluation, as a rendered reason. *Why:* Mark should not have to interpret only `r=...`; the sentence explains the observed split while leaving the correlation as the ranking statistic. **Explicit non-changes:** this does not write to `fan_control.py` thresholds, the speed ladder, `Profile.fan_auto_enabled`, or any persisted setting. A future threshold retune can use this evidence, but must be a reviewed human decision. **Verification:** targeted backend tests cover sentence generation, bedroom rollup assembly, missing-bedroom `None` behavior, and early-waking wiring; ruff and mypy are clean on the touched backend files.

### 2026-07-02 — Batch 35 — Last night as the single morning hub

106. **The "Last night's sleep" card becomes the single morning hub: the baseline range folds into the Home comparison table (last night's number tinted by its in/out-of-band tone, the range shown as a muted sub-line) so the standalone `/baselines` page is retired, and the retrospective overnight-room read moves into the sleep card while tonight's live fan/bedroom controls stay in the evening card.** Designed with Craig on 2026-07-01 (`docs/designs/last-night-morning-hub.md`) and implemented on `feat/batch-35-last-night-hub`; frontend-only, no backend change and no migration (the baseline quartiles and the bedroom-overnight summary were already on their payloads). **Table change:** `MetricComparisonTable` drops the separate "vs your normal" column and instead tints last night's value using the existing `baselineDiff` tone — direction-aware, so an out-of-band value in the *good* direction stays green rather than flipping amber — with `formatBaseline`'s `lower–upper` string as a muted sub-line under it; the "vs your age" ✔/⚠ icon+text and the range text remain, so colour is an enhancement, not the only signal (preserving the Batch 28 accessibility stance). Three columns keeps it readable on Mark's phone; the rejected alternative (keep the column and add a fourth Baseline column) was too wide. **`/baselines` retired:** `pages/BaselinesPage.tsx`, its `App.tsx` route + lazy import, and the now-dead `components/MetricsBaselineTable.tsx` are deleted; the `MetricBaselineRow` type and `formatBaseline` move into `MetricComparisonTable.tsx`, its sole remaining consumer. This **partially reverses Batch 28's deliberate "keep the `/baselines` detail link" (#98):** the range is now inline, so the detail page no longer earns its place; the only Home entry point kept is the "Full morning brief" (`/brief`) link. **Room read moved:** the self-contained `OvernightGlance` (Batch 33 room-verdict badge + the "19→21 °C, fan ran 3.5 h" glance, fetched via `useBedroomOvernight`) renders inside `SleepSnapshotCard` under the table instead of as a Home sibling, so last night's sleep and the room it happened in read together. **Judgment call settled (the one item `/batch-start` was to decide with Craig):** the outdoor "Overnight low" weather stat stays in the evening `BedroomSummaryCard` rather than moving to the sleep card — the glance already carries the *indoor* overnight range, and the outdoor low pairs naturally with Wind as forward-weather context; moving it would thread thermal props into the sleep card for marginal gain. *Why:* Craig asked to (1) fold baseline values into the sleep table and colour the number so the separate page isn't needed, and (2) make last night's room part of last night's sleep — both collapse Home toward one richer morning card. **Verification:** `MetricComparisonTable.test.tsx` asserts the 3-column layout, the tinted number (success in-band / warning out-of-band / neutral with no baseline) and the range sub-line; `DashboardPage.test.tsx` asserts the glance renders inside the sleep card and the `/baselines` link is gone; the `BaselinesPage` case is removed from `DailyDetailPages.test.tsx` and `MetricsBaselineTable.test.tsx` deleted. Full web vitest 60 passed / 17 files, lint 0 errors, build (`tsc` + Vite) clean; backend untouched. Tier 🟢 Mid.

### 2026-07-02 — Batch 36 — Unified Today card

107. **Home's "today's workout" collapses from a summary card plus N separate per-session cards into one "Today" card — one verdict badge on the day header, session rows in the body each keeping their own scoped controls, and a day-level footer.** Designed 2026-07-01 (`docs/designs/unified-today-card.md`) and implemented on `feat/batch-36-unified-today-card`; pure frontend recomposition, no backend/payload change, no migration. **What changed:** `DayPlanCard` (`apps/web/src/pages/DashboardPage.tsx`) is now a single `Card` — header `"{label} day"` + one verdict `Badge`; body renders each planned workout as a `WorkoutRow` (the former `TodayCard`, stripped of its own `Card`/title/badge) separated by a top border divider, or the rest-day empty state when there are no workouts; footer holds `AddWorkoutButtons`, "View week", "Skip whole day", and `ActualWorkoutForm` ("I did something else") — previously the summary card and the footer actions but without the per-session rows. **Scoping preserved:** each `WorkoutRow` keeps its own `panel`/`ignored`/duration-intensity `useState`, so two same-day sessions (e.g. a mixed cycle+weights day) expand and mutate independently — verified by a new mixed-day test that opens the second row's swap panel and asserts only that workout's id is sent to `/workout-delivery/planned-workouts/{id}/swap`. **Why drop the row-level badge, not the header one:** the day already owns one verdict; duplicating it per session was the exact problem the batch targets. **Verification:** `DashboardPage.test.tsx` updated (dropped the removed "Today's session" text assertions, added a verdict-shown-once assertion and the new mixed-day scoping test) — full web vitest 61 passed / 17 files, lint 0 errors, build (`tsc` + Vite) clean; backend untouched. Tier 🟢 Mid.

### 2026-07-02 — Batches 38/39 withdrawn; post-strength analysis added (Batch 43)

108. **The two in-app "guided session" batches (38 — strength interval player, 39 — flexibility follow-along video) are withdrawn, and a per-session post-strength analysis (new Batch 43) is added, after Mark clarified he tracks his strength and flexibility workouts on his watch and only wants the *post-workout analysis* in the app — not an in-app player to run the session.** Reported 2026-07-02 via Craig. **What Batches 38/39 were:** the non-cycling equivalent of Zwift playing a structured ride — an in-app interval *player* for strength (38) and an uploaded follow-along *video* for flexibility (39), each logging completion into a new `guided_sessions` table and reconciling it with the Garmin activity. **Why withdrawn:** Mark already runs both session types on his watch, which produces the Garmin activity we need; the app's job is to *read* that activity, not to guide the session. So the players, the `guided_sessions` table + migration, and the completion/reconciliation machinery are all unneeded. The design docs `docs/designs/strength-guided-player.md` and `docs/designs/flexibility-video-player.md` are kept but banner-marked **WITHDRAWN** (history, not deletion — so the idea and its reasoning survive and aren't re-proposed). **The gap this surfaced:** Mark asked for post-workout analysis for **both** strength and flexibility. Batch 40 (post-flexibility/mobility analysis) already gives flexibility its per-session read from the Garmin activity, but *nothing* gave strength a per-session analysis — strength had only the Batch 19 *rollup* watching-brief (#80), and Batch 38 (now gone) never added an analysis, only a player. **Chosen fix:** add **Batch 43 — Post-strength analysis**, a direct sibling of Batch 40: the same Batch 8 machinery (hourly poll → lean packet → thin Anthropic boundary → `analyses` `analysis_type='post_strength'` → daily-loop), keyed on the Garmin strength activity, with a lean HR/consistency packet (no power/FTP/time-series) and a strength-coach prompt. It reuses the existing `is_strength_activity` selector (#49/#80, `exclude_from_recovery`) and Batch 19's `compute_strength_rollup` for the consistency read, so it is even higher-reuse than Batch 40; recovery isolation (#49/#80) is preserved — strength stays advisory. Full spec: `docs/designs/post-strength-analysis.md`. **Impact review of the batches beyond 38/39 (the second half of Craig's ask):** none are broken. Batch 37 (Collapse-not-remove Home sections) sits *before* 38/39 and is frontend-only. Batches 40/41/42 (post-flexibility / walking / breathwork) each key on the **Garmin activity**, never on `guided_sessions` — Batch 40's spec explicitly said it "requires neither 38 nor 39"; the only trace was an *optional* guided-session enrichment in the Batch 40 packet, now removed since 39 will not ship. Batches 41/42 had no references at all. **Decision-number reconciliation:** the log is append-only with no gaps, so this replan takes the next real number **#108**; the still-planned reservations shift down by one to fill the slots 38/39 vacated — Batch 37 → **#109**, Batch 40 → **#110**, Batch 41 → **#111**, Batch 42 → **#112**, new Batch 43 → **#113**. (Batch 37's #109 is recorded immediately below, as it is already built; 40–43 stay "assigned at `/batch-start`".) The old reservations #109 (Batch 38) and #110 (Batch 39) are retired unused. **Build order:** Batch 43 shares the most machinery with Batch 40 and is naturally built alongside it; because Mark explicitly asked for the strength read, 43 may be prioritised with (or just after) 40 rather than left to the end. No code, no migration in this change — docs only (`DECISIONS.md`, `STATUS.md`, `docs/phase-batches.md`, the two withdrawn specs, the three 40–42 specs' number hints + the Batch 40 enrichment cleanup, and the new Batch 43 spec).

### 2026-07-02 — Batch 37 — Collapse-not-remove Home sections

109. **Home stops swapping whole section-sets by phase (the Batch 24 remove-model) and instead renders the full section set on every load, collapsing the sections that aren't primary for the current data state — so nothing Mark might want ever disappears from Home; it's one tap away. Data state stays the driver of *what's primary*; the clock only *nudges ordering*, never adding or hiding a section.** Designed with Craig on 2026-07-01 (`docs/designs/home-collapse-not-remove.md`) and implemented on `feat/batch-37-collapse-home-sections`; frontend-only, no `/api/v1/daily-loop` payload change, no backend change, no migration. **Supersedes the Batch 24 remove-model** (the "read-first Home" that #91/#97 assume, where `DashboardPage` rendered exactly one of three phase blocks and off-phase sections were *absent* — a ride made the sleep snapshot and day-plan vanish). Batch 24's single-primary *focus* and its data-state (not clock) driver are **kept**; only "absent" becomes "collapsed", plus a clock-driven *ordering* nudge. **What changed:** (1) a reusable `components/CollapsibleSection.tsx` — a `Card` whose header shows title + one-line summary + chevron and whose body is rendered **only while open**, so a data-heavy collapsed section (e.g. the sleep card's bedroom-overnight query) costs nothing; (2) a pure `lib/homeSections.ts` — `PRIMARY_BY_PHASE` (pre-ride→`today`, post-ride→`afterRide`, rest-day→`lastNight`), `orderedSections(phase, {hasRide, isEvening})`, and `isEveningNow()`; (3) `DashboardPage` now builds a `sections` record for the six-section superset (`lastNight` / `today` / `afterRide` / `tomorrow` / `tonight` / `bedroom`) and renders `orderedSections(...).map(...)` with `defaultOpen = key === primary`, replacing the three near-duplicate phase branches. The former phase cards became body components (`SleepSnapshotBody`, `DayPlanBody`, `PostRideBody`, `TomorrowBody`, `SleepPrepBody`, `BedroomBody`); the day label + verdict badge moved onto the Today section header (badge shown once, preserving #107). **Presence is data-gated, never phase-gated:** `afterRide`/`tomorrow` are the only sections that can be absent — and only because no ride has been analysed today (nothing to collapse), not because of the phase — so `lastNight` + `today` are always present and stay on Home post-ride (the exact object-permanence loss this batch pays back). **Lazy body ⇒ where the room read lives:** the collapsed Last-night summary is built from the daily-loop payload only (duration + qualifier + REM context); the `OvernightGlance`/room-verdict (a separate `useBedroomOvernight` query) sits inside the lazy sleep body, so pre-ride (Today primary, Last-night collapsed) the overnight query doesn't fire until Mark opens the card — honouring "a collapsed data-heavy section costs nothing" over surfacing the room verdict in the collapsed header. **Evening nudge = order only:** after 20:00 local (`EVENING_HOUR`), `tonight` + `bedroom` float up to just behind the primary; the nudge never changes which sections exist or which is expanded, so Home is correct whether Mark rides at 06:00 or 18:00. **Collapse state is derived per load, not sticky** (avoids a stale-open-panel feel; a session-remembered manual expand is a deferred non-goal). **Decision-number correction:** the ledger row + spec were pre-written as "#108", but the 2026-07-02 38/39-withdrawal replan (#108 above) consumed that number and explicitly renumbered Batch 37 → **#109**; this entry takes #109 and the `docs/phase-batches.md` row + `docs/designs/home-collapse-not-remove.md` header are reconciled to match. **Verification:** new `lib/homeSections.test.ts` (8 pure tests — per-state ordering, ride-gating, the evening float, primary-stays-first) and a rewritten `DashboardPage.test.tsx` around the section list (per state the right section is expanded and the rest render collapsed-but-present with their summary in the DOM; expanding a collapsed section mounts its lazy body incl. the overnight query; the evening nudge reorders via a faked `Date` without changing which sections exist; offline still renders; all Batch 29/36 workout-row interactions preserved). Full web vitest **71 passed / 18 files**, lint 0 errors, build (`tsc` + Vite) clean; backend untouched. Tier 🔴 High.

110. **Mobility/flexibility gets its own advisory post-session analysis path, keyed by activity name rather than Garmin's broad `other` bucket, so Mark's near-daily "Mobility Workout" sessions receive a lean coach read without old misclassified road rides leaking in.** Designed with Craig on 2026-07-02 (`docs/designs/post-flexibility-analysis.md`) and implemented on `feat/batch-40-post-flexibility-analysis`; backend + frontend, no migration. **Selector decision:** `is_flexibility_activity` matches `"mobility"` in `activity_name` and explicitly does **not** treat `activity_type == "other"` as enough, because the live census found that same bucket also contains 153 old road rides already handled by the ride selector. Yoga remains excluded for now. **Open calls settled at `/batch-start`:** analyse both the 16-minute and 3-minute mobility sessions (the prompt weights short sessions lightly instead of skipping them); keep a sibling `PostFlexibilityAnalysisService` rather than prematurely generalising Batch 8 before walking/strength land; expose a dedicated `postFlexibilityAnalyses` list on `/api/v1/daily-loop`; and backfill the full mobility routine history via a one-off runner. **What shipped on the branch:** `services/post_flexibility_analysis.py` mirrors the Batch 8 shape (pending selector -> lean packet -> thin Anthropic Messages boundary -> `analyses` row with `analysis_type='post_flexibility'` + `activity_id`) but the packet only carries duration, avg/max HR vs resting HR, consistency/streak, planned mobility session, activity-linked check-in, and guardrails. It deliberately omits power, FTP/zones, cadence, stamina, Performance Condition, Training Effect, and time-series. The hourly Garmin activity poll now runs the flexibility pass after rides; `flexibility_analysis_backfill.py` dry-runs by counting pending sessions and only generates with `--commit`. The daily loop serializes `postFlexibilityAnalyses`, shared schemas parse it, and Home renders an advisory markdown "Flexibility read" inside the Today section on mobility days. **Recovery isolation preserved:** mobility analysis never feeds the Green/Amber/Red verdict or ride recovery decision, and the output is advisory-only. **Verification:** new backend tests cover selector landmines, consistency rollup, lean packet/no power keys, fakeable generation/idempotency, and newer activity-linked check-in regeneration; daily-loop tests cover payload surfacing; Home tests cover the Today-section read. Full backend pytest 389 passed / 134 skipped; backend ruff + format-check clean; touched-source mypy clean; full web vitest 72 passed / 18 files, lint 0 errors (existing Fast Refresh warnings only), build clean; shared tests + typecheck clean. Full backend `mypy src` still hits the existing local `pydreo` missing-stub/import issue in `services/dreo_fan.py`, outside this batch. Tier 🔴 High.

111. **Walking is treated as advisory active-recovery context plus threshold-gated post-session analysis, not as a new recovery/verdict input: ambient walks feed only the deterministic walking brief, while deliberate walks (30 min OR 3 km) get a lean HR/pace `post_walk` analysis.** Implemented on `feat/batch-41-walking-integration`; backend + frontend, no migration. **Open calls settled at `/batch-start`:** keep the spec's OR threshold (`WALK_ANALYSIS_MIN_DURATION_SEC = 30*60`, `WALK_ANALYSIS_MIN_DISTANCE_M = 3000`) so a genuine longer easy walk is not missed just because one field is conservative; keep Home labelling informational ("Walking base") rather than relabelling rest days as active recovery; keep a sibling `PostWalkAnalysisService` instead of prematurely generalising the post-session engine before strength lands; use profile KB heart-rate zones when present, with a max-HR percentage fallback only for packet assembly; and provide a dry-run/commit full-history backfill runner (`python -m src.walk_analysis_backfill --since YYYY-MM-DD [--commit]`). **What the branch adds:** `services/walking_brief.py` mirrors Batch 19 with pure `compute_walking_rollup`, `WalkingBriefService`, `GET /api/v1/walking-brief`, and `walkingBrief` on `/api/v1/daily-loop`; `services/morning_analysis.py` adds `activeRecovery.deliberateWalkVolume` with `classificationImpact="none"` so Green/Amber/Red math is unchanged; `services/post_walk_analysis.py` mirrors Batch 40's idempotent analysis path but uses an HR/pace packet (`heartRateReview`, HR-zone distribution from `activity_timeseries.heart_rate_bpm`, pace/speed/drift, active-recovery volume, planned session, check-in) and explicitly omits power/FTP/cadence/stamina/Performance Condition/Training Effect. Elevation gain is surfaced as unavailable when not stored rather than inferred from another channel. The hourly Garmin activity poll runs walk generation after ride and flexibility passes; the daily loop serializes `postWalkAnalyses`; Home renders a compact walking-base panel and advisory "Walk read" markdown cards. **Recovery isolation preserved:** walking never feeds ride recovery decisions or deterministic verdict classification. **Verification:** targeted backend walking tests cover thresholds, rollup maths, active-recovery advisory context, HR/pace packet/no power keys, fakeable generation and idempotency (DB-backed generation skipped locally without Postgres); daily-loop serializer tests were included; web tests cover the Home panel/read; shared schema tests, web lint/build, backend ruff/format and targeted mypy are clean. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-02 — Batch 42 — Breathwork integration

112. **Breathwork becomes a deterministic habit brief plus an additive morning-verdict recovery lever, not a per-session analysis and not a new recovery input.** Implemented on `feat/batch-42-breathwork-integration`; backend + frontend, no migration. **Open calls settled at `/batch-start`:** trigger the lever on the existing low-recovery signal family — Red verdict, recovery-low Garmin readiness (excluding the existing `load_driven` interpretation), or unbalanced/low/poor/below-baseline HRV;
