keep the recommendation in the existing `planAdjustments` array rather than adding a new UI lane; ship the brief and lever together; and include a last-7-day session count from the brief when available. **What the branch adds:** `services/breathwork_brief.py` mirrors the Batch 19/41 brief pattern with pure `compute_breathwork_rollup`, `BreathworkBriefService`, `GET /api/v1/breathwork-brief`, and `breathworkBrief` on `/api/v1/daily-loop`; `services/morning_analysis.py` adds a compact `breathworkBrief` packet and a pure `should_recommend_breathwork(signal)` helper that appends one breathwork suggestion string to `planAdjustments`; shared schemas parse the new daily-loop field; Home renders a compact "Breathwork rhythm" line in the Today section. **Recovery isolation preserved:** breathwork never changes the deterministic Green/Amber/Red classification, never feeds ride recovery decisions, and never mutates recovery math — the verdict can recommend it, but it is not evidence for the verdict. **Rejected paths:** no per-session LLM analysis for a 3-minute drill, no HRV/stress correlation engine in this batch, and no new table/cron/cloud call. **Verification:** pure tests cover rollup maths, selector behavior, the lever predicate, Green/high-readiness non-trigger, and low-recovery advisory copy; DB-backed service/daily-loop tests cover synced breathwork rows where Postgres is available (skipped locally without `DATABASE_URL`); shared schema and Home tests cover the new field/panel; backend ruff/format, targeted mypy, shared typecheck/tests, web lint/test/build are clean. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-02 — Batch 43 — Post-strength analysis

113. **Strength sessions get a Batch-8-style per-session analysis reusing the existing selector and the Batch 19 rollup, kept strictly advisory — it complements, never replaces, the Batch 19 watching-brief and never feeds verdict/recovery.** Implemented on `claude/batch-start-43-h33k5y`; backend + frontend, no migration (`analyses.analysis_type` is already `String(50)`). **Origin:** the 2026-07-02 replan (DECISIONS #108) withdrew the in-app strength *player* (old Batch 38) because Mark tracks strength on his watch and wanted only the post-workout *analysis*; this batch delivers that, the direct counterpart to Batch 40 for strength. **Open calls settled at `/batch-start`:** reuse the existing `is_strength_activity` selector (Batch 19, delegating to the stored `exclude_from_recovery` flag, #49/#80) with no new classification code; reuse Batch 19's pure `compute_strength_rollup` for the consistency block rather than a bespoke function (higher reuse than Batch 40, which had to add both); keep a sibling `PostStrengthAnalysisService` mirroring Batch 40 rather than prematurely generalising the post-session engine; run the strength pass in the hourly Garmin poll after the ride + flexibility passes in its own try/except; and provide a dry-run/commit backfill runner (`python -m src.strength_analysis_backfill --since YYYY-MM-DD [--commit]`). **What the branch adds:** `services/post_strength_analysis.py` (`assemble_strength_packet` — duration, avg/max HR vs resting HR, the reused consistency rollup, planned session, activity-linked check-in — a strength-coach `SYSTEM_PROMPT`, the fakeable Anthropic boundary, and idempotent `generate_and_store` keyed on `activity_id` and regenerated on a newer check-in, storing `analyses.analysis_type='post_strength'` with `verdict='advisory'`); scheduler wiring; `_post_strength_analyses` + `postStrengthAnalyses` on `/api/v1/daily-loop`; `dailyLoopPostStrengthAnalysisSchema`; a Home "Strength read" card; and `strength_analysis_backfill.py`. **Recovery isolation preserved (#49/#80):** the packet omits power/FTP/cadence/stamina/Performance Condition/Training Effect/zones/time-series, the analysis never feeds the Green/Amber/Red verdict or ride-recovery decisions, and the wrist-HR note is carried in the packet. **Rejected paths:** no new selector, no new consistency maths, no new table/cron/cloud call, no change to the Batch 19 rollup brief. **Verification:** pure test that `is_strength_activity` selects strength / rejects rides; DB-backed tests (real local Postgres) for the lean packet (HR-vs-resting, reused consistency, no power/zone/time-series keys), idempotency, regenerate-on-newer-check-in, and daily-loop serialization of `postStrengthAnalyses`; shared schema test; Home "Strength read" web test. Backend pytest 547 passed, ruff + `ruff format --check` + mypy (87 files) clean; shared typecheck + 9 tests; web lint 0 errors, 74 vitest, and vite build clean. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-03 — Batch 44 — Interval-resolved ride analysis

114. **The post-ride analysis grades each *work* interval against its own %FTP target instead of judging a structured ride by its blended whole-ride average power or its name — the executed per-second trace is segmented on the planned IR's interval boundaries, and warm-up/recovery/cool-down power is described but never graded.** Designed with Craig on 2026-07-02 (`docs/designs/interval-resolved-ride-analysis.md`) from a bug Mark named in plain English — *"it's basing it on average power expecting the power for the full workout to be in sweet spot range… it needs to analyse the workout as a set, not base it all on its name."* Implemented on `feat/batch-44-interval-resolved-ride-analysis`; backend-focused + optional frontend interval table, **no migration** (intervals are derived at packet-assembly time and land in the existing `analyses.context_packet` JSONB). This is the **first batch that goes back *into* the cycling `post_workout` packet** to enrich it — Batches 40–43 forked *lean* packets away from it because those non-cycling types carry no power/time-series; cycling is the one type that does, and we had been flattening it to averages. It reuses the two things already shipped: Batch 12.1's `build_structured_workout_ir` (ordered steps with `durationSec` + `powerStartPct`/`EndPct` %FTP targets) and the DECISIONS #93 per-second `ActivityTimeSeries` — **no new Garmin call.** **Five open calls settled at `/batch-start` (all per the spec's recommendation except the fade signal):** (1) *interval source* = planned-IR alignment over the stored trace, not Garmin `get_activity_splits` — accurate for Mark's ERG Zwift rides, no migration, no extra sync; splits (which would also unlock free/outdoor rides) are the documented follow-up; (2) *free/outdoor rides* (no planned IR) fall back to the current whole-ride + zone-histogram read, no regression; (3) *fade signal* = **both** power-fade (the graded `fade` boolean, first-third vs last-third avg power drop) **and** a descriptive `hrDriftPct` decoupling signal from the same slice — the richer option, chosen because it costs nothing extra and gives the model grounding for "no fade / no surges"; (4) *rating* = qualitative, **no numeric score** (a coarse band was rejected as false precision that won't reproduce run-to-run); (5) *backfill* = recent structured rides only, via `python -m src.ride_analysis_backfill --since YYYY-MM-DD [--commit]`. **What the branch adds:** pure DB-free `services/ride_intervals.py` (`segment_ride_intervals`, `classify_roles`, `summarize_execution`, and a shared `power_zone` now reused by `_power_zone_distribution`) computing per-interval NP (30 s rolling, mean below the window) / %FTP / zone / adherence (`on`/`over`/`under` vs the target band with a ±5%-FTP tolerance) / fade / HR-drift, with the **role rule** — warm-up/cool-down from the IR `phase` or a leading/trailing ramp, a steady step at/below 60% FTP between efforts as a recovery valley, everything else work, and a promotion guard so an all-easy ride still grades something; `assemble_context_packet` now carries `plannedWorkoutIr`, `intervals`, and an `execution` summary, **keeping** `activity.avgPowerWatts` + `timeSeriesSummary` but relabelling them as context; the `SYSTEM_PROMPT` + `outputRules` grade on the work intervals and forbid treating the whole-ride average as under-performance; `PROMPT_VERSION` bumped to `post-workout-analysis-v2-2026-07-03`, and a new `_analysis_is_current` makes the hourly poll + backfill regenerate any analysis predating the live prompt version. **Optional 44.6 frontend:** the daily-loop serializer surfaces `intervals` + `execution`, a typed `rideIntervalSchema` parses them, and a compact "Interval execution" table under the post-ride card grades the work intervals only (renders nothing for a free/outdoor ride). **Invariants preserved:** the recovery decision and Green/Amber/Red are untouched (narrative + grading only, #49/#80); idempotent (one analysis per activity, regenerated only on a newer check-in or the prompt bump); the thin Anthropic boundary (#47) stays fakeable; a ride with no planned IR or no per-second trace degrades to the whole-ride read rather than erroring. **Rejected/deferred:** Garmin ground-truth splits, algorithmic interval *detection* for free rides, a concision/density pass (Mark's deflected "refined vs dense" question), and a VO2max trend surface — all tracked separately. **Verification:** 11 pure `test_ride_intervals` cases (warm-up→2×SS→cool-down grades only work; fade fires on a decaying block and not a steady one; over/under; NP mean-below-window vs rolling-above; no-plan/no-trace → `[]`; endurance single-step → work; all-easy → promoted; ramp-direction roles; execution summary with/without plan; zone thresholds) + a pure `_planned_ride_ir` selector/fallback test; DB-backed packet cases (structured ride grades the work interval / free ride falls back / prompt-bump marks a stale analysis for regeneration) run in CI and skip locally (no Postgres on this Mac); a shared schema test; two Home interval-table web tests. Backend ruff + `ruff format --check` + mypy (89 files) clean, full pytest **421 passed / 141 skipped**; shared 10 tests; web lint 0 errors, **76 vitest**, vite build clean. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-03 — Batch 45 — Proactive push + fan-reconciled nudges

115. **The app becomes push-first — the morning verdict and every post-workout read push the moment they are generated — and the evening thermal nudges defer to the Batch 27 fan autopilot instead of telling Mark to hand-cool a room the fan is managing. Reuse the existing notification boundary + idempotency; no migration, no coaching-logic change.** First batch of the 2026-07-03 passive-first plan; implemented on `feat/batch-45-proactive-push-fan-reconciled` (spec `docs/designs/proactive-push-fan-reconciled.md`). **Problem it closes:** the two highest-value outputs were generated **silently** — `run_morning_weather_sync` stored the Green/Amber/Red verdict and the hourly `run_garmin_activity_poll` stored each per-session read, but only the static 20:00 nudge + thermal/stale alerts ever pushed, so Mark had to *open the app* to find his verdict/read; and the pre-fan thermal nudges (`notification-rules:v1`) still told him to "pre-cool / seal it" while `run_fan_control` was already driving the room. **45.1/45.2 push (chosen: reuse `_send_once`, not a new service or cron):** `NudgeAlertService` gains `push_morning_verdict` and `push_workout_analysis`, each building a `NotificationPlan` and going through the **existing** `_send_once` → `send_notification` path (timezone/quiet-hours aware, records the send). Idempotency is the existing `analyses`-tag dedupe: the verdict tags `verdict-{subject_date}` (**one per profile per day** — the 09:30 backstop + any regeneration re-run never double-push) and each analysis tags `analysis-{activity_id}` (**one per activity** — a regeneration on a newer check-in or a `PROMPT_VERSION` bump is a *new* `Analysis` row but the same tag, so it never re-pushes). The verdict push title is `Today: {status}` with the verdict's first `reasons` line as the body (deep-links `/`); the post-workout push title is per kind (ride/strength/flexibility/walk, deep-links `/`). **Breathwork pushes nothing** — it has no per-session analysis (#112), enforced by `build_analysis_push_plan` returning `None` for an unregistered kind or an analysis with no `activity_id`. **New audit `analysis_type`s `verdict_push` / `analysis_push`** are written by `_send_once` exactly like the existing `evening_nudge` / `thermal_alert` audit rows and are **never surfaced** — `daily_loop` and the reviews/handover composers all filter `Analysis` by specific types, so the push rows stay invisible to the user (chosen over a new table: they are one-per-(type,tag,day) audit markers, the `analyses` audit is their natural home, #71). **Wiring + failure isolation:** the verdict push fires in `run_morning_weather_sync` after `analysis_result.generated`, wrapped so a push failure never blocks the Amber regeneration; the post-workout pushes fire via a `_push_new_analyses` helper after each `generate_for_pending_*` pass for **newly generated** analyses only, each wrapped so a failure never blocks the poll, with the audit rows landing in the poll's trailing commit (the verdict push self-commits since `generate_and_store` already committed). **45.3 fan reconciliation (chosen boundary — the one real judgment call):** `evaluate_thermal_alert` takes an optional `FanReconcileState` (`Profile.fan_auto_enabled` + the latest `fan_state_readings` tick's `action` + whether the fan is on at `MAX_SPEED`); `run_monitoring_alerts` loads it via `_fan_reconcile_state`. When the autopilot is **armed**, the manual pre-cool/seal/peak nudges are **suppressed** (the fan owns the overnight room) and a **single** "check the fan" push (severity critical, deep-links `/bedroom`) is escalated **only** when the room is warm (`temp_c >= ON_THRESHOLD_C` 19.5 °C) **and** the fan demonstrably cannot cope — latest action `unreachable`/`no_data`, or `temp_c >= 20.0` while the fan is at `MAX_SPEED`. **Judgment recorded:** the escalation is gated on the room actually being warm — a *comfortable* room stays silent even if the fan is unreachable, because there is nothing for Mark to physically act on ("notify only if he must act"); and because the fan writes no tick outside its overnight window (the evening pre-cool window is `idle`), an armed autopilot with a stale/absent latest action still **suppresses** the manual nudge (the fan is armed and will run at 21:30) rather than falling back to the old "you pre-cool it" copy. Autopilot **off** (`fan_auto_enabled == False`, Mark cooling by hand) keeps the pre-Batch-45 manual protocol nudges **unchanged**. **Quiet-hours honesty:** a push suppressed by `send_notification`'s quiet hours (or missing VAPID) still records its `_send_once` audit row and returns `True` the first time, so the next poll's dedupe sees it and does not retry. **Invariants preserved:** no migration; the `fan_control.py` decision logic/thresholds, the Green/Amber/Red verdict, and recovery isolation (#49/#80) are untouched — this only *notifies* about already-generated outputs and *re-scopes which nudges fire*; secret-safe (no creds on the push path, no new cloud call). **No frontend/shared change** — pushes ride the existing web-push path and deep-link via `data.url`; a per-category Settings toggle (verdict / analysis / bedroom) is a deferred nice-to-have. **Verification:** +11 pure tests (verdict/analysis push-plan builders incl. the breathwork/no-activity `None` guard; fan-reconciled suppress/escalate/comfortable-room/autopilot-off) + 2 scheduler push-wiring tests (verdict pushed once when generated; one push per pass across the four kinds) + 3 DB-backed tests (verdict once-per-day, analysis once-per-activity across regeneration incl. breathwork-none, `_fan_reconcile_state` reads the latest tick) that run in CI and skip locally (no Postgres). Backend ruff + `ruff format --check` clean, mypy 89 files clean, full pytest **431 passed / 144 skipped**. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-03 — Batch 46 — Evening sleep projection

116. **Tonight gets a deterministic, advisory sleep projection on the existing daily-loop surface, but the first Batch 46 implementation deliberately skips the optional evening push/audit row so the read can ship before adding another scheduler/idempotency path.** Shipped in PR #66 (`5bf9940`; spec `docs/designs/evening-sleep-projection.md`). **Boundary chosen:** a pure DB-free `services/sleep_projection.py` consumes already-synced facts — today's activities (local timing, duration, Training Load, aerobic/anaerobic Training Effect), Mark's measured sleep drivers from the existing Batch 17/34 `InsightsService.drivers()` seam, fresh bedroom temperature, overnight weather, the KB `sleep_protocol`, and `Profile.fan_auto_enabled` — and produces one of `routine` / `watch` / `protect` with a short qualitative summary, evidence lines, and 1-2 prep actions. It **never predicts a numeric sleep score** (same false-precision concern as #114), never changes Green/Amber/Red, never writes `analyses`, and never tunes `fan_control.py`; the output is read-only advice. **Fallback rule:** no synced training today, or fewer than the measured-driver sample gate, falls back to the plain protocol rather than making generic claims. **Fan reconciliation:** when the room/weather path needs action and auto is enabled, copy tells Mark to let Auto manage the pre-cool and only check Bedroom if it is still warm near seal time; when auto is off, copy uses the manual pre-cool/seal step. **Surface chosen:** `/api/v1/daily-loop` carries `sleepProjection` and Home's Tonight section renders it with actions plus evidence behind a details disclosure; the shared schema keeps the field optional so stale cached payloads render the previous static copy instead of breaking. **Deferred intentionally:** the optional Batch 45 push/audit row (`analysis_type='sleep_projection'`) and an "impact on tonight's sleep" line inside post-workout analyses remain future work; adding them now would broaden the batch into scheduler/audit semantics rather than closing the visible loop first. Verification: pure projection tests cover hard-late/warm, easy-early, rest fallback, insufficient-driver fallback; API/shared/Home tests cover payload and render; backend ruff/format/mypy, full API pytest, full web vitest/lint/build, and shared tests/typecheck are green; production smoke on the merge SHA passed Railway + Vercel same-origin health, web `/`, and auth-gated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` direct and via Vercel. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-03 — Batch 47 — Block-to-block progression

117. **The last completed training block can seed the next generated block, but only as an advisory draft input: it never changes FTP or plan rows by itself.** Implemented on `feat/batch-47-block-progression` (spec `docs/designs/block-to-block-progression.md`). **Boundary chosen:** a new deterministic `services/block_progression.py` core maps a `BlockOutcome` to a `NextBlockProposal` using only already-shipped signals — completed 13-week `plan_blocks`, planned workout duration/counts, `manual_entries` adherence, activity load/duration, Batch 44 `post_workout.context_packet.intervals` work-interval grades, Batch 17 `InsightsService.ftp_drift`, and morning verdict trend. No new statistics engine, no LLM, no migration, and no scheduler. **Generator integration:** `BlockGeneratorService.generate()` asks the progression service for a proposal only when the caller does not supply `ftpWatts`; the proposal's `recommendedFtpWatts` becomes the draft seed, and the full evidence is stored as `progressionProposal` inside the existing `knowledge_base section='generated_block'` draft payload. A manual FTP override still wins. **User control preserved:** `generate` still returns 409 when an unlocked draft exists, the `/builder` page still follows generate → refine → lock, and only `lock` writes `plan_blocks` / `planned_workouts` and triggers the Batch 29 push-on-plan-set delivery. The proposal is therefore inspectable evidence, not an auto-applied FTP bump or plan mutation. **Fallback rule:** before a full completed block or enough planned workouts exists, the proposal status is `fallback` and the generator uses the current profile/default FTP. **Surface chosen:** `/builder` shows the proposed FTP change, focus carry-forward, structural nudge, and evidence lines in the existing draft view, with the existing FTP input remaining the edit/override mechanism. Verification: pure tests cover over-target+rising → FTP bump, under-target+falling → cut/hold, insufficient-history fallback, and interval-grade aggregation; DB-backed generator seeding/never-clobber tests run where Postgres is available and skip locally without `DATABASE_URL`; backend ruff/format/mypy, focused pytest, shared tests/typecheck, web test/lint/build are green. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-03 — Batch 48 — Explicit daily/block loop model

118. **"The loop" becomes a first-class object: a pure `services/daily_loop_state.py` model + orchestration seam, mirrored by a generalised frontend `useDailyPhase`, that generalises the cycling-shaped phase to any modality and adds a real evening `wind_down` phase — but the shipped Batch 45–47 scheduler wiring is left untouched (scope chosen with Craig at `/batch-start`).** Implemented on `feat/batch-48-explicit-loop-model` (spec `docs/designs/explicit-loop-model.md`). **Scope decision (the one open call):** Batch 48 is explicitly optional/deferrable and 45–47 had shipped cleanly + prod-verified, so rather than the full "rewire 45–47 to consume the seam" reading of the ledger, Craig chose **"model + frontend, no rewire"** — build the model + seam and deliver the user-visible generalisation, but do **not** touch the prod-verified push/projection/block wiring (it can adopt `describe_loop_state` opportunistically later). This trades the literal "45–47 consume the seam" acceptance line for zero regression risk on shipped code, consistent with the spec's own deferral boundary. **What the model is:** `DayPhase = rest_day | pre_training | post_training | wind_down` with precedence *evening `wind_down` (sleep prep is the evening's focus, Batch 46) → `post_training` (any post-session read) → `rest_day` (nothing planned) → `pre_training`*; `post_ride` is generalised to `post_training` fired off the OR of ride/strength/flexibility/walk reads (fixing the symptom that a strength/walk-only day was stuck `pre_ride`); a first-class `wind_down` replaces the 20:00 clock-reorder hack. `BlockPhase = build | recovery | taper | consolidation | transition` is classified from the active block's `block_type`/name, and `consolidation` (wk13) is the explicit end-of-block boundary (`at_block_boundary`, the Batch 47 "plan your next block" trigger). `describe_loop_state(...)` is the pure orchestration seam ("where is Mark + what's next", `next_action` ∈ await_training/review_session/wind_down/rest). **How it's consumed (no rewire):** the daily-loop payload gains a read-only `loopState { dayPhase, blockPhase, nextAction, atBlockBoundary }` (`DailyLoopService` derives it from the snapshot's post-session counts + planned workouts + the profile-local clock + a new cheap `_active_block` query); the frontend `useDailyPhase` **prefers** the server data stage and falls back to local derivation for a stale/offline payload, applying the live-clock `wind_down` overlay itself so evening still updates without a refetch. `homeSections` replaces the phase→section map with a `hasRide`-aware `primarySection` (a non-ride `post_training` day leads with the Today card, where those reads render; `wind_down` leads with Tonight), and `DashboardPage` threads **one** `isEveningNow()` read through both the phase and the ordering so they never disagree. **Intended behaviour changes (the point of the batch, not regressions):** a non-ride post-session day now advances to `post_training`; the evening now leads with Tonight as a real `wind_down` phase (previously `lastNight`/`today` led with tonight/bedroom merely floated up). The per-section renders are unchanged (no visual regression in that sense); the pinned `homeSections`/evening tests were updated to document the new selection. **Boundaries kept:** behaviour-preserving beyond those two intended generalisations — **no** change to the verdict, fan, or analysis engines; **no** new coaching logic; **no** migration; `loopState` is optional in the shared schema so pre-48 cached payloads still parse. **Verification:** 34 pure `test_daily_loop_state.py` cases (phase precedence incl. evening-wins parametrized over post/planned; `is_evening` boundary; block classification from type/name incl. unknown→None; consolidation boundary; next-action map; `describe_loop_state` integration + camelCase `to_dict`); a non-flaky `loopState`-shape assertion + a new DB-backed block-boundary test (seeds a "Week 13 Consolidation" block → `blockPhase='consolidation'`, `atBlockBoundary=True`) in `test_daily_loop.py`; new `useDailyPhase.test.ts` (server-stage preference, wind_down overlay, per-modality local fallback) + rewritten `homeSections.test.ts`; a shared `loopState` parse test. Backend ruff + `ruff format --check` + mypy (**92 files**) clean, backend pytest for the touched files 34 pure + 34/7-skipped daily-loop (DB cases skip locally without Postgres); shared typecheck + 10 tests; web lint 0 errors (5 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), full vitest **89 passed / 19 files**, `tsc` clean, and the web build is clean under Node 20 (local Node 18 trips a pre-existing `vite-plugin-pwa`/`workbox-build` dynamic-require issue, reproduced with the batch stashed). Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-03 — Batch 49 — Navigation & IA refactor + Sleep hub

119. **The primary tab bar becomes Home / Week / Sleep (was Home / Plan / Trends) and "More" is re-tiered into For you / Coaching / Setup, with a new `/sleep` hub composed entirely from existing components — no new data, no backend change.** Implemented on `feat/batch-49-nav-sleep-hub` (spec `docs/designs/navigation-sleep-hub.md`), the first of the Home & navigation UX batches (49–51, see the "Also 2026-07-03" note above). **Why:** the shipped nav gave the sleep half of the daily loop no front door (`/brief` and the old `/bedroom` were reachable only via Home detail-links) while `Trends`, a browse-when-curious surface, held a primary slot; "More" also mixed Reviews (real block-loop output) in with raw dev-tool-ish labels (`Tests`, `Coach state`, `Plan builder`). **Decisions:** (1) demote Trends to More (kept one tap away under "For you") rather than a 4-tab bar — a phone bottom bar stays cramped past three tabs + More; (2) absorb the old `/bedroom` page into `/sleep` via a `<Navigate replace>` redirect rather than keeping two sleep destinations; (3) rename Plan→Week, Tests→Experiments, Plan builder→New training block, Coach state→Coach memory, and re-tier "Coach tools" into **Coaching** (New training block, Experiments) + **Setup** (Coach memory, Handover, Settings), while explicitly keeping "Handover" as Mark's own vocabulary. **Implementation:** `navConfig.ts`'s `PRIMARY_TABS`/`MORE_GROUPS` changed only in data — `TabBar`, `MoreMenu`, and `TopBar` already render off that config generically, so none of the three needed a structural change. The sleep/bedroom body pieces that used to be private functions inside `DashboardPage.tsx` — `SleepSnapshotBody`, `SleepPrepBody`, `BedroomBody`, `OvernightGlance`, plus `DetailLinkCard` and a new `OvernightChartCard` (the overnight-chart-plus-pager, moved out of the retired `BedroomPage.tsx`) — became standalone components under `apps/web/src/components/`, so the new `pages/SleepPage.tsx` (a `Last night | Tonight` segmented `Tabs`) and Home's `DashboardPage` render the identical pieces. `BedroomBody` grew a `variant: 'compact' | 'full'` prop — `compact` (Home's evening "Bedroom" section) keeps the read-only status line + a detail link into `/sleep`; `full` (the Sleep hub's Tonight view) carries the Auto toggle and manual Off/Low/Med/High controls that used to live only on the retired `/bedroom` page. `SleepSnapshotBody` grew a `showOvernightGlance` prop (default `true`) so the `/sleep` hub, which already renders the full `OvernightChartCard` with its own room-verdict badge, can suppress the compact glance rather than showing a link to the page it's already on (Home keeps the glance, since it's genuinely a link to elsewhere). `App.tsx` adds the `/sleep` route and turns `/bedroom` into a redirect; `BedroomPage.tsx` is deleted outright rather than left as a thin stub. **Boundaries kept:** no new endpoint, payload field, or migration — `/sleep` reads the same `/api/v1/daily-loop` + `/api/v1/bedroom/overnight` queries the Home sections already used; Home's own section set/ordering is untouched (that's Batch 50). **Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint 0 errors (the same 5 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings + 1 pre-existing `tailwind.config.ts` `require()` error, both outside this diff); full web vitest **92 passed / 21 files** (new `Nav.test.tsx` covering the primary bar, active-state, and the re-tiered/de-jargoned More groups on both `TabBar`/`MoreMenu` and desktop `TopBar`; new `SleepPage.test.tsx` covering both tabs, the fan-command mutation, and the `/bedroom → /sleep` redirect; `DailyDetailPages.test.tsx` split into `MorningBriefPage.test.tsx`, its Bedroom-specific cases removed since the page no longer exists); web build clean under Node 20; backend suite untouched (no backend files touched). **Live-verified** in a headless preview against a temporary mock `/api` (reverted before commit, per the in-repo UI-walkthrough method): the bottom bar shows Home/Week/Sleep, `/sleep`'s Last night tab renders the metrics table + overnight chart with a single room-verdict badge (no duplicate glance), the Tonight tab renders the projection + working Auto toggle/manual speed buttons, `/bedroom` redirects to `/sleep`, and the More sheet shows the exact For you / Coaching / Setup groups and labels specced above. Tier 🟢 Mid.

### 2026-07-03 — Batch 50 — Action-first Home

120. **Home becomes action-first: a deterministic, payload-only `nextAction` resolver drives one "Next" strip under the verdict hero and overrides the Batch 37/48 phase→primary selection, so the section holding the top pending action is the one expanded — regardless of time of day — and a collapsed section can signal it needs a tap. Frontend-only, no backend/payload change, no migration.** Implemented on `feat/batch-50-action-first-home` (spec `docs/designs/action-first-home.md`), the second of the Home & navigation UX batches (49–51). **Why:** since Batch 45 the app is push-first — the morning verdict and every post-workout read push the moment they land — so Mark arrives on Home to *act*; but Home was still time/data-phase-driven — the one expanded section came from `primarySection(phase)`, so an actionable item in a non-primary section (a pending coach adjustment `delivery.changed && isBike`, an unlogged ride check-in) sat collapsed and invisible; the only CTA was a lone "Check in" button; collapsed summaries were state-blind; and the verdict rendered twice (hero + Today header badge). **Decisions settled at `/batch-start` (per the spec's recommendations):** (1) **action overrides phase always**, not morning-only — an unactioned adjustment matters at 18:00 too, so rungs 1–3 fire regardless of the clock and only the protect-sleep rung is evening-gated; (2) the **priority ladder** = pending coach change (→ expand `today`) > ride analysed today with no post-ride check-in (→ expand `afterRide`) > no daily check-in (→ `/check-in`) > evening & `sleepProjection.tone==='protect'` (→ `/sleep`) > all-clear ("You're all set"); (3) **one primary action** in the strip (CDS restraint), with Check-in demoted from the prominent button to the strip's rung-3 CTA plus an always-available fallback link in the Today footer; (4) this **revises, not replaces, the Batch 37/48 phase→primary model** — the phase primary stays the fallback via `actionSection(nextAction) ?? primarySection(phase, {hasRide})`. **What it adds:** a pure `lib/homeActions.ts` (`nextAction(data, {isEvening})` → `{key, label, to?, sectionKey?, tone}` + `actionSection`), fully unit-testable and payload-only (no clock read of its own — `DashboardPage` threads the single `isEveningNow()` it already computes for the phase); `orderedSections` gains an optional `primary` override so the effective primary both **leads** the order and is the one `defaultOpen`, with the evening-float otherwise unchanged; `CollapsibleSection` gains a `tone` prop that renders a `bg-warning` "needs a tap" dot while collapsed and an `id` so the Next strip can scroll to a section-target action; `DashboardPage` renders the `NextActionStrip` (a labelled region; the all-clear state is a quiet button-less status line), makes `todaySummary`/`afterRideSummary` return `{text, tone}` (Today→warning on a pending change, After-your-ride→warning on an unlogged ride check-in), drops the duplicated Today verdict `Badge` (VerdictHero canonical), and makes Home's evening `tonight`/`bedroom` compact cards that deep-link into the Batch 49 Sleep hub (Bedroom's compact `DetailLinkCard` already shipped in Batch 49; Tonight gains one, added at the Home section level so the shared `SleepPrepBody` doesn't self-link on `/sleep`). **The `ignored` note:** the resolver keys the pending-change rung on the payload's `delivery.changed && isBike` only — the client-only Ignore dismiss (#99) isn't on the payload, and the underlying change is still pending until approved, so the Next strip honestly reflects the payload while the WorkoutRow's local Ignore stays a per-view dismiss. **Boundaries kept:** no new endpoint, payload field, or migration — every signal (`delivery.changed`, `postRideCheckIn`, `manualEntry`, `sleepProjection.tone`) already rides `/api/v1/daily-loop`; exactly one section stays expanded (need first, time second); no new push/notification logic (that is Batch 45 — this only *surfaces* the action on Home); the `/sleep` deep-link targets the hub, whose Last night | Tonight tabs are local state not URL-driven, so rung 4 links to `/sleep` rather than the Tonight tab directly (deferred). **Verification (local, all green):** new pure `homeActions.test.ts` (11 cases — each rung fires in order; the precedence chain; a changed non-bike session is not a pending change; a logged ride does not re-surface; protect-sleep only in the evening; the `actionSection` mapping); `homeSections.test.ts` +3 (the `primary` override leads over the phase primary, falls back without an override, and still respects the evening float); `DashboardPage.test.tsx` verdict-now-renders-once fix (two places) + 3 new (check-in strip by default; a pending change overrides the phase primary to expand Today while the collapsed After-your-ride shows the warning dot; the all-clear strip). `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint 0 errors (the same 5 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings); full web vitest **109 passed / 22 files**; web build clean under Node 20 (local Node 18 trips the pre-existing `vite-plugin-pwa`/`workbox` dynamic-require issue); backend + shared suites untouched (only `apps/web/src/**` changed). Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-03 — Batch 51 — Desktop two-column dashboard

121. **On `md+` viewports, Home's six sections split into an act lane (Today, After your ride, Tomorrow) and a context lane (Last night, Tonight, Bedroom) via a single CSS Grid, sharing the exact same component tree as mobile — no duplicate render, no new component.** Implemented on `feat/batch-51-desktop-dashboard` (spec `docs/designs/desktop-dashboard-layout.md`), the third and last of the Home & navigation UX batches (49–51). **Decision settled at `/batch-start`:** proceed with the batch as specced rather than drop it — Craig confirmed the layout-only polish was still worth building even though the primary user (Mark) is phone-only. **The act/context split** (the other open call in the spec) went: `today`/`afterRide`/`tomorrow` → act (do-something-now sections, and `tomorrow` rides along as the direct forward continuation of a ride's `afterRide` read rather than standing alone); `lastNight`/`tonight`/`bedroom` → context (read-first sleep/environment sections). **Implementation:** a new pure `sectionLane(key): 'act' | 'context'` in `lib/homeSections.ts`; `DashboardPage` wraps the existing `order.map(...)` in one `grid grid-cols-1 gap-5 md:grid-cols-2 md:items-start` container and passes each `CollapsibleSection` a `className` of `md:col-start-1` (act) or `md:col-start-2` (context) — `CollapsibleSection` gained a passthrough `className` prop on its outer `Card` for this. On `md+`, CSS Grid's default auto-placement algorithm walks the DOM in source order and drops each item into the first free row of its explicit column, so the act lane and context lane each stack in `orderedSections`' existing order with no extra logic — the section already leading (the Batch 50 action/phase primary) stays first in its own lane because it's already first in the flat `order` array. On mobile (`grid-cols-1`), the same single DOM tree collapses to exactly the previous single stacked column, byte-for-byte the pre-batch order — there is no separate mobile/desktop render path, so state (open/collapsed, in-progress edit panels) can never diverge across a resize. **No change** to `homeSections`' `orderedSections`/`primarySection`, `useDailyPhase`, `homeActions`, or any section body — purely a container/placement change. **Boundaries kept:** frontend-only, no backend/payload/migration change. **Verification:** new `sectionLane` pure tests (act vs context membership) in `homeSections.test.ts`; a new `DashboardPage.test.tsx` case asserting the exact `md:col-start-1`/`md:col-start-2` classes land on the right section cards and that every card still shares one `grid-cols-1` parent; `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint 0 errors (same 5 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings); full web vitest **112 passed / 22 files**; web build clean under Node 20; backend suite untouched (only `apps/web/src/**` changed). **Visually confirmed** in a headless preview: injected the same Tailwind classes the component emits into the running dev server's DOM and screenshotted at desktop (1280×800, confirmed two columns, act left/context right, each in source order) and mobile (375×812, confirmed single stacked column in the original order) — a lighter-weight check than the full mock-`/api` walkthrough used for Batches 49/50, appropriate here since this is a pure CSS Grid placement change with no data/auth surface to exercise. Tier 🟢 Mid.

### 2026-07-04 — Batch 52 — Design foundations (token + primitive tier)

122. **The shipped design system is lifted from "developer-dark" to "calm premium" at the token + primitive layer only: the dark surface/border ramp is re-spaced into a clear value ramp, inputs get their own raised control fill, and mono-uppercase is pulled back to eyebrows so form labels become sentence-case. Frontend-only, no per-screen layout change, no endpoint/payload/migration.** Implemented on `feat/batch-52-design-foundations` (spec `docs/designs/design-foundations.md`; overview `docs/designs/frontend-premium-review.md`), the first of the four 2026-07-03 front-end premium batches (52–55) — the load-bearing one 53–55 inherit. **The three design calls the spec deferred to `/batch-start`, now settled (with the actual values, chosen by contrast math not eyeballing — a throwaway CIELab/WCAG evaluator, not in the repo):** (1) **Dark surface value steps + elevation model.** The old dark tiers sat in one narrow near-black band (`bg #0A1112 → surface #111E1F → elevated #192A2B → overlay #213436`, each only ~+5 CIELab L\*), so cards didn't separate and Home read as a flat monotone wall (P0-1). Re-spaced to `bg #0A1314 → surface #152628 → elevated #1F383A → overlay #294648` — deliberate ~+8 L\* steps — keeping the deep teal-graphite hue that harmonises with the CheckMark icon tile; borders lifted to `#2E4C4E`/`border-strong #3D5F61` so they read against the surfaces (contrast ≥ 1.69). **Depth is carried by value first, shadow second:** the shadow tokens were *softened* (lower opacity, wider spread — `--shadow-md` 0.5→0.44, `--shadow-lg` grew and lightened), not strengthened — "calm premium," not glossy drop-shadows. The light palette already separated well, so it is left as-is **except** a real AA fix (below). (2) **Input control-fill + AA floor.** Inputs/selects/textareas used `bg-bg`/`bg-surface` (dark-on-dark) with a faint border and a `#7B859B` placeholder, so on Check-in the fields nearly vanished — a genuine accessibility miss for a 57-year-old daily user (P0-2). They now render on a dedicated **raised control fill** (`--control #223C3E` dark / `#FFFFFF` light) with a **stronger idle border** (`--control-border #436769` dark / `#CBD2D9` light), a clearer focus ring (`--shadow-glow` opacity 0.25→0.35, reused unchanged as the ring), and a lifted placeholder/label. **The AA floor is held in both palettes and verified:** dark `--text-muted` lifted `#7B859B → #98A2B4` so muted/placeholder clears WCAG AA (≥ 4.6:1) even on the lightest control fill, `--text-secondary` lifted `#94A3B8 → #A6B4C4` to stay above muted (ordering primary > secondary > muted preserved); **light `--text-muted` darkened `#8A93A1 → #6B7280` — the old value was actually *failing* AA at ~2.8–3.1:1 on the light surfaces**, an unflagged pre-existing bug this batch fixes. (3) **Mono-uppercase reservation.** `font-mono uppercase tracking-[0.25em]` was used for date eyebrows, "NEXT", More headings **and** form-field labels ("OVERALL (0–10)"), which read techy and hurt label legibility (P1-6). It is now **reserved for eyebrows/kickers/numerics/the wordmark**; the `Label` primitive became sentence-case at a legible `text-sm` (the eyebrows/kickers keep mono-uppercase — those are Batch 53/54's surface). A documented type scale (display/title/body/label/caption/eyebrow) was added as a comment block in `index.css`. **What changed, concretely:** `index.css` (both palettes) + `theme/tokens.ts` (the JS mirror — also synced its stale `shadow.glow` teal `20,184,166` → emerald `16,185,129` to match the CSS var actually used) + `tailwind.config.ts` (new `control`/`control-border` utilities); primitives `input.tsx` (new exported `controlFieldClassName` shared base), a new `textarea.tsx` primitive, `select.tsx` (trigger on the control fill; dropdown content → `elevated`, item-hover → `overlay` for a proper lighter-on-hover step), `label.tsx` (sentence-case); the two ad-hoc `textareaClassName` copies in `DashboardPage.tsx`/`CheckInPage.tsx` replaced by the shared `Textarea`; and the PWA/status-bar `theme-color` (index.html meta + pre-mount script, `ThemeContext.DARK_THEME_COLOR`, the manifest `theme_color`/`background_color` in `vite.config.ts`) synced `#0A1112 → #0A1314`. **`Card`/`Button` were deliberately left unedited** — they consume `bg-surface`/`border-border`/`border-border-strong`/`shadow-sm`, so the wider ramp, stronger borders, and softened shadow flow into them through the tokens with no class churn (that IS the "elevated fill + stronger border" the spec asked of them). **Boundaries kept:** token + primitive only — no per-screen layout or copy change (that is Batches 54/55), no brand-mark or verdict redesign (Batch 53), no new component library, and no backend/endpoint/payload/migration. **Verification:** new `components/ui/controls.test.tsx` (4 cases locking the control-fill on Input/Textarea, prop/min-height forwarding, and the sentence-case Label); the CheckIn textarea swap left `CheckInPage.test.tsx` green (queries by label/role, not tag). `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint 0 errors (6 Fast-Refresh warnings — the 5 pre-existing plus one for `input.tsx`'s new exported const, the same benign class as the existing `buttonVariants`/`badgeVariants` exports); full web vitest **118 passed / 23 files**; web build clean under Node 20; backend/shared suites untouched. **Live-verified** in a headless preview against a temporary prod-free mock `/api` (reverted before commit): Home, Check-in, and Sleep at mobile width in **dark and light** — dark surfaces now visibly separate (verdict hero, section cards, nested wells, table header), Check-in inputs are legible raised fields with readable placeholders, form labels render sentence-case, and the light palette's separation is intact with the darkened muted legible. **Drive-by test-hygiene fix (not a design change):** `DashboardPage.test.tsx` was flaky-by-clock — `isEveningNow()` reads `new Date().getHours() >= 20` and the daytime-layout tests never mocked the clock, so 11 of them failed whenever the suite ran after 20:00 local. **CI does not run the web vitest suite** (the `.github/workflows` web job is lint + typecheck + vite build only), so this never blocked CI — it only breaks the *local* `pnpm test` verification gate, which is why Batch 51 shipped green (its local run happened earlier in the day, not by any CI coverage). Still a real bug — a test that fails after 8pm is broken — so fixed: a `beforeEach` freezes the wall-clock to a deterministic daytime instant (`2026-06-20T09:00`, `toFake: ['Date']` so userEvent's real timers still work); the one evening test keeps its own `setSystemTime(21:30)` override. (A follow-up worth considering separately: add web vitest to CI so this class of regression is actually caught.) Tier 🔴 High.

123. **The CheckMark mark is now an in-product identity cue, with a restrained branded verdict hero and a single brass action-band role; this is presentation-only and leaves verdict/data/auth behavior untouched.** Implemented on `feat/batch-53-branded-verdict` (spec `docs/designs/branded-verdict-hero-login.md`), the second front-end premium batch. **Mark placement:** a reusable `Logomark` in `components/Brand.tsx` renders the generated `public/brand/checkmark-icon-primary.svg` asset (no hand-edited SVG); it appears in the login/activation splash via the shared splash brand, in the mobile and desktop top-bar lockups, and inside the verdict hero's branded ring. Sizes are intentionally defined at each surface: 96 px on the login splash, 30 px in the top bar, and 48 px inside an 80 px verdict ring. **Verdict boldness:** `VerdictHero` becomes the daily heartbeat without becoming glossy — Batch 52 surface/elevation, a quiet top highlight, a tonal ring, the existing Green/Amber/Red/pending `verdictCopy` and icon semantics, and a small verdict cue. The hero is more crafted, but it does not add new copy, new logic, or new backend state. **Gradient/accent scope:** the wordmark gradient is allowed on the brand lockup/splash; brass is reserved for the default Next action band and its CTA as the one secondary emphasis on Home, while warning states stay warning-coloured and all-clear stays a muted success status. The verdict ring uses semantic Green/Amber/Red plus Steele rather than brass so the accent does not compete with the action band. **Boundaries:** no rename/rebrand, no palette replacement, no endpoint/payload/migration, no daily-loop or verdict/recovery logic change, no auth-flow change. **Verification:** focused web vitest for `VerdictHero`, `LoginPage`, `Nav`/`TopBar`, and `DashboardPage` passed (36 tests); full web vitest 123 passed / 24 files; web typecheck clean; lint 0 errors / 6 known Fast-Refresh warnings; web build clean; local browser pass with a mock API confirmed login, mobile Home, and desktop Home with no horizontal overflow. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-04 — Batch 54 — Home hierarchy & calm density

124. **Home is recomposed into a curated brief — one lead/primary section stays prominent, every other section recedes under a quiet "More detail" grouping (collapse-not-remove kept); the session card's five-button cluster collapses to one primary + one secondary + a "More options" overflow; the greeting folds into a compact lockup; collapsed summaries truncate on a word boundary; and section expand gets a subtle, reduced-motion-aware animation. Presentation/interaction only — no payload/endpoint/migration change.** Implemented on `feat/batch-54-home-hierarchy-calm-density` (spec `docs/designs/home-hierarchy-calm-density.md`; overview `docs/designs/frontend-premium-review.md`), the third of the four front-end premium batches. **"More detail" grouping:** a new pure `splitPrimaryDetail(order, primary)` in `lib/homeSections.ts` splits the already-ordered section list into the one `lead` (the existing `primary`/action-override section — Batch 50) and the rest as `detail`, preserving the one-expanded model, the evening float, and the Batch 51 desktop lanes exactly (it is just "order minus lead", not a new ordering rule). `DashboardPage` renders the lead section at full prominence (unchanged `CollapsibleSection` styling, `defaultOpen`) followed by a quiet "More detail" label and the `detail` sections rendered with a new `variant="secondary"` on `CollapsibleSection` — a lighter `font-medium text-text-secondary` title and a borderless/transparent card — all still collapsed-but-present (Batch 37 kept) and still governed by the same tone/warning-dot logic. **Button overflow:** the session card's `WorkoutRowActions` (new) replaces the flat 5-button row (Approve, Ignore, Manual edit, Swap day, Skip) with one primary + one secondary always visible, and the rest in a "More options" `DropdownMenu` (reused, not new) — pending-change rows show Approve/Ignore visible with Manual edit/Swap/Skip in the overflow; non-pending bike rows show Edit/Swap visible with Skip in the overflow; non-bike rows show Swap/Skip visible with no overflow needed. **Compact greeting:** the full `PageHeader` h1 is replaced (on the loaded state only) with a small `text-sm` greeting + date lockup so `VerdictHero` sits higher on cold load. **Word-boundary truncation:** a new pure `truncateWords(text, maxLength)` in `lib/truncate.ts` (used centrally inside `CollapsibleSection` at 72 chars) cuts at the last space instead of a mid-word CSS ellipsis. **Expand animation:** `CollapsibleSection`'s body now mounts inside a `framer-motion` `motion.div` (fade + a small settle, not a measured `height:auto` tween — that path pulls in jsdom-unsafe `scrollTo` calls for no visible benefit here, since there is no matching close animation to choreograph) via the same `useReducedMotionConfig` hook already used by `score-input.tsx`, honouring `prefers-reduced-motion`. **Boundaries kept:** no change to the `nextAction` resolver or the one-expanded selection logic (Batch 50) beyond visual weighting; no payload/endpoint/migration change; no persistence of manual expand/collapse state. **Verification:** new `lib/truncate.test.ts` (4 cases), new `components/CollapsibleSection.test.tsx` (5 cases — default vs. secondary variant, word-boundary truncation, lazy body mount, the warning dot), `lib/homeSections.test.ts` gained 4 `splitPrimaryDetail` cases, and `DashboardPage.test.tsx` gained/updated cases for the overflow menu (Skip/Manual edit behind "More options"), the primary+secondary buttons staying directly visible, and the "More detail" divider/receded-card styling — the pre-existing verdict-once and offline-banner cases were unaffected. Full web vitest **137 passed / 28 files** (up from 123/24); `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint 0 errors (the same 6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings); web build clean under Node 20; backend/shared suites untouched (only `apps/web/src/**` changed). Tier 🟢 Mid.

### 2026-07-04 — Batch 55 — Screen polish & states

125. **The Batch 52 calm-premium system now covers Sleep, Check-in, and Week, and a shared on-brand `EmptyState`/`ErrorState`/`OfflineNotice` replaces the generic "please try again" cards app-wide. Presentation only — no data/endpoint/analysis-engine/migration change.** Implemented on `feat/batch-55-screen-polish-states` (spec `docs/designs/screen-polish-states.md`; overview `docs/designs/frontend-premium-review.md`), the last of the four 2026-07-03 front-end premium batches. **Three open calls settled at `/batch-start`:** (1) **The "vs your age" column folds into a per-row descriptor** (not kept as a column) — `MetricComparisonTable` drops the dedicated age column (mostly empty dashes for metrics with no age norm) and instead renders the age comparison as a small tinted sub-line under the "Last night" value (`"23 below for your age"`), only on rows that actually have one; rows with no age norm (e.g. sleep score) show nothing, removing the empty-dash clutter the spec called out. (2) **The shared empty/error/offline pattern is say-what-happened + a single recovery CTA** — a new `components/EmptyState.tsx` exports `ErrorState` (always carries a "Try again" retry action wired to the query's `refetch()`), `EmptyState` (the action is optional, since a true empty state has nothing to retry), and `OfflineNotice` (a quiet status row, not a card) — all sharing one dashed-border `Card` shell with an icon, title, and description, replacing the ad-hoc `Card`/`CardHeader`/`CardTitle` "couldn't load" blocks on Home, Sleep, Week, and (newly, since Check-in previously had no loading/error branch at all) Check-in. (3) **Check-in moves to a single unified save flow** — the previous per-card "Save check-in" (manual entry) and per-workout "Save session" (adherence) buttons are replaced by one "Save check-in" action at the foot of the page that fires the manual-entry `PUT` and then every planned workout's adherence `PUT` in sequence against the same existing endpoints, so there is one clear "am I done" moment instead of five buttons scattered down the page. **Also applied:** `SleepPrepBody`'s evidence `<details>` disclosure is lightened from a bordered `bg-bg` pill to a quiet muted-text toggle with a left rule on the expanded list (same content, no evidence/copy change); `WeekAheadPage`'s instructional intro `Card` is dropped to plain body text (reduced nesting) and its loading/error branches move to `Skeleton`/`ErrorState`. **Boundaries kept:** no metric, copy, endpoint, or analysis-engine change — the age comparison and evidence content are identical, only their presentation moved; no nav/IA change. **Verification:** new `components/EmptyState.test.tsx` (5 cases — error retry, custom retry label, empty with/without action, offline status region); `components/MetricComparisonTable.test.tsx` updated for the folded age column (5 cases, same coverage); new `CheckInPage.test.tsx` cases for the unified save (manual + per-workout adherence in one click) and the new error branch (loads without blocking manual entry); new `SleepPage.test.tsx`/`WeekAheadPage.test.tsx`/`DashboardPage.test.tsx` error-state cases; a handful of pre-existing `DashboardPage.test.tsx` age-comparison assertions were loosened from exact-text to substring matches to tolerate the new "for your age" suffix (no behavior change, just the folded copy). Full web vitest **147 passed / 27 files**; `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint 0 errors (the same 6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings); web build clean under Node 20; backend/shared suites untouched (only `apps/web/src/**` changed). **Live-verified** in a headless preview against a temporary local mock `/api` (reverted before commit, not part of this diff): logged in, then walked Home (Amber verdict, action band, session card), Check-in (legible raised inputs, single "Save check-in" firing both the manual-entry and adherence `PUT`s in one click, confirmed via the network log), Sleep (Last night's folded age descriptors rendering correctly with no empty-dash clutter; Tonight's lightened Evidence disclosure), and Week (plain-text intro, reduced nesting) — all in dark mode at desktop width, no console errors. Tier 🟢 Mid.

126. **A morning check-in that lands *after* the wake verdict re-runs the verdict and re-proposes the eased ride — but only while that ride is still `proposed`, and only when the verdict actually worsens to Amber/Red.** Built on `fix/pre-ship-thermal-and-morning-flow` (backend: `ExecutableCoachingService.regenerate_after_morning_checkin`, invoked from `PUT /manual-entry` for the profile-local *today*). **Why:** the wake verdict is computed from sleep/recovery *before* Mark checks in, and the intended morning flow (Sleep → check-in → ride) puts the check-in after the verdict/eased ride already exist — so although the framework *reads* the subjective score (`morning_analysis` folds `manualEntries` into the packet; a low score blocks Green), a check-in that lands late never reached today's session. Subjective is **downgrade-only** (a low score blocks Green; a high one never upgrades), so this can only ever *ease* the session, never harden it — which is what makes it safe to apply automatically. **Guardrails:** (1) it runs only while the eased ride is still `proposed` — an already approved/pushed proposal is never silently changed (Decision #29); (2) the packet status is recomputed **deterministically first** and the LLM re-runs *only* when the verdict genuinely worsens, so an ordinary check-in stays fast and free; (3) it is best-effort — wrapped so a save never breaks. Not a numbered batch — a pre-ship fix. Tier 🔴 High.

127. **In the morning (`pre_training`/`rest_day` phase, before evening), Home's `nextAction` ladder orders sleep → check-in → eased ride; the eased ride sits *below* the check-in even though approving it is what pushes the adjusted workout to Zwift.** Built on `fix/pre-ship-thermal-and-morning-flow` (frontend, `lib/homeActions.ts`). **Why (Craig's call, confirmed 2026-07-05):** Mark's real morning is read last night → log how he feels → *then* set the ride, so recovery is read before the ride is decided; outside the morning the ladder keeps the prior need-first order (pending coach change > unlogged ride check-in > check-in) because the ride's Zwift consequence is the top concern once he's up and about. **Completion signal:** there is no server "seen last night" flag, so a new per-day client flag (`lib/sleepReview.ts` — localStorage keyed by the daily-loop `subjectDate`, mirroring the client-only Ignore dismiss of #99) is set when Mark opens `/sleep`; the sleep rung completes off it and steps down to the check-in instead of nagging with no way to mark it done. The morning sleep rung only fires once overnight metrics have synced (`morningAnalysis != null`), so opening Sleep pre-sync doesn't pre-empt the prompt once metrics land the same day. Frontend-only — no payload/endpoint/migration change. Tier 🟢 Mid.

128. **A Hive device's self-reported `lastSeen` is never trusted when it is meaningfully in the future: `_hive_captured_at` clamps a far-future device timestamp back to observation (poll) time, and `is_hive_temperature_fresh` uses an *absolute* delta so a future-dated reading cannot read as fresh.** Built on `fix/pre-ship-thermal-and-morning-flow` (backend, `services/environment_sync.py` + `services/environment_freshness.py`). **Why:** a boiler module was observed reporting a `lastSeen` decades ahead (a "2068" reading); stored verbatim it then read as *perpetually fresh* and shadowed the real latest temperature, and the old one-sided freshness check (`now - captured <= LIMIT`) let a negative delta satisfy the bound. The clamp fires regardless of the `prefer_fallback_when_stale` flag — a future device clock is garbage in either direction. Do **not** "simplify" the abs-delta check or the future clamp away. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-05 — Batch 56 — Verdict calibration & personal baselines

129. **The sleep gate is softened only for Mark-specific, evidence-backed recovery: an age-adjusted sleep score in the soft band (60-73) can stay Green when HRV is clean, resting HR is inside his personal baseline band, readiness is not low/poor, and the subjective check-in is absent or >=5; the Red floor and Red-never-VO2 guarantee remain unchanged.** Shipped via PR #78 / squash `20437e8` with `PROMPT_VERSION="morning-analysis-v2-2026-07-05"`. **Why:** the 2026-07-05 prod diagnosis confirmed the data is mostly present — daily metrics/sleep/activities span 2025-06-24 → 2026-07-05, strength is classified, and the active plan exists — while recent verdicts showed Amber/Red days driven by sleep despite balanced HRV and no HRV-below-baseline flag. Generic sleep thresholds were therefore over-cautious for Mark. The shipped change also carries personal baseline bands into morning/review/trend packets, adds a compact `yesterdayLoad` morning input with linked post-session analyses, adds a structured `training_schedule` KB section (Mon/Fri rest days) that existing users receive through missing-section seeding, adds `readiness_score` to DB-history baselines, and tightens review readiness trends so a 4-point move like 80→76 is stable rather than "eroding." No migration, no endpoint change, no delivery-rule change; Batch 57 / Decision #130 has since shipped the broader data-truth wording and coverage/source-state safeguards. Tier 🔴 High.

130. **Review and trend narratives must treat coverage, sample counts, and source-state flags as binding evidence, not optional context.** Shipped via PR #79 / squash `4e0497a` (spec `docs/designs/coaching-calibration-and-data-truth.md`). Review packets now include an explicit `coverage` block for expected days, sleep/recovery/verdict/thermal coverage, activity count, planned rows, and adherence capture; sleep/recovery trends carry first-half → second-half means, deltas, and sample counts; adherence carries `sourceState='no_active_plan_rows'` when there are no active plan rows; and the strength packet carries `sourceState='no_tracked_strength_activity'` when the 12-week lookback has no tracked strength sessions. The Reviews API/shared schema and Reviews page expose those facts so the deterministic surface and generated prose agree. The review prompt/version (`reviews-v3-2026-07-05`) and trends prompt versions (`trends-*-v3-2026-07-05`) now require every trend claim to cite from→to numbers and sample counts, and forbid "stopped", "zero planned sessions", or poor-adherence claims when the packet says the source is absent/not tracked. **Why:** Mark's "strength stopped" / "zero planned sessions" / vague "eroding" feedback came from truthful empty inputs narrated as behaviour. The safer invariant is: missing source ⇒ say missing/not tracked; low sample count ⇒ say low coverage; trend word ⇒ cite the numbers. No migration, no new endpoint, and no speculative production backfill in this batch; the existing diagnosis SQL and resumable Garmin history backfill remain the operational path if coverage gaps are found. Production smoke verified Railway + Vercel same-origin health on the merge SHA, web `/` and `/reviews` 200, and unauthenticated review/trend read paths 401 direct and via Vercel. Tier 🔴 High.

131. **Batch 58's sleep-stage age comparison rides on the existing `ageComparison` payload as a sibling `sleepRows` group, and the stage comparisons use sleep-stage percentages rather than raw minutes.** Implemented on `feat/batch-58-sleep-stage-age-comparison` (spec `docs/designs/coaching-calibration-and-data-truth.md`). **Structure choice:** Home's compact Batch 55 `MetricComparisonTable` should stay the brief morning read, so the existing `ageComparison.rows` remains the general-fitness set (VO₂max / resting HR / HRV) while a new `sleepRows` array carries the deeper Sleep-page-only table. This avoids either bloating Home with six new rows or introducing a second endpoint for data already assembled in morning analysis. **Metric choice:** age norms for Deep/Light/REM/Awake are expressed as **stage mix** (percent of measured sleep) rather than raw minutes, because the question Mark asked is "how does the shape of my sleep compare for my age?" and percentage is the age-band-normalised frame that holds across different total durations. Duration is still compared as hours, and Restless stays a count when present. No verdict change, no prompt change, no migration, no new endpoint. Tier 🟢 Mid.

### 2026-07-05 — Batch 59 — Chronic-pattern suggestions

132. **Chronic sleep suggestions are deterministic daily-loop readouts, not generated prose or new persisted state.** Implemented on `feat/batch-59-chronic-pattern-suggestions` (spec `docs/designs/coaching-calibration-and-data-truth.md`). A new pure `services/chronic_patterns.py` core looks back 4 weeks, requires at least 21 observed sleep nights before calling a pattern, and emits explicit `insufficient_history` / `clear` / `active` states with an evidence window. It compares sleep-stage metrics against the Batch 58 age-norm frame (REM, Deep, Duration, Awake, Restless; **Light is not suggestion-driving** because it is too broad and usually just the remainder of other stages) and compares related markers against existing personal-baseline bands where those bands exist (sleep score, age-adjusted sleep, readiness, HRV, resting HR). Suggestions map repeated misses to concrete sleep-protocol actions and prioritise the first measured sleep driver from `InsightsService.drivers()` that matches the pattern (thermal, training-load, stress, or resting-HR levers). The payload rides `/api/v1/daily-loop` as optional `chronicSuggestions` because Home and `/sleep` already read that surface and no independent historical browsing workflow is needed; the router reuses the same driver report already required for `sleepProjection` so it does not duplicate correlation work. Frontend rendering lives in `ChronicSuggestionsCard` inside `SleepSnapshotBody`, so Home and Sleep share the same evidence-windowed advice. No migration, no new endpoint, no `analyses` row, no LLM call, and no Green/Amber/Red or delivery-rule change. Tier 🔴 High.

133. **The soft-sleep recovery override now judges readiness against Mark's *own* baseline median rather than a generic `readiness_score >= 70`; the Red floor, the categorical Garmin Low/Poor guard, the clean-HRV / resting-HR-in-band / subjective conditions, and Red-never-VO2 are all unchanged.** Built directly on #129 (`services/morning_analysis.py`: `_soft_sleep_recovery_override` gains a `readiness_center` argument computed from the `readiness_score` metric-baseline via `baseline_center`; it falls back to a mid-Moderate 60 when no personal readiness baseline exists; `PROMPT_VERSION` → `morning-analysis-v3-2026-07-05`). **Why:** the 2026-07-05 prod validation showed #129's flat `>= 70` gate rejected normal-for-Mark mornings — his readiness genuinely runs Moderate (trailing-84-night median 53.5, q3 65), so 2026-07-05 (readiness 66, resting HR 43, balanced HRV, soft sleep 72) stayed Amber even though every recovery signal was strong. A per-metric check confirmed Garmin's `readiness_level` maps cleanly to score (POOR ≤16, LOW 25–48, MODERATE 50–72, HIGH 76–86), so the low values are **genuine** Poor/Low days (no data cleaning needed) and the categorical guard reliably blocks them; the personal median floor only ever admits Moderate/High readiness at or above his own typical. Downgrade-only + the Red floor stay intact, so this can still only *ease* a soft-sleep Amber to Green, never harden. Prod prerequisite: the `metric_baselines` rebuild that added the `readiness_score` band (run 2026-07-05). No migration, no endpoint/payload-shape change. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-06 — Batch 60 — Completed-workout consolidation

134. **A ride is marked complete when its post-workout read is generated — the read then attaches to the session's own Today-card row and the workout can no longer be moved.** Implemented on `feat/batch-60-completed-workout-consolidation` from Mark's 2026-07-06 feedback (three snags: the approve/upload controls lingered after a ride was done and its read sat in a separate section; no check-in from the Sleep page; completed workouts were still movable). **Two calls settled at `/batch-start` (Craig):** (1) **persist completion** rather than derive it — a new nullable `analyses.planned_workout_id` (migration 012) links the read to the day's bike `planned_workouts` row, and `PostWorkoutAnalysisService.generate_and_store` flips that workout to `status='completed'` (the enum value existed but was previously never set) via the reusable `services/workout_completion.py` `complete_matched_planned_workout` (matches by local date + `cycle` category, skips a row already claimed by another activity's analysis so two same-day rides spread across the two planned rows, idempotent on re-run); (2) **compact + link** for the Home display — the completed row shows a ✓ Completed badge, the one-line tomorrow-impact, and the ride check-in, with the full coach read + interval table behind a "View analysis" disclosure, and the standalone "After your ride" section is kept **only for unplanned rides** (those with no matching planned row). **#3 (move-lock) rides the same signal:** `swap_day` now 409s when the source *or* target day holds a `status='completed'` workout (defence in depth), the Home row drops all its controls once done, and the Plan view hides Move + shows a "Done" badge — all keyed off the already-exposed `status` (no new plan-schedule field). **#2 (Sleep check-in):** a "Morning check-in" button at the foot of `/sleep` links to the existing `/check-in`, so Mark can log after reading last night without going Home. **Scope boundary:** completion is **ride-scoped** this batch (Craig's approved decision text) — strength/flexibility/walk sessions do not yet flip to completed, so a done non-bike session keeps its Swap/Skip/Move controls; the generic helper is ready for a fast-follow. Historical rides analysed before deploy are not back-filled (completion matters for today's Home + the forward plan window only); today's rides flip naturally on the next hourly poll. **Verification:** new backend DB tests (a ride marks the matched bike workout completed + links the analysis; an unplanned ride links nothing; `swap_day` 409s a completed session — these run in CI, skip locally without Postgres); a shared schema test for `plannedWorkoutId`; web tests for the completed Today row (Completed state, no ride controls, check-in present, "View analysis" discloses the read, no standalone section), the Plan move-lock (Done badge, no Move), the Sleep check-in link, and the `homeActions` matched-ride → Today target. Backend ruff/format/mypy (95 files) clean, full pytest **486 passed / 152 skipped**; shared **11** tests + typecheck; web **162** tests, `tsc` clean, lint 0 errors (6 known Fast-Refresh warnings), build clean under Node 20. No live headless walk-through this batch — the completed state needs a `status='completed'` row that prod won't have until the backend deploys and Mark completes a ride, so the deterministic vitest mount tests are the proof (mirroring the Batch 50 precedent). Tier 🔴 High.

**Follow-up in the same batch — the morning check-in is made optional (revises #127).** Craig's call after the completed-workout work: "review last night" and "morning check-in" collapse into one morning step, and the check-in stops being a blocking action. `nextAction` (`lib/homeActions.ts`) drops the `!manualEntry → 'Morning check-in'` rung from **both** the morning and the rest-of-day ladders and retires the `'check-in'` action key — so reviewing last night is the one required morning step, and once it's done a pending eased ride surfaces immediately (previously the eased ride sat *below* the check-in in the morning; that ordering was the point of #127, which this revises). The check-in stays **offered, not nagged**: the `/sleep` foot now frames it as an optional card ("Add today's check-in — optional… sharpens the coach's read and can ease today's ride", grounding it in the #126 subjective-score-eases-the-ride path), and the Today-card footer link is unchanged. The per-ride "how did it feel?" check-in on a completed/unplanned ride is untouched (that one is still surfaced). Frontend-only, no payload/endpoint change. Tests updated: the `homeActions` ladder is now sleep→ride with the check-in optional (a missing check-in never surfaces; protect-sleep and the eased ride move up a rung), and the DashboardPage morning strip clears to "all set" once sleep is reviewed with the footer check-in link still present. Post-follow-up gates: web **162** + tsc + lint clean; shared **11**; backend unchanged (**486 / 152**). (Numbering note: recorded under #134 rather than a new decision because the next free number, **#135**, is already earmarked by the in-flight age-adjusted-sleep-norms plan.)

### 2026-07-06 — Batch 61 — Age-adjusted sleep norms & real age-adjusted score

135. **Age-adjusted sleep is now a deterministic age-band recompute from stored Garmin sub-scores, and the Sleep-page age comparison shows healthy ranges rather than point targets.** Implemented on `feat/batch-61-age-adjusted-sleep-norms` and shipped via PR #84 / squash `7936fcb` (spec `docs/designs/age-adjusted-sleep-norms.md`) after Mark challenged the app's "typical" sleep-stage targets and the old age-adjusted score. **Score choice:** `services/sleep_scoring.py` replaces the flat Garmin `+4` with a pure credit model over Garmin's own `Sleep.factors_json` components (`remPercentage`, `deepPercentage`, `lightPercentage`, `awakeCount`) plus stored stage seconds and KB profile age/sex. A stage earns non-negative credit only when Garmin marked it down against its young-adult target but the user's age band accepts it; credit is capped, the score never drops below Garmin raw, and a night already good on Garmin's own bands reproduces Garmin raw. `garmin_sync` therefore stops writing `age_adjusted_score`; morning analysis recomputes it live, writes it back forward-only for history surfaces, and uses the pure helper for the verdict. DB-history baselines, reviews, and chronic-pattern suggestions call the same scorer when profile context exists and otherwise keep the stored column so older imported rows do not silently invent precision. **Reference choice:** `age_norms.py` keeps the general-fitness rows (VO2max/RHR/HRV) as average comparisons, but sleep-stage rows now use sex/decade healthy bands: for Mark's 50-59 band, REM 15-23%, Deep 12-20%, Light 48-62%, Awake 0-12%, Duration 6.5-8.0 h. Restless is Garmin-proprietary, so it is descriptive-only and never age-warns or drives chronic age-norm flags. Rows carry `bandLow`/`bandHigh` and nullable Garmin young-adult targets where Garmin exposes comparable stage-% targets (REM 21-31, Deep 16-33, Light 30-64), letting `/sleep` render "Healthy range (50-59)" plus a quiet Garmin-target contrast while Home stays compact. **Safety call from the real-night probe:** a read-only `railway run` over Mark's 375 scored sleep rows found 21 rows crossing the sleep `>=74` threshold under the new recompute, including 4 days with Garmin Poor readiness. The intended invariant is that genuine Poor-readiness days still gate, so `_morning_verdict` now treats `readiness_level='Poor'` as an unconditional cautious gate (Amber unless a stronger Red rule fires) and never as `load_driven`; Low readiness keeps the pre-existing load-driven escape when recovery/load evidence justifies it. The final probe showed those 4 Poor-readiness threshold-crossing days resolve Amber, not Green. **Boundaries:** no migration, no new endpoint, no historical backfill by default, Red floor and Red-never-VO2 unchanged, prompt version bumped to `morning-analysis-v4-2026-07-06`. **Closeout:** PR #84 CI passed in both push and PR contexts; production smoke verified Railway + Vercel same-origin health on `7936fcbb0cb7e48e7ff03f6eeadd81f81c2e3523`, web `/` and `/sleep` 200, and unauthenticated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` 401 direct and via Vercel.

### 2026-07-07 — Batch 62 — First-open latency: persist cache & thin daily-loop

136. **First-open latency is fixed at two layers — the client persists the daily-loop brief so a cold open paints instantly, and the server stops recomputing the 120-day driver correlation on every open — with no change to any decision output.** Implemented on `claude/next-batch-model-82pgjw` (spec `docs/designs/first-open-performance.md`). Measured first: warm production `/api/v1/health` is ~0.10 s, so the container is **not** cold-starting — the real causes are (1) an empty client cache on a fresh PWA launch and (2) `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` being the fattest endpoint. **62.1 — persist the client cache:** `App.tsx` swaps `QueryClientProvider` → `PersistQueryClientProvider` (`@tanstack/react-query-persist-client` + `query-sync-storage-persister`, all three `@tanstack` packages pinned to `5.101.2` to dedupe `query-core`), with `maxAge` 24 h, `buster` = build SHA (`__APP_BUSTER__` injected via a vite `define` from `VERCEL_GIT_COMMIT_SHA`), and `dehydrateOptions` that persist **only** a successful `daily-loop` query (a new `lib/queryClient.ts` centralises the client, persister, and a `clearPersistedCache()` called alongside every `queryClient.clear()` on login/activate/unlock/logout so one user's health data can't rehydrate into another session); `useDailyLoop` gains `staleTime` 60 s so a hydrated brief renders immediately and the refetch is background, not blocking. **62.2 — precompute drivers:** `run_morning_weather_sync` now calls a new `InsightsService.record_drivers` per profile (writes the deterministic 120-day report into the existing `analyses` `driver_correlation` audit row, idempotent per `subject_date`, **no migration**), and `_envelope` reads it back via `InsightsService.cached_drivers`, which reconstructs the report from the stored packet (`_drivers_report_from_packet`) and **falls back to a live compute** when the packet is absent (new user, failed sync, past `subjectDate`) — so the payload is identical, only *when* it is computed moves. **62.3 — thin the snapshot:** the four post-`{workout,flexibility,strength,walk}` analysis SELECTs collapse into one `analysis_type IN (...)` query partitioned in Python (`_post_activity_analyses`), preserving the exact per-type `(start_utc desc, generated_at_utc desc)` order. **Scope call (the one deviation from the spec):** the spec's second half of 62.3 — running the three activity briefs concurrently on separate `AsyncSessionLocal()` sessions — was **built then reverted**. A separate session reads from a different connection/transaction than the request, which breaks read-your-writes within the request transaction (the identical-payload snapshot test proved it: the parallelised briefs read empty because the seeded data lived in the request's uncommitted transaction). For a 1–2 user app the three small brief scans are a marginal win, so per the spec's own sanctioned staging ("the SELECT collapse lands first; the brief parallelization second") only the safe collapse ships; brief parallelization is deferred. **62.4 — connection warmth:** a new `run_connection_warmup` job runs `SELECT 1` every 10 min (well inside the 30-min `pool_recycle`) so a pooled connection is usually hot on first open; Railway↔Supabase region colocation is a config-only closeout check (can't verify from the sandbox). **62.5 — measurement:** the daily-loop GET handler now logs `snapshot_ms`/`envelope_ms`/`total_ms` so the before/after can be attributed from the logs. **Privacy trade-off (accepted):** the daily-loop payload (sleep/HRV/verdict) is now at rest in `localStorage` on the device — accepted for a private single-user PWA that already stores tokens there, bounded by `maxAge`, the daily-loop-only dehydrate filter, and the logout clear. **Boundaries:** verdict logic, morning analysis, sleep scoring (#135), soft-sleep override (#133), completed-workout/check-in (#134), and Red-never-VO2 are all untouched — this batch changes *when* and *how fast* data is computed and delivered, never *what* it says (the identical-payload DB test is the guard). No migration. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-07 — Batch 63 — Lighten the morning check-in (fast path)

### 2026-07-08 — Batch 64 — Rate & correct any summary (feedback primitive)
