137 (cont.). **The second half of #137 ships the feedback primitive: any AI summary can be rated in one tap and, when it's off, corrected in Mark's own words; the correction is persisted user-scoped and the most recent corrections feed the next read — "guide, not magic wand."** Implemented on `claude/batch-start-64-7fg0zg` (spec `docs/designs/summary-feedback.md`), completing the two-batch plan begun by Batch 63. **Why keyed to `analysis_id`:** every AI summary the app generates is already exactly one `analyses` row (verdict, post-`workout`/`walk`/`strength`/`flexibility`, `weekly`/`monthly`/`seasonal_trend`), so one primitive keyed to `analysis_id` covers the whole app with real referential integrity rather than a generic `target_type`. **64.1 — `feedback` table + migration `013`:** `id` uuid PK, `user_id`→`profiles` (CASCADE), `analysis_id`→`analyses` (CASCADE), `kind` (`summary`|`suggestion`), `rating` (short per-axis token), `correction_text` Text nullable, `created_utc`; **unique `(user_id, analysis_id)`** so the endpoint upserts (exactly one row per user per analysis) + index `(user_id, analysis_id)`. **64.2 — `PUT /api/v1/analyses/{analysis_id}/feedback`** (new `routers/feedback.py` + `services/feedback.py`) in the `{data, meta, errors}` envelope, **user-scoped**: the service raises **404** when the analysis doesn't exist and **403** when it exists but belongs to another profile, so ownership can't be spoofed; the rating axis is validated against the kind (422 on mismatch). `feedbackInputSchema`/`feedbackSchema` (+ `feedbackKind`/`feedbackRating`) added to `packages/shared`, and the daily-loop serializers + the `/reviews` `StoredReview` now carry each analysis's existing `feedback` (one batched `feedback_for_analyses` query on the snapshot) so the widget renders its current state. **64.3 — reusable `FeedbackControl`:** one-tap axis buttons — **accuracy** for summaries (spot on / a bit off / way off), **agreement** for suggested edits (agree / not for me / already doing) — and a negative tap reveals an optional "what did we get wrong?" textarea whose free-text is the real payload; mounted on the Home verdict (kind chosen per day: `suggestion` when the verdict carries a plan adjustment, else `summary`, since one row per analysis), the post-session read cards (ride/flexibility/strength/walk), and the `/reviews` written review. **64.4 — feed corrections forward:** the morning **and** post-workout context-packet assemblers now include the 5 most-recent free-text corrections for that user (`recentCorrections`), and both system prompts were extended to treat each as ground truth to weigh/acknowledge **but never** as an override of the Red floor, the #133 soft-sleep rule, the #135 Poor-readiness gate, or Red-never-VO2; `PROMPT_VERSION` bumped (`morning-analysis-v5-2026-07-08`, `post-workout-analysis-v3-2026-07-08`). **Boundaries kept:** no rating dashboard/aggregation (n=1 — the *correction* is the value, not the score); corrections **feed the next read**, they do not auto-regenerate; the `/sleep` client-side review has no control in v1 (it isn't an `analyses` row — sleep feedback piggybacks on the day's morning analysis, which carries the sleep read); no separate suggestion entity. **Verification:** migration `013` up→012→up verified against a local Postgres and the table matches the model; backend `test_feedback.py` (endpoint upsert/one-row, 404, 403, 422, recent-corrections newest-first-text-only, scoped `feedback_for_analyses`, morning-packet-includes-corrections) + full backend suite **665 passed**, ruff/format/mypy (98 files) clean, single alembic head `013`; shared typecheck + **12** tests; web `FeedbackControl.test.tsx` (5) + full web vitest **179 passed**, `tsc` clean, lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing warnings), build clean under Node 22. No production smoke run from this environment (deferred to `/closeout`). Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-07 — Batch 63 — Lighten the morning check-in (fast path)

137. **The `/check-in` default becomes a two-tap quick check-in — an "Overall" button-group plus a few one-tap chips — with every other field (BP, notes, supplements/food, per-workout adherence) moved behind a collapsed, reachable "More" disclosure.** Implemented on `claude/batch-start-63-9cdavo` (spec `docs/designs/summary-feedback.md`), the first of the two batches scoped from Mark's 2026-07-07 feedback-primitive ask; batch 64 (rate & correct any summary) is deferred to a separate build. **Why now, this way:** Mark named the real constraint — a quick check-in "will be significantly less than what I'm doing now" — so this batch is pure UX-budget cutting on the engine that already exists (`manualEntryInputSchema` + `PUT /api/v1/daily-loop/{date}/manual-entry`, which already fires `regenerate_after_morning_checkin` for today's date regardless of payload shape). **63.1 — quick surface:** `CheckInPage.tsx` replaces the free-typed "Overall (0-10)" field with five tap buttons (Rough=2, Meh=4, OK=6, Good=8, Great=10, `aria-pressed` on the active one) writing straight to `manual_entries.subjective_score`, plus three one-tap chips (Slept well / Low energy → `feel`; Niggle → `notes`) that toggle a short token on/off inside the existing free-text columns as a comma-joined list (`toggleToken`/`hasToken`) — no new columns, no new endpoint, no migration. **63.2 — regen preserved:** the manual-entry PUT path is untouched, so the quick save still fires `regenerate_after_morning_checkin` exactly as before (verified by reading, not changing, `daily_loop.py`). **63.3 — stays optional:** no Home change was needed — the existing "Morning check-in" link (Home Today footer, `/sleep` foot) already points at `/check-in`, which is now the quick form by default; `homeActions.ts`'s ladder (revised by #134) still has no blocking `!manualEntry` rung, and this batch does not reintroduce one. **63.4 — "More":** BP, the free-text "in a few words"/notes inputs, supplements/food, and per-workout adherence move inside a reused `CollapsibleSection` titled "More" (collapsed by default, no sticky state — same primitive Batch 37/50 use on Home), so the full detail stays one tap away but is never required; the single unified "Save check-in" action (Batch 55) is unchanged and still saves whatever is in state regardless of whether "More" was opened. **Verification:** `CheckInPage.test.tsx` rewritten — a quick save (tap "Good" + "Slept well" + Save) asserts the PUT body without ever opening "More" or typing; a chip-toggle test asserts the token lands in the right column (`notes` for Niggle, not `feel`) and clears on a second tap; the BP/adherence save paths are re-verified with "More" opened first; the error-state test confirms the quick tap surface stays usable when the daily loop fails to load. Full web gates green: `tsc --noEmit` clean, lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings, unrelated), full vitest **174 passed** (up from the prior 169; +5 net in this file), build clean under Node 20; shared package unchanged (**12** tests, typecheck clean). No backend or shared-schema file touched, so the backend suite carries no regression risk from this batch (not re-run in this environment — no venv available in the sandbox; nothing in `apps/api` or `packages/shared/src` changed). No migration, no new endpoint. Tier 🟢 Mid.

### 2026-07-08 — Batch 65 — Separate cycling & strength + correct Mon/Sat mapping

138. **Cycling and strength are now separate, independently-movable plan rows, and the right strength is on the right day (Dumbbells Monday, Bodyweight Saturday) — moving a ride never drags the strength with it.** Implemented on `feat/batch-65-separate-cycling-strength` from Mark's 2026-07-07 feedback (spec `docs/designs/workout-scheduling-feedback.md`), which surfaced two defects with one root cause: every build-week Saturday in `apps/api/data/plans/plan_no2.json` was a single `bike_endurance` row titled "Z2 + Neuromuscular + Dumbbells" (its `structured_workout.summary` literally ended "Then: 20min dumbbells"), so the day read and moved as one Cycle unit; and the Mon/Sat strength was mirror-imaged (Bodyweight Monday, Dumbbells Saturday). **Key pre-work finding:** multi-workout days already work end-to-end — the schedule service returns a list per day and `WeekAheadPage` renders one Move-able `WorkoutRow` per workout (keyed by `workout.id`) via the version-as-slot half of the `(user_id, workout_date, version)` unique constraint — so only the importer and swap-target detection assumed one workout per day. **65.1 — data:** the plan JSON is rewritten so every Monday (all 13 weeks) is the **Dumbbell** full-body circuit (`strength_maintenance`, ~22 min — biceps/shoulder-press/triceps/rows/flys/shoulder-matrix/pullover/core, from `Dumbbell & Bodyweight 19.06.26.docx`), and each **build-week** Saturday (9 weeks) splits into two same-`dow` entries — a `bike_endurance` "Z2 + Neuromuscular" (the welded "Then: 20min dumbbells" tail dropped) followed by a **Bodyweight** `strength_maintenance` session (squat/dead-bug/mountain-climber/glute-bridge/push-up). Recovery/consolidation/taper Saturdays (weeks 3, 9, 12, 13) keep their single "Easy Z2" row; a semantic old-vs-new diff confirmed every other cell is byte-identical (all bike prescriptions unchanged), so the plan row count goes 78 → 87. **65.2 — importer:** `import_plan` assigns **incrementing versions per date** (cycle = v1, strength = v2, in stable JSON order) instead of a flat `version=1`, so the two Saturday rows satisfy the unique constraint; `build_plan_rows` already emits one row per day entry, and a re-import lands on the same versions. **65.3 — swap engine:** `_active_workout_on` gains an optional `category` filter and `swap_day` computes the source's day-category (`category_for_workout_type`) and passes it, so swap-target detection is scoped to the same category — a moved ride swaps only with the target day's ride (never dragging a same-day strength/flexibility row), and swapping two ride days leaves both days' strength in place. The Batch 60 completed-session 409 guards are unchanged. This deliberately changes the prior cross-category behaviour where moving a ride onto a flexibility-only day dragged the flexibility back to the vacated day; the new behaviour is a move (the ride joins that day, the flexibility stays), which `test_plan_actions.py` now documents. **65.4 (closeout, not run at batch-start):** the prod re-import must run **forward from next Monday** (`python -m src.plan_import apps/api/data/plans/plan_no2.json --start-date <next-Monday>`) so Mark's already-hand-juggled current week is preserved, then `reconcile_deliveries` re-syncs Zwift for the new bike rows. **Boundaries:** **no migration** (version-as-slot reused, no `slot` column); no plan-editor UI; only the Mon/Sat strength mapping + the Saturday split changed — no bike prescription touched; the schedule API doesn't expose `structuredWorkout`, so the strength step shape is internal-only; the Green/Amber/Red rules, the #133 soft-sleep override, the #134 completion/check-in changes, the #135 Poor-readiness gate, and Red-never-VO2 are all untouched. **Verification (local):** backend pytest **504 passed / 165 skipped** (the added importer-versioning + two category-scoped multi-workout swap tests are DB-backed and skip without local Postgres, validated in CI), ruff check + format clean, mypy clean (98 files); shared typecheck + **12** tests; web vitest **180 passed / 30 files** (incl. the new split-day render guard), `tsc`/lint (0 errors, 6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings)/build clean under Node 20. Production smoke + the 65.4 re-import deferred to `/closeout`. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-08 — Batch 66 — Swap-first recovery guidance

139. **When readiness is low and a hard session is scheduled, the morning verdict now leads with a concrete one-tap week swap (move the hard session to a better day, pull an easier one forward) — Mark's own instinct — with softening kept only as the fallback.** Implemented on `feat/batch-66-swap-first-recovery` from Mark's 2026-07-07 feedback (spec `docs/designs/workout-scheduling-feedback.md`); the second of the two workout-scheduling batches (65 split the sessions so this one can move them independently). The engine to do this already existed and was simply unreachable — `_plan_adjustments` (`morning_analysis.py`) only ever recommended *softening* ("Cut duration 20-30%…" / "Substitute recovery…"), the opposite of Mark's preference. **66.1 — KB:** a new `coaching_protocol` knowledge-base section records the swap-first preference (`lowReadinessResponse.preference = "swap_first"`), auto-seeded for existing users via `ensure_seeded`'s missing-section path (no migration). **66.2 — verdict leads with the swap:** on an **Amber/Red** morning `assemble_context_packet` computes a read-only `SwapSuggestion` and, when one exists, prepends its concrete lead ("move it to Saturday and bring <easier session> forward…") to `verdict.planAdjustments` and attaches `verdict.swapSuggestion`; the softening line stays as the explicit fallback beneath it. `SYSTEM_PROMPT` gained a swap-first instruction and `PROMPT_VERSION` bumped to `morning-analysis-v6-2026-07-08` (morning generation does not mass-regenerate on a version bump — today's verdict picks it up on the next scheduled/check-in run, past days untouched). **66.3 — actionable:** the daily-loop `AnalysisOut` + shared `dailyLoopAnalysisSchema` carry an optional `swapSuggestion`; Home's Today card renders a `SwapSuggestionCard` whose one tap ("Move it to <weekday>") calls the **existing** category-scoped `swap_day` (`{workoutId, targetDate}`) — no new endpoint. **The swap-first engine is `weekly_restructure`, used read-only.** New pure `plan_swap_first(items, subject_date)` reuses the module's spacing primitives (`HARD_CATEGORIES`, `_conflicts`, `MIN_GAP_DAYS`): it finds the soonest *later* bike day carrying an easier (non-hard) session that the hard session can trade places with while keeping the ≥2-day VO2/Sweet-Spot no-stack rule, returning `None` (→ soften) when today has no hard session or no sound swap exists. It never brings another hard session forward and is immune to a split day's strength row (bike-only date map). **Deliberate scope call — the fuller "restructure preview → apply" surface (spec's preferred 66.3) was NOT wired.** `WeeklyRestructureService.apply_for_week` re-versions a whole *date* (`_version_workout` deactivates all active rows on the date and inserts one), which — after Batch 65's split Saturdays (bike + Bodyweight on one date) — would silently **drop the strength row** on any changed date. So the batch takes the spec's sanctioned fallback: read-only suggestion + the Batch 65-safe category-scoped `swap_day`. Batch 66 does not make `apply_for_week` newly reachable from any UI, so the latent data-loss stays contained; fixing `_version_workout` for multi-workout days is a prerequisite follow-up before restructure-apply gets a user surface (flagged). **Boundaries:** **no migration**; the Green/Amber/Red rules, the #133 soft-sleep override, the #134 completion/check-in changes, the #135 Poor-readiness gate, and Red-never-VO2 are all untouched — Batch 66 changes the *recommendation and its reachability*, not the gate; `adjust_ir_for_verdict` softening + `blocks_red_vo2` are unchanged, and a swapped VO2 satisfies no-stack by construction. **Verification (local):** backend pytest **511 passed / 167 skipped** (7 new pure `plan_swap_first` tests; 2 new DB-backed morning-analysis integration tests — swap leads + softening fallback, Green no-suggestion — skip without local Postgres, validated in CI), ruff check + format clean, mypy clean (98 files); shared typecheck + **13** tests (new swap-suggestion schema case); web `tsc` clean, lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), vitest **181 passed / 30 files** (new DashboardPage swap-card render + one-tap-swap test), build clean under Node 20. Batch-start render proof is the DashboardPage mount test (card renders + button fires the correct swap POST); the Vercel preview build is the visual/deploy proof at PR time. Production smoke deferred to `/closeout`. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-09 — Batch 67 — Real structured workouts + harden delivery parsing

140. **Every bike session in the plan is now a real multi-step structured workout (warm-up ramp → priming efforts → work intervals at an explicit % → recovery valleys → cool-down), transcribed faithfully from Mark's authoritative plan doc; the two silent delivery-parser holes are closed; and the app-displayed total traces the summed steps.** Implemented on `feat/batch-67-structured-workouts` from Mark's 2026-07-07/08 feedback (spec `docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md`), the trunk fix of the workout-fidelity thread. **Root cause:** every one of the 65 bike sessions in `apps/api/data/plans/plan_no2.json` was authored as a single collapsed step (`{label, target: <prose>, minutes: <total>}`), with the real structure living only in an unparsed human `summary` string. Running the real parser over it delivered the VO2 day as a **flat 55% / 154 W Z1 ride** (the `return 55` fallback on an unparseable `"VO₂ (see prescription)"`), the Z2 day at the **top of its band** (the en-dash defeated band-averaging → 72% not 68%), and every duration was a hand-typed total that had drifted (VO2 `60` vs the real ~47). **67.1 — grammar can now author ramps.** `_expand_step` (`workout_delivery.py`) gains a ramp raw-step form `{"label","minutes","ramp":[startPct,endPct]}` → a genuine ramp IR step (`powerStartPct != powerEndPct`, kind `ramp`); previously it could only emit **steady** steps, so even the app's own VO2 builder made a flat warm-up. **67.2 — no silent fallback + import gate.** `_power_pct` no longer `return 55`s on an unresolvable target — it raises 422 (the named-zone map, e.g. `"easy spin"→50`, is kept so existing callers resolve). New pure `expand_structured_steps` + `validate_deliverable_bike_workout` are called from `build_plan_rows`, so a bike workout that can't resolve, is single-block, or lacks a warm-up/cool-down/ramp — or whose `duration_min` doesn't trace the summed steps — **fails at import, before anything reaches Zwift.** **67.3 — en-dash bands → midpoint.** The band regex accepts the unicode dash family (U+2010–U+2015, U+2212) and collapses a band to its **midpoint**, so `"65–72%"` delivers **68%** and a 64.9% ride grades "on" (±5) instead of "under" vs 72. **67.2b — full transcription.** All 65 `bike_*` workouts (13 weeks × Tue VO2 / Wed Z2 / Thu Sweet-Spot / Sat ride / Sun Long-Z2) were re-authored from the source doc `Full 13 Wk. 2121 Plan No. 2 Start 06.07.26.docx` (the lossy JSON `summary` strings were **not** trusted) into multi-step `steps` arrays, with `duration_min` = the true summed steps. VO2 uses recovery-after-each-rep (matching the spec's ~47-min figure); the Saturday neuromuscular block is `6 × (12 s @185% + 2:48 @55%)`; endurance ranges are authored as en-dash bands so they resolve to their midpoint (**Long Z2 68%, easy/recovery Z2 62%**). **Decided (Mark, 2026-07-09):** day placement stays **Dumbbells Monday / Bodyweight Saturday as separate movable rows** (Batch 65 preserved — a semantic diff confirmed all 35 non-bike/rest rows are byte-identical and only the 65 bike days changed); FTP stays **280 W**; "no hard bike Mon & Fri" is deferred to Batch 70's rebalancer, not a placement change here. **Method:** the transcription ran through a throwaway generator (scratchpad, not committed) that mutates only bike days in place and validates each via the real engine; the committed artifact is the reviewed JSON, independently locked by a shape-guard test suite. **Boundaries:** **no migration** (data + parser only); the Green/Amber/Red rules, #133 soft-sleep, #135 Poor-readiness, and Red-never-VO2 are untouched; no per-interval workout-editor UI (the manual-override intensity dial remains the escape hatch); `build_structured_workout_ir` is unchanged for callers — it now delegates step expansion to `expand_structured_steps`. **Verification (local):** backend pytest **528 passed / 168 skipped** (new `test_plan_fidelity.py` shape guard — 65-bike count, total-time trace, no-flat-55, midpoint bands, VO2-as-120% intervals, import-gate accept/reject — plus 10 new grammar/parser/ZWO-snapshot cases in `test_workout_delivery.py`), ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean, mypy **98 files** clean; shared typecheck + **13** tests; web `tsc`/lint/vitest/build under Node 20 (untouched by this backend-only batch). **Closeout (67.4, not run at batch-start):** re-import **forward from the resume Monday** (`python -m src.plan_import apps/api/data/plans/plan_no2.json --start-date <resume-Monday>`) so the reset/off week isn't clobbered, then `reconcile_deliveries` re-pushes the corrected bike rows + a Zwift spot-check that the VO2 shows intervals with ramps, not a flat block. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-09 — Batch 68 — Grade what he actually rode

141. **Post-workout analysis now grades the delivered/accepted workout IR when one exists, rather than always grading the stale planned row.** Implemented on `feat/batch-68-delivered-ir-grading` from Mark's 2026-07-07/08 workout-fidelity feedback (spec `docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md`). **Why:** after Mark accepted the app's eased/substituted ride, the delivery rail correctly held a pushed proposal IR for what went to Zwift, but `PostWorkoutAnalysisService` still built `plannedWorkoutIr` from `planned_workouts.structured_workout`. That made the read say he attempted the original VO2 and grade the ride against VO2 work, even when he had actually accepted "drop VO2, ride easy Z2." **Implementation:** packet assembly now selects a `RideGradingTarget`: prefer the latest pushed `WorkoutDeliveryProposal` for the planned workout id, fall back to latest same-date pushed proposal for older delivery rows, and only then build the planned-row IR. The selected IR still flows through the existing `segment_ride_intervals` / `summarize_execution` path, so the interval grading math and whole-ride-average context rules are unchanged. The context packet adds `gradingTarget` (source, proposal id/status, event id, `origin`, `adjustment`) and `workoutAdherence` (including `actualWorkoutJson.changeSummary`) so the prompt can say "you did the recovery substitution/manual override" rather than narrating a VO2 attempt. `PROMPT_VERSION` is bumped to `post-workout-analysis-v4-2026-07-09`, making older ride reads stale for regeneration via the existing `_analysis_is_current` check. **Boundaries:** no migration, no delivery write, no grade-math rewrite, no frontend/shared schema change, and no change to Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, or Red-never-VO2. **Verification (local):** focused post-workout pytest **12 passed / 8 skipped**; full backend pytest **528 passed / 169 skipped**; backend ruff format/check clean; touched-file mypy clean. Full backend mypy still hits the known unrelated local `pydreo` missing-stub issue in `services/dreo_fan.py`. Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-09 — Batch 69 — Accept = logged; move session-logging post-ride

142. **Approving a coach-adjusted ride now seeds adherence immediately, and planned-ride session logging lives on the completed Today-card row rather than the morning check-in.** Implemented on `feat/batch-69-accept-logged` from the same workout-fidelity feedback thread (spec `docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md`). **Why:** two mismatches remained after #141: (a) approving an eased/substituted ride changed the live Zwift event but logged nothing, so Mark was later asked to re-type the app's own change; and (b) "How did your sessions go?" still lived under the morning `/check-in`, which meant the app was asking pre-ride how the ride had gone. **Implementation:** `ExecutableCoachingService.approve_adjustment` now idempotently seeds the `planned_workout` adherence row with `status='modified'` and accepted-adjustment detail in `actualWorkoutJson` (`type`, `intensity`, `changeSummary`, `source='accepted_adjustment'`), filling blank fields without clobbering a later real post-ride save. On the frontend, `/check-in` is reduced back to the morning read only, while the Batch 60 completed-ride Today-card flow gains the moved logger as one combined post-ride form that saves both the ride check-in and the planned-workout adherence in one action. The moved logger also surfaces the previously-missing structured substitution fields — **Outcome**, **Actual minutes**, **What did you do instead?**, **Target / intensity**, and **What changed?** — so changed rides round-trip more honestly through the existing adherence JSON that Batch 68 now reads. **Boundaries:** no migration, no verdict/Green-Amber-Red change, no change to #133/#135/Red-never-VO2, and unplanned rides keep the standalone post-ride check-in rather than gaining a fake planned-workout logger. **Verification (local):** focused backend pytest **7 passed / 34 skipped** (`test_executable_coaching.py`, `test_daily_loop.py`), backend ruff clean; focused web vitest **35 passed** (`CheckInPage`, `DashboardPage`); web build clean; web lint passes with the repo's 6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings. Full backend mypy still hits the known unrelated local `pydreo` missing-stub issue in `services/dreo_fan.py`. Tier 🟢 Mid.

### 2026-07-09 — Batch 70 — Weekly-mix maintenance & dynamic rebalancing

143. **The morning verdict now tracks Mark's weekly quality mix (VO2×1 / Sweet-Spot×1 / Zone-2×3) as a soft, readiness-gated quota, and when a cautious morning eases today's hard bike session it either re-patches it to a sound later day this week or says plainly it won't be made up — never silently.** Implemented on `feat/batch-70-weekly-mix` from Mark's 2026-07-07/08 workout-fidelity feedback (observation 4: "if it drops the VO2 for an easier Z2, does it notice no VO2 was done this week and patch it back in?"; spec `docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md`). **Why the soft quota (not a hard quota, not pure metric-driven):** a masters athlete keeps top-end fitness on a small, deliberate dose of quality work, so the mix is worth *protecting*; but forcing a VO2 onto a poor-recovery day to hit a number contradicts #133 / #135 / Red-never-VO2 / Batch 66 swap-first and is the burnout Mark fears. With no target the app can't even answer "did I miss my VO2?"; with no readiness veto it drifts too easy. Confirmed by Mark 2026-07-09: **mix is a protected target, readiness gets the veto, and any shortfall is made visible and explained.** **Implementation:** new pure `services/weekly_mix.py` — `summarize_weekly_mix` is a deterministic reducer over the week's planned + completed bike rows that reports, per bucket, the plan-derived `target` (not a hardcoded number — a recovery week with no VO2 reads `target=0`), what's `done` (`PlannedWorkout.status=='completed'`), what's still `due`, and `at_risk` when what's owed exceeds what's genuinely still scheduled (today's eased hard session no longer counts as a scheduled slot). The re-patch reuses the Batch 66 swap-first engine (`plan_swap_first`) — the same one-tap category-scoped `swap_day` move — extended with `PROTECTED_WEEKDAYS={Mon,Fri}` so a hard bike is never parked on Mark's Dumbbells/coffee days (belt-and-braces: those days carry no bike in the current plan, but it guards a future layout). `assemble_context_packet` always attaches `verdict.weeklyMix` (so the week view shows the mix even on Green) and, on an Amber/Red morning that eases today's hard session, appends the re-patch ("you'd be a VO2 short — moving it to Saturday keeps the week's quality work") or the explicit "no VO2 this week — readiness gets the veto" message to `planAdjustments`; `PROMPT_VERSION` bumps to `morning-analysis-v7-2026-07-09` (regenerates stale reads). `AnalysisOut.weeklyMix` + shared `weeklyMixSchema` surface it; a reusable `WeeklyMixCard` renders the done/target chips on the Home Today card and the `/delivery` Plan page (the Plan page also shows the shortfall message, reading `daily-loop.morningAnalysis.weeklyMix`). **Boundaries:** advisory only — nothing auto-schedules; no migration (derived read-only accounting over existing rows); Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2, and the ≥2-day no-stack rule are all untouched; empty-day *insertion* of a make-up session is out of scope (that needs Batch 71's editable quick-add) — the re-patch only ever trades with an existing easier bike day. **Verification (local, all green):** backend pytest **537 passed / 173 skipped** (new `test_weekly_mix.py`: bucket mapping, plan-derived target, past-miss vs future-slot, eased-today at-risk, `_eased_bucket` gating, re-patch/not-this-week shortfall, three DB-backed service cases; plus a protected-weekday `plan_swap_first` case and two DB-backed morning-analysis packet cases — the DB-backed cases skip locally without Postgres and run in CI), backend ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean, backend mypy **99 files** clean; shared typecheck + **14** tests; web `tsc` clean, lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), full web vitest **186 passed** (new `WeeklyMixCard.test.tsx`), build clean under Node 20. **Shipped** (PR #95, squash `7598b6f`): CI went green in both push and PR-context waves; production verified on the merge SHA (Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both `7598b6f`, web `/` + `/delivery` 200, auth-gated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` — now carrying `weeklyMix` — 401 direct and via Vercel). The live PWA *visual* walkthrough of the mix card is deferred to Craig (blocked locally per the UI-walkthrough method; the card renders only on a live authenticated Amber-with-hard-bike morning). Tier 🔴 High.

### 2026-07-09 — Batch 71 — Editable quick-add on the Week tab

144. **Tapping "+ Cycle / + Weights / + Flexibility" on the `/delivery` Week tab now opens a session picker with an editable duration instead of silently dropping a hardcoded 45-min Zone-2 ride.** Implemented on `feat/batch-71-editable-quick-add`, from Mark's 2026-07-09 sign-off feedback (screenshot: quick-add always inserted the same fixed default with no way to choose or adjust it) — a candidate item logged alongside the workout-fidelity thread but scoped independently (spec `docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md`, "Newly surfaced" section). **Why a catalog, not a full workout-authoring UI:** the ask was "let me pick and tweak what gets added," not a per-interval editor (that escape hatch already exists via the manual-override intensity dial, and Batch 67's real structured workouts). A small per-category subtype catalog, each with a bounded duration range, gives Mark a real choice without reopening the authoring-fidelity problem Batch 67 just closed. **Implementation:** new `QUICK_ADD_CATALOG` in `services/plan_actions.py` — cycle: endurance / sweet_spot / recovery (drawn from the existing `WORKOUT_TYPE_CYCLE` set); weights: maintenance / recovery (`WORKOUT_TYPE_WEIGHTS`); flexibility: mobility only (matches today's single flexibility type) — each option carrying a title, workout type, intensity target, default duration, and a `[min, max]` duration bound. `workout_for_selection(category, subtype, duration_min)` resolves the chosen option, validates the duration against its bound (422 outside range), and builds the `structured_workout` (bike: warm-up/main/cool-down steps sized so the total sums to the chosen duration; strength/mobility: unchanged single-block shape). `add_workout` and the `POST /days/{date}/workouts` route accept optional `subtype` + `durationMin`; omitting both preserves the exact prior default behaviour (first catalog entry = the old hardcoded ride), so existing callers/tests are unaffected. A new `GET /api/v1/plan-actions/quick-add-options?category=` lists the catalog for a category (shared `quickAddOptionsEnvelopeSchema`/`planAddWorkoutInputSchema` gained `subtype`/`durationMin`). On the frontend, a new `QuickAddSheet` (same `Sheet` pattern as `MoveWorkoutSheet`) replaces the instant-add buttons on `WeekAheadPage`: tapping a category button fetches its options, lets Mark pick a subtype (defaulting duration to that subtype's default) and edit the duration within its bound, then submits. **Boundaries:** no migration; existing move/skip/swap flows untouched; no per-interval editor; the default no-subtype path is preserved byte-for-byte so nothing regresses for any caller that doesn't yet send a subtype. **Verification (local):** backend pytest **541 passed / 175 skipped** (3 new cases: catalog listing + unknown-category 422, subtype+duration override producing the right workout/steps, out-of-bounds duration → 422), backend ruff check clean, mypy clean on touched files (full-repo mypy still hits the known unrelated `pydreo` missing-stub gap in `services/dreo_fan.py`); shared typecheck clean; web `tsc` clean, full web vitest **186 passed** (updated `WeekAheadPage.test.tsx` to drive the picker: select a subtype, confirm, assert the POST body), lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), build clean under Node 20. **Manually verified in a live preview** (headless Chromium + a temporary mock `/api` middleware — no prod contact, cleaned up after): opened the sheet from a rest day, confirmed the three cycle subtypes render with correct default/min/max, selecting "Sweet Spot" updated the bound to 25–75 min, editing the duration and clicking Add posted successfully and closed with a "Workout added" toast. Tier 🟢 Mid.

145. **A chronic REM miss now surfaces a broader, rotating set of REM interventions handed out one or two at a time, instead of the same two static lines every week.** Implemented on `feat/batch-72-chronic-rem-depth` from Mark's 2026-07-09 sign-off note (his REM has run below its age norm since he got the watch, so the Batch 59 chronic-pattern card flags `rem_sleep_pct` most weeks but only ever showed the same standing pair) — a separate sleep thread from the 67–71 workout-fidelity work (spec `docs/designs/workout-fidelity-and-feedback-loop.md`, "Batch 72" section). **Root cause:** `chronic_patterns._actions_for` mapped `rem_sleep_pct` to exactly two hardcoded strings (a `{bedtime}` lights-out line + a "don't move the wake time earlier" line), so the same advice repeated indefinitely; every other chronic metric was unaffected. **Why a deterministic, stateless rotation (not a persisted "shown" ledger):** for a 1–2-user app a persisted cursor is unjustified state — a calendar-week seed gives the same "rotate through a wider set" behaviour, is reproducible in tests, needs no migration, and matches the deterministic/read-only norm the rest of the chronic-pattern surface already follows (#132/#143). **Implementation:** new pure `services/rem_interventions.py` holds an **ordered library of 12 REM-specific levers** — each a short imperative action grounded in the sleep-protocol values where they exist (`bedtime`, `sealTargetTime`, `preCoolTemperatureC`, `coherenceBreathingTime`, `latestSnackTime`) or in standard REM physiology (REM is late-cycle heavy and fragile to short sleep, alcohol, warmth, late stimulation, and circadian drift): wake-time anchoring, protecting the last cycle, a hard bedtime, alcohol-free evenings, an afternoon caffeine cut-off, a cool room in the back half of the night, evening light-down, a consistent wind-down, late-meal timing, stress offload, REM-rebound recovery, and keeping hard/late rides off priority nights. `select_rem_interventions(as_of, …)` hands out a **focused window of two**, seeded from the ISO-Monday of `as_of` (stable Mon–Sun, advancing weekly) and walking the whole library before repeating (12 ÷ 2 = a 6-week cycle); a measured sleep **driver biases** the week (thermal → cool-room, load → late-ride, stress → wind-down/offload) by pinning its lever into the set even if the blind rotation had not reached it. The `rem_sleep_pct` branch of `_actions_for` calls the selector (the existing driver-derived line still leads); `ChronicSuggestion` gains an optional `rotation` ({`periodLabel`, `shown`, `total`}); shared `chronicSuggestionItemSchema` gains an optional nullable `rotation`; `ChronicSuggestionsCard` renders a "Rotating focus — N of M levers this week, a fresh set next week" caption under the REM actions (shared across Home's "Last night's sleep" and `/sleep`). **Boundaries:** no migration, no new endpoint, no Anthropic-boundary call (the library is deterministic and unit-testable without `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`); the Green/Amber/Red verdict, #133 soft-sleep, #135 Poor-readiness, and Red-never-VO2 are all untouched (read-only sleep-coaching depth, the Batch 59 contract); **no non-REM chronic suggestion changes** (regression-guarded). **Verification (local, all green):** backend pytest **546 passed / 175 skipped** (new `test_rem_interventions.py` — unique ids + rendering, stable within a week, walks the whole library before repeating + wraps, driver pins its lever every week, no duplicate when already scheduled, protocol values render; plus two `test_chronic_patterns.py` cases — REM rotates week-to-week and carries `rotation` and drops the pre-72 static line, a non-REM chronic carries no rotation), backend ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean, mypy clean on touched files (full-repo mypy still hits the known unrelated `pydreo` missing-stub gap in `services/dreo_fan.py`); shared typecheck clean + **14** tests (added a `rotation` assertion); web `tsc` clean, full web vitest **186 passed** (`SleepPage.test.tsx` now asserts the rotating-focus caption), lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), build clean under Node 20. **Deferred to Craig (manual):** the live PWA *visual* walkthrough of the caption — blocked locally per the UI-walkthrough method (needs the proxied dev build + `/activate`) and only renders on a live authenticated daily-loop with an active chronic REM flag; the shared component is unit-tested rendering the real card with the rotation field. **Shipped** (PR #97, squash `92019ed`): CI went green in both push and PR-context waves across all 7 jobs plus a successful Vercel preview; production verified on the merge SHA (Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both `92019ed`, web `/` + `/sleep` 200, auth-gated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` — now carrying `rotation` — 401 direct and via Vercel). Tier 🔴 High.

147. **Skip and Remove are now deliberately separate semantics: a coach-planned session keeps Skip (`status='skipped'`, adherence-visible history), while a workout Mark added himself gets Remove (`is_active=false`, no skipped-adherence noise) and still deletes any live Zwift event.** Implemented on `feat/batch-74-home-skip-remove` from Mark's 2026-07-10 follow-on feedback after Batch 73 shipped: a skipped workout still came back on Home after reload, and an added ride could only be "skipped" rather than actually removed. **Why this split:** the app already has two different kinds of session intent. A coached/planned workout being skipped is meaningful history and should stay visible to adherence/reporting, which the existing free-text `status` column already captures. A user-added filler ride is not the same kind of evidence; when Mark removes it, the row should simply leave the active plan instead of manufacturing a skipped coaching event. **Implementation:** `daily_loop._planned_workouts` now matches the Week schedule seam by excluding `status='skipped'`, so Home no longer resurrects skipped sessions. `ExecutableCoachingService.remove_workout(...)` is a narrow sibling to `skip_workout(...)`: it is only allowed for `source='plan_action_add'`, deletes any live intervals.icu event through the existing delivery rail, deactivates the row (`is_active=false`), and records a `workout_removed` audit row; planned sessions still use the unchanged skip path and its `workout_skipped` audit. `DashboardPage.tsx` now keys off `workout.source` and gives an added workout a first-class **Remove** action on Home (with Swap moved to overflow), while planned workouts keep Skip. **Boundaries:** no migration; no change to the delivery rail beyond reusing its existing delete path; no change to planned-session adherence semantics; no batch broadening into Week editing or scheduler logic. **Verification (local):** targeted backend pytest on `test_executable_coaching.py`, `test_daily_loop.py`, and `test_plan_actions.py` **9 passed / 45 skipped** (new cases: remove deactivates an added workout and deletes its Zwift event, remove rejects non-added workouts, Home excludes skipped workouts, Week parity test), backend ruff clean, touched-file mypy clean; web `DashboardPage.test.tsx` **34 passed** (new Remove visibility + confirm/remove call), web lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), web build clean under Node 20. 148. **The cycle quick-add catalog now covers "a ride with some Z3 / some efforts" in one tap, and a plain "just ride it" line makes the post-hoc analysis path discoverable — a real interval builder stays deliberately out of scope.** Implemented on `feat/batch-75-bespoke-rides` from Mark's 2026-07-10 follow-on feedback (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 75): the Batch 71 cycle catalog only offered endurance/sweet-spot/recovery, so any ride with some tempo/threshold work or short efforts had no quick-add match. **Why extend the catalog rather than build a per-interval editor:** the app's model for a genuinely bespoke ride is post-hoc analysis (ride it, then the post-ride read covers it) — a full interval builder would duplicate that path and add authoring-fidelity risk the app just closed in Batch 67. The common cases (some Z3, some short efforts) are narrow enough to cover as two more real, structured presets. **Implementation:** `QUICK_ADD_CATALOG["cycle"]` (`services/plan_actions.py`) gains `tempo` (**Tempo / Threshold (Z3)**, `bike_tempo`, steady ~84% FTP main block) and `vo2_efforts` (**VO2 (with efforts)**, `bike_vo2`, work/recovery interval pattern at 118%/60%), both authored with real Batch 67 ramp warm-up/cool-down steps (`warmup_ramp_pct`/`cooldown_ramp_pct` on `QuickAddOption`) instead of the flat "easy" block the three original subtypes use — matching the step grammar `expand_structured_steps`/`validate_deliverable_bike_workout` already parse. `workout_for_selection` gained an interval branch: for `vo2_efforts`, the chosen duration's main portion resolves to the nearest whole rep count in `[min_reps, max_reps]` (3–8, at 2 min work / 2 min recovery), and the returned `planned_duration_min` reports the *true* traced duration (which may differ slightly from an off-boundary request) rather than echoing the raw input, so `duration_min` always sums the steps. `tempo`'s bounds are 25–65 min (default 40); `vo2_efforts`'s are 30–50 min (default 38, landing on exactly 5 reps). Both map into the existing `weekly_mix`/`weekly_restructure` category buckets (`bike_tempo`→Z2, `bike_vo2`→VO2) with no new category work. The Week page and Home's rest-day copy each gained one plain line — "Doing something different? Just ride it — I'll read it after." — next to the existing add controls, pointing at the unplanned-ride post-hoc read path that already exists (`DashboardPage.tsx`'s "After your ride" section). **Boundaries:** no migration; no shared-schema change (`quickAddOptionSchema` already covers arbitrary catalog entries); no per-interval editor UI; existing endurance/sweet_spot/recovery/maintenance/mobility subtypes are untouched (flat-block shape preserved exactly). **Verification (local, all green):** backend pytest **550 passed / 179 skipped** (4 new cases: tempo builds a real ramp warm-up/cool-down and traces the duration, VO2-efforts builds a 5×2min/2min interval pattern at the right %, an off-boundary VO2-efforts duration rounds to the nearest valid rep count and reports the true traced duration, an out-of-bounds VO2-efforts duration 422s; updated the catalog-listing test for the two new subtypes), backend ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean, mypy clean on `plan_actions.py`; shared typecheck + 14 tests unaffected; web `tsc` clean, full web vitest **192 passed**, lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), build clean under Node 20. **Shipped** (PR #100, squash `1e448d2`): CI went green in both push and PR-context waves across all 7 jobs plus a successful Vercel preview; production verified on the merge SHA (Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both `1e448d2`, web `/` + `/delivery` 200, auth-gated `GET /api/v1/plan-actions/quick-add-options?category=cycle` 401 direct and via Vercel). Tier 🟢 Mid.

149. **Batch 76 settles Skip semantics around already-done reality: a whole-day skip means "skip what remains," not "rewrite the day," and "done" includes both `status='completed'` and an already-logged adherence outcome.** Implemented on `feat/batch-76-skip-done-sessions` from Mark's 2026-07-10 organiser feedback (`docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 76). **Two `/batch-start` calls were settled:** (1) keep the whole-day control available, but when the day already contains a completed session the UI must say **Skip remaining** and explain that completed sessions stay put; we do **not** hide the action, because Mark still needs the one-tap way to clear the sessions he has not done yet. (2) "logged" is broader than `status='completed'`: the skip guard treats the latest linked adherence row as done when it records `completed`, `modified`, `done`, or `did_something_else`, because those are all evidence that the session's reality has already been captured and should not be overwritten by a later skip. **Implementation:** `PlanActionService.skip_day(...)` now filters its active-day workout list to exclude both completed rows and workouts whose latest adherence row is in that done set, so a whole-day skip only touches still-outstanding sessions. `ExecutableCoachingService.skip_workout(...)` mirrors Batch 60's completed-session move lock and 409s with a clear "already done" message before touching intervals.icu when the session is already completed or already logged. `WeekAheadPage.tsx` keeps the day-level action visible but relabels it to **Skip remaining** and adds an explanatory note whenever the day already contains a completed session, matching the backend truth. **Boundaries:** no migration; no change to remove semantics, verdict logic, #133, #135, or Red-never-VO2; genuinely outstanding skip/remove flows are unchanged. **Verification (local, green):** targeted backend pytest on `test_plan_actions.py` + `test_executable_coaching.py` **13 passed / 38 skipped** (new cases: whole-day skip leaves a completed and a logged session intact while skipping only the outstanding one; per-item skip of a logged-done session 409s), backend ruff clean, touched-file mypy clean; `WeekAheadPage.test.tsx` **4 passed**; web lint clean except the repo's 6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings; web build clean under Node 20. Tier 🟢 Mid.

151. **Batch 78 delivers an outdoor ride to Garmin Connect by uploading Garmin's own structured-workout JSON directly on the existing garth session, recorded in a new `garmin_workout_deliveries` table — the indoor→Zwift rail is left untouched.** Building on `feat/batch-78-outdoor-garmin-delivery` from Mark's `Workout Structure for The App 10.07.26.xlsx` Indoor/Outdoor field + Q2 (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 78; design note `docs/designs/outdoor-garmin-delivery.md`). Batch 77 already stores the `delivery` flag (`indoor`/`outdoor`) in `planned_workouts.structured_workout` and skips outdoor rides from Zwift; this batch gives them a home. **Two `/batch-start` calls were settled with Craig:** (1) **direct Garmin upload, not intervals.icu's own Garmin sync.** `garminconnect` 0.3.6 — already our authenticated (read-only-today) dependency — ships `upload_workout`/`schedule_workout`/`get_workouts`/`delete_workout`/`unschedule_workout` and a `CyclingWorkout` model with a `POWER_ZONE` target, so we can author a power-target ride straight onto Mark's Garmin calendar. Direct upload gives a synchronous result we can be honest about on failure (#97), needs no dependency on Mark having wired Garmin↔intervals.icu, and keeps the intervals.icu path meaning "Zwift" only; routing through intervals.icu's Garmin sync would make delivery async/unobservable and overload that path's semantics. (2) **A new `garmin_workout_deliveries` table (one migration), not a reuse of `workout_delivery_proposals`.** The `provider` discriminator on the intervals table would technically fit, but its columns are intervals-shaped (`zwo_xml` NOT NULL, `intervals_event_id`/`intervals_payload`) and reuse would force provider-guards onto the three live Zwift-path queries (`latest_delivered_for_date`/`_for_workout`, week-ahead) — real risk to the rail Mark rides daily. A dedicated table fully isolates the Garmin write path (the acceptance criterion's "isolated"), stores the Garmin workout-id + scheduled-id + payload under honest names, and survives Batch 77's row re-versioning by keying on `(user_id, workout_date)`. The indoor/outdoor *flag* itself still rides in `structured_workout` JSONB (no migration for that — shipped in #150). **Implementation:** pure `services/garmin_workout_export.py::build_garmin_workout(ir, ftp_watts)` maps the Batch 67 IR to Garmin's cycling-workout JSON (flat expanded steps — warmup/interval/recovery/cooldown types, `time` end-condition, `power.zone` targets in absolute watts derived from FTP; ramp steps become a low→high target range, steady steps a tight band); write methods on `GarminConnectClient`; async `GarminWorkoutDeliveryService` uploads+schedules via `asyncio.to_thread`, upserts the delivery row, is idempotent per current version, honest on failure (`status='failed'` + `last_error`, never silently dropped), and replaces in place on edit. `ExecutableCoachingService.reconcile_deliveries` now also reconciles outdoor bike workouts to Garmin (isolated per workout; Garmin is only touched when the window actually contains an outdoor ride, so the indoor-only path and its tests are unchanged). Outdoor delivery status is surfaced read-only on the workout so a failure is visible. **Boundaries:** the indoor→Zwift rail, verdict logic, #133, #135, and Red-never-VO2 are unchanged; no arbitrary graph editor; Garmin remains ingestion-direct (#27) — this only *writes* a planned workout, it does not change the read/sync path. 153. **Batch 80 makes the post-workout read render an explicit, honest deviation verdict when a completed ride diverged from the day's planned/delivered session — was overriding the plan the right call (Mark's Q1a) — judged on the objective grade, never sycophantic.** Implemented on `feat/batch-80-deviation-verdict` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 80). **Why:** Mark's first question after doing his own thing is "was that the right call?" — the read previously graded the ride but never said plainly whether backing off / skipping / self-choosing was smart or a setback. **Implementation (backend-only, `services/post_workout_analysis.py`):** a pure `detect_ride_deviation(...)` runs in `assemble_context_packet` and attaches a deterministic `rideDeviation` to the packet, reusing the Batch 68 delivered-vs-actual grade (`execution`) as the objective anchor. Divergence fires only when a bike session was actually on the plan/delivery and he didn't do it as prescribed: (a) `skipped_and_rode` — the day's bike workout is `status='skipped'` yet a ride was completed; (b) `easier_than_planned` / `harder_than_planned` — every gradable work interval came in off target in the *same* direction (all under / all over), so it's a different session, not a fade (a real attempt lands ≥1 interval on target → not flagged). It never flags an **approved coach-adjustment** (Batch 68 `adjustment.changed` / Batch 69 `actualWorkoutJson.source='accepted_adjustment'` → `wasApprovedAdjustment`, a sanctioned change, not a self-chosen override) and never flags a day with **no bike plan** (`free_ride` — a spontaneous ride is not a plan override, so casual rides stay unflagged). The packet carries the divergence `kind`/`reason`, the objective `signals` (work/on/over/under counts), the planned-vs-actual summary, and the morning readiness (`morningReadiness` from the day's morning verdict) so the good-call/bad-call *judgement* is the prompt's, anchored on readiness + numbers. `SYSTEM_PROMPT` gains the deviation-verdict instruction (explicitly forbids softening a poor call into praise or manufacturing a problem where the call was sound — the one place it must not be sycophantic) plus three output rules; `PROMPT_VERSION` → `post-workout-analysis-v5-2026-07-11`, which regenerates older ride reads via the existing `_analysis_is_current` staleness check. The deviation verdict flows through the existing post-workout `output_markdown`, so **no frontend/shared change**. **Boundaries:** **no migration**; no delivery write; no grade-math change; Green/Amber/Red, #133 soft-sleep, #135 Poor-readiness, and Red-never-VO2 all untouched (no morning/verdict/executable-coaching code changed). **Scope call:** a genuinely unplanned ride on a no-bike-plan day is treated as a free ride, not an override — flagging every spontaneous ride would be noise, and Mark's Q1a presupposes a plan to override. **Verification (local, green):** backend pytest **565 passed / 192 skipped** (7 new pure `detect_ride_deviation` cases — easier/harder/on-plan-attempt/skipped/approved-adjustment/free-ride/ungradable-no-false-positive — run locally; 3 new DB-backed `assemble_context_packet` integration cases — self-chosen easy ride on a Red day, skipped key session on a Green day, on-plan sweet-spot → no deviation — plus approved-adjustment + free-ride assertions folded into the existing Batch 68 tests, run in CI), backend ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean, `mypy src` clean (103 files). Tier 🔴 High. **Shipped** (PR #105, squash `1598d12`): CI went green across all 7 jobs in both push and PR-context waves plus a successful Vercel preview; squash-merged to `main`; production verified on the merge SHA (Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both `1598d12`, web `/` + `/delivery` 200, and unauthenticated `GET /api/v1/daily-loop` 401 direct and via Vercel — the deviation verdict rides in that auth-gated payload's downstream post-workout read, no new endpoint). The deviation copy itself is deferred to a live-use eyeball on the next genuinely diverged ride (automated smoke can't exercise a Claude-written `output_markdown`).

159. **Batch 86 leads the morning brief with a deterministic "Today" action block — the workout adjustment first-class and tappable-to-approve, plus swap/sleep/thermal — assembled by the backend next to the prose, with the coaching reasoning kept below.** Implemented on `feat/batch-86-today-actions` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 86; depends on Batch 85). **Why:** Mark reads the brief for the "why" but wanted the day's actions scannable and actionable up top rather than buried in prose. **Decision settled at `/batch-start` (with Craig): the actions are assembled deterministically by the backend, not emitted by the model.** The batch text said "the model emits structured actions," but the pattern it cited (`swapSuggestion` / `weeklyMix` / `planAdjustments`) is in fact 100% deterministic backend computation frozen in `context_packet["verdict"]`, and the shared Anthropic boundary (`anthropic_text.generate_anthropic_text`) is text/markdown-only — nothing in the repo parses model JSON. 160. **Batch 87 makes every supported post-activity read check-in-first: the hourly Garmin poll syncs and nudges without generating, the generic activity-linked check-in force-dispatches inline to the ride/strength/flexibility/walk reader, and a 20:30 local backstop generates any same-day session Mark ignores.** Implemented on `feat/batch-87-checkin-first-post-workout`. **Kickoff calls:** generation is not hard-gated on subjective input — all fields remain optional and the CTA **"Read my workout"** can be submitted empty for the objective read; pending copy is **"Reading your workout…"**; the nudge is **"How did it feel? / Your {workout} is synced — check in and I will read it."** and deep-links to that activity on Home; the backstop is a same-day sweep at **20:30 Europe/London** with no age threshold. 161. **Batch 88 gives Mark full control of a ride's structure via a free-form segment builder, and scopes a deliberate reversal of the Red-never-VO2 invariant to his explicit manual authoring path only: there the power / ramp / Red-never-VO2 gates become non-blocking warnings, while the coach/automated path keeps all three hard.** Implemented on `feat/batch-88-freeform-workout-editor` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 88; full spec `docs/designs/full-control-workout-editor.md`; depends on the shipped Batch 77). **Why:** Craig wants Mark to be able to build an arbitrary multi-segment workout on any given day — beyond Batch 77's single interval-pair-or-block shape and the Today-card's whole-workout scaling — warned but never blocked. **Key finding:** the delivery format was never the limit — `expand_structured_steps` already walks an arbitrary ordered `steps` list (ramp / steady / interval-pattern, any count/order) into the IR that both the intervals.icu/Zwift push and the Batch 78 Garmin export consume; the single-pair-or-block ceiling lived only in the builder spec `CustomBikeWorkoutSpec` and its UI. So this is a builder + UI change over the same rail, not a delivery rewrite. **`/batch-start` decisions (settled with Craig):** (1) **mechanism = a `soft_gates` flag on the builder, defaulting to hard**, not a separate validation entrypoint — `build_freeform_bike_workout` is the single manual chokepoint (called only by the two manual endpoints; the coach path via `block_generator`/`vo2_progression`/`weekly_restructure`/`plan_import` never touches it), so threading `soft_gates=True` from `add_workout`/`edit_structured_workout` cleanly scopes the reversal, and the default-hard branch keeps a future non-manual caller safe (proven by test); (2) **warnings contract = `warnings: [{code, detail}]` on the `WorkoutActionEnvelope`, sibling to `errors`** (the advisory analog), codes `power_out_of_band` / `missing_ramp` / `red_vo2`, shared `apiWarningSchema` + `workoutActionResponseSchema`, structured so copy stays swappable (Batch 86 principle); (3) **live power-profile preview is in scope now** (SVG trapezoid/bar profile + running total, built from the expanded IR the engine already produces); (4) **no migration** — segments serialize into the existing `structured_workout` JSON `steps` grammar; (5) **a minimal hard floor stays even under soft warnings** — power `1-300`% FTP and positive per-segment durations and total ≤ `480` min are rejected outright (undeliverable garbage the ZWO/intervals/Garmin payloads can't represent), while sane-but-aggressive choices (power `1-44` or `151-300`, a VO2 set on a Red day, no warm-up/cool-down ramp) only warn. **Implementation (backend):** `CustomBikeWorkoutSpec`/`build_custom_bike_workout` replaced by `FreeformBikeWorkoutSpec` (ordered `WorkoutSegment` tuple, `kind ∈ ramp/steady/interval`) + `build_freeform_bike_workout(...) -> (BuiltCustomBikeWorkout, [WorkoutWarning])`, reusing the exact per-kind step emission and labelling leading/trailing ramps "Warm-up ramp"/"Cool-down ramp" so the expander's phase detection is unchanged; the power (soft-band) and ramp gates warn-or-raise by `soft_gates`. The **Red-VO2** warning is computed in the service (`PlanActionService._append_red_vo2_warning`) via the existing `blocks_red_vo2` predicate against the stored morning verdict — the delivery gates (`send_today` / `approve_adjustment` / `auto_push_due`) keep Red-never-VO2 **hard** for coach adjustments, so the reversal is strictly the workout Mark built for himself. The router body is a discriminated segment union whose pydantic bounds enforce only the absolute floor (power `1-300`, duration `1-480`), never the soft band. **Implementation (frontend):** `StructuredWorkoutSheet` rewritten as a segment-list editor (add/remove/reorder rows, per-row kind selector + fields), live client-side warnings shown as amber "Heads-up… you can still deliver it" hints (never blocking submit), a live power-profile preview + running total, and a round-trip parser from the stored `steps`; `WeekAheadPage` sends `{delivery, segments}` to the unchanged add (`customBike`) + structured-edit endpoints and surfaces server `warnings` as toasts. **Boundaries:** indoor→Zwift and outdoor→Garmin delivery paths unchanged (authoring only); completed workouts still cannot be structurally edited; verdict / #133 / #135 unchanged; Red-never-VO2 stays hard everywhere except the explicit manual authoring path. **Verification (local, green):** backend `test_plan_actions` **15 passed / 17 skipped** (DB-backed cases run in CI) — new: segment→steps mapping, arbitrary order preserved, soft gates warn (power+ramp), hard mode blocks both, absolute floor rejects power>300 + total>480 even soft, the import gate stays hard on a rampless plan, and DB-backed VO2-on-Red warns-but-still-delivers + endurance-on-Red has no warning; backend ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean, `mypy src` clean (105 files); shared typecheck + **16** tests; web `tsc` clean, full web vitest **215 passed** (6 new `StructuredWorkoutSheet` cases: default payload, add interval in order, remove+reorder, out-of-band power warns-but-submits, missing-ramp warning, cleared field blocks submit), web lint 0 errors (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings), build clean under Node 20. The phone eyeball of the segment editor + a real free-form ride reaching Zwift/Garmin is a closeout/live-use step. Tier 🔴 High. **Shipped** (PR #113, squash `13c64e5`): CI went green across all jobs in both push and PR-context waves plus a Vercel preview; squash-merged to `main` as `13c64e571ff7c356a0fac4b63749a4777dbe4f07` (one `fix(test)` follow-up after CI caught a DB-backed `add_workout` case still reading `.id` off the new `WorkoutActionResult`); production verified on the merge SHA (Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both `13c64e5`, web `/` + `/delivery` 200, unauthenticated `POST /api/v1/plan-actions/days/{date}/workouts` + `.../planned-workouts/{id}/structured` 401 direct and via Vercel). 162. **Batch 89 enables Row Level Security on the 18 `coach.*` tables migration 001 left uncovered, as defense-in-depth — no policies, guarded so it only applies on Supabase.** Implemented on `fix/batch-89-coach-rls` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 89). **Why:** the 2026-07-11 full-app QA review (`QA_REVIEW_2026-07-11.md`, Finding 1) found the Supabase security advisor raising a **critical `rls_disabled`** lint — migration 001 only put the five auth/notification tables (`profiles`, `refresh_tokens`, `push_subscriptions`, `notification_preferences`, `audit_log`) under RLS, so every table added in migrations 002-014 (all of Mark's health data) was left with RLS off. This Postgres is shared with a separate public-facing movie app whose anon key ships in its frontend, which raises the stakes. **Key finding (verified while scoping):** the `anon` and `authenticated` roles currently hold **no grants** on the `coach` schema (`has_schema_privilege('anon','coach','USAGE') = false`, and `false` for SELECT/INSERT on the tables), and the REST Data API is even egress-restricted (402) — so nothing is actually reachable today. The exposure is therefore **latent**, not open: the real fix is a backstop so a future stray `GRANT` or an "Exposed schemas" change can't leak data, plus clearing the advisor. **Design:** enable RLS with **no policies**. The FastAPI backend connects as the `postgres` **owner** role, which bypasses RLS (no `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY`) — proven by the fact that `profiles` reads work in prod today despite 001's `auth.uid()`-scoped policies (a non-owner would be denied when `auth.uid()` is NULL). So RLS-with-no-policy is deny-all for `anon`/`authenticated` and a no-op for the app, exactly the posture `audit_log` already has. **Implementation:** migration `015_coach_rls.py` holds an `RLS_TABLES` constant (the 17 remaining coach model tables + `alembic_version`) and emits `ALTER TABLE coach.<t> ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` for each, wrapped in migration 001's exact `IF EXISTS (SELECT FROM information_schema.schemata WHERE schema_name = 'auth')` guard so it runs only on Supabase and is a no-op on plain Postgres — keeping CI's `migration-check` (upgrade head → downgrade base) and the unit-test Postgres green; downgrade disables. A pure regression test (`tests/test_coach_rls_migration.py`) asserts 001's set ∪ 015's set equals the coach model tables on `Base.metadata`, so a future model table shipping without RLS fails the test. **Boundaries:** no schema/data change beyond the RLS flag; no policies (owner-bypass model); verdict / #133 / #135 / Red-never-VO2 untouched; the auth tables' existing policies unchanged. **Verification (local, green):** new test 3 passed; backend pytest **598 passed / 200 skipped**; ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean; `mypy src` clean (106 files); migration chain single-head `015` and the offline-rendered upgrade SQL confirmed as the guarded 18-table `ENABLE` block. Tier 🟢 Mid. **Shipped** (PR #114, squash `cae3888`): Craig made the repo public → the GitHub Actions billing block cleared, both CI waves went green across all 7 jobs (incl. `migration-check` on real Postgres) plus a Vercel preview; squash-merged to `main` as `cae3888adb4a8e72e4869c5c59a79ed0e521cd1b`. **Production verified on the merge SHA:** Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both `cae3888`, web `/` 200, unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` 401 (app up + auth intact — RLS did not break the app); migration 015 applied on Railway startup → **RLS ON for all 23 `coach` tables (0 off)**, and the Supabase **critical `rls_disabled` advisory cleared** (coach tables now report only the benign INFO `rls_enabled_no_policy`, confirming deny-all with the owner-bypass intact). Separately surfaced for Craig (not part of this batch): the shared project's REST Data API is egress-restricted (402, `exceed_egress_quota`) — read-pressure stats point at the co-hosted movie app full-scanning its public tables (`movies`/`movie_credits`/`collection_items` show `idx_scan=0`).

164. **Batch 91 makes the morning brief state bed/wake, the date, and Mark's check-in in his own local, human terms — local wall-clock times beside the `*Utc` fields, an authoritative header-date label, and the check-in word — so the read never prints an hour-behind UTC time, re-derives the wrong date, or surfaces the "subjective feel 6" he never recognised giving.** Implemented on `feat/batch-91-brief-read-fidelity` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 91; surfaced by Mark's 2026-07-12 feedback). **Why:** the packet fed the model naive-UTC bed/wake (`sleepStartUtc`), only `subjectDate`/`subjectWeekday` for the header, and the raw `subjectiveScore` int — so a BST night (`00:17Z`) could read as 00:17 not 01:17, the date could drift to "13 July" when the model re-derived it, and the one-tap "OK" check-in came back as "subjective feel 6". **Kickoff decision (settled with Craig at `/batch-start`):** the check-in score→word map is done **in the packet, not as a prompt instruction** — a deterministic, unit-testable field consistent with Batch 90/91's "supply it, never let the model derive it" philosophy; the raw `subjectiveScore` stays for the deterministic verdict. **Implementation (backend-only, `services/morning_analysis.py`):** (1) `_sleep_packet` now takes `player.timezone` and adds `sleepStartLocal`/`sleepEndLocal` — the naive-UTC bed/wake rendered as the user's local wall-clock `HH:MM` via `_local_clock` (`.replace(tzinfo=UTC).astimezone(ZoneInfo(tz))`, unknown-zone → UTC fallback), **alongside** the untouched `*Utc` fields; (2) a top-level `subjectDateLabel` (`_date_label` → e.g. "Sunday 12 July 2026", built without the platform-specific `%-d` for portability) is supplied beside `subjectWeekday`; (3) `subjective_score_label` (anchors from the frontend one-tap scale `CheckInPage.tsx` `OVERALL_OPTIONS`: 2=Rough, 4=Meh, 6=OK, 8=Good, 10=Great; off-scale legacy values fall to the nearest band; `None`→`None`) adds `subjectiveLabel` to both `manualEntries[]` and the verdict block. **Prompt (91.2/91.3):** `SYSTEM_PROMPT` extends Batch 90's authoritative-`subjectWeekday` rule to `subjectDateLabel` (never re-derive/reformat the date) and time-of-day (state bed/wake from `sleepStartLocal`/`sleepEndLocal`, never print a `*Utc` timestamp or convert one), and instructs the read to refer to the check-in by `subjectiveLabel` (e.g. "you said you felt OK"), never the raw `subjectiveScore`/"6/10" term; three `outputRules` tokens added; `PROMPT_VERSION` → `morning-analysis-v11-2026-07-12` (regenerates stale reads via the existing staleness check). Because the whole `context_packet` is JSON-dumped to the model, the packet keeps both the structured `*Utc`/`subjectiveScore` fields and the human local/label fields, and the prompt rules are the guard against leaking the former into rendered prose. **Boundaries:** **no migration**, no frontend change (the score→word anchors are duplicated from `OVERALL_OPTIONS`, which Batch 94 will unify end-to-end), no shared-schema change (the new fields are internal packet fields the model reads, not surfaced on `AnalysisOut`); the deterministic `_morning_verdict` still reads `subjective_score` exactly as before, so Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, and Red-never-VO2 are untouched. **Verification (local, green):** backend pytest **604 passed / 200 skipped** (6 new pure cases — BST+GMT DST localization with `*Utc` retained, missing-time/bad-zone tolerance, the portable date label, the score→word map incl. off-scale + `None`, the manual-entry packet carrying both score and word, and a prompt-rule regression that the read is told to use local times/label and never print a `*Utc` timestamp or the raw score; the DB-backed main packet test also asserts the GMT-night local clock, `subjectDateLabel`, and both `subjectiveLabel`s, and runs in CI), backend ruff check + `ruff format --check` clean, `mypy src` clean (105 files). The phone eyeball of the next real morning brief (local bed/wake time, correct date, "OK" wording) is a closeout/live-use step — an LLM-written brief can't be smoke-tested. Tier 🔴 High. **Shipped** (PR #116, squash `5fa2f05`): both CI waves passed all 7 jobs in push and PR-context plus a Vercel preview; squash-merged to `main` as `5fa2f05535e90c623826746d4fc6ed7294fa8afb`. **Production verified on the merge SHA:** Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both `5fa2f05`, web `/` + `/check-in` 200, unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` 401 direct and via Vercel (the morning brief rides in that auth-gated payload; no new endpoint, no migration). 165. **Batch 92 makes the morning thermal read describe the room while Mark was actually asleep and credit a genuine pre-cool as separate evidence.** Implemented on `feat/batch-92-overnight-thermal-window` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 92; surfaced by Mark's 2026-07-12 feedback). **Why:** morning analysis queried a private fixed 18:00→08:00 window, so an 18:1x reading of 24.05°C became the claimed overnight peak even though the sleep-period peak was ~20.2°C; the `/bedroom` chart separately used 21:30→09:00, and the pre-bed 18.64°C low could only produce `precool_target_missed`. **Kickoff decision:** keep the shared 21:30→09:00 chart window as the observation/query envelope and fallback, then expose `preCoolLowC`, `sleepOnsetC`, and `preCoolDropC` as the explicit pre-bed signal beside sleep-only `indoorPeakC`/`indoorLowC`/`indoorLastC`; a material ≥1°C drop or a pre-cool low at/below the 19.5°C disruption threshold earns `precool_credited` and suppresses `precool_target_missed`. This credits effective cooling even when the strict 17°C target was not reached or most of the earlier drop occurred before the chart window. **Implementation:** `MorningAnalysisService._overnight_temperature_rows` now calls `bedroom_overnight.night_window(subject_date - 1, timezone)` with the same inclusive-start/exclusive-end bounds as `/bedroom`; `_thermal_review(..., sleep=...)` partitions those rows at Garmin's `sleep_start_utc`/`sleep_end_utc`, uses only asleep rows for the indoor peak/low/last and thermal-disruption flags, and falls back to the full shared night window if sleep times are absent/invalid. The prompt and `outputRules` require the read to treat the pre-cool fields separately and explicitly credit `precool_credited`; `PROMPT_VERSION` → `morning-analysis-v12-2026-07-12`. **Boundaries:** backend-only, **no migration**, no frontend/shared change; thermal stays advisory/environmental and does not feed `_morning_verdict`, so Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, and Red-never-VO2 are untouched. **Verification (local, green):** backend pytest **607 passed / 200 skipped**; new pure cases prove a 24.05°C pre-bed spike cannot become the sleep peak (20.2°C), the 18.64°C pre-cool is surfaced/credited without a miss, missing-sleep fallback, and shared chart/morning date-window semantics; backend ruff + format-check clean; touched-file mypy clean. 168. **Batch 95 gives Home a first-class pre-brief state so the "Say good morning" hero, the Next-action strip, and Sleep's check-in prompt all agree before today's brief exists.** Implemented on `feat/batch-95-pre-checkin-home` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 95; surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-12 walkthrough). **Why:** since Batch 85 the hero (`GoodMorningCta`) already shows "Say good morning" whenever `morningAnalysis` is null, but the Next-action strip's morning ladder (`homeActions.ts`) required `morningAnalysis != null` for its first rung and fell through everything else to "You're all set" — contradicting the hero directly beneath it. Separately, `rest_day`'s phase-primary section is `lastNight`, so a pre-brief rest morning auto-expanded the raw sleep comparison table before any coached read existed. **Kickoff decision (95.1/95.2 — "new primary override vs. a guard in the existing primary selection"): a guard in the existing selection, not a new override mechanism.** `nextAction`'s existing action-override pattern (`actionSection(action) ?? primarySection(...)`) already covers 95.1 for free — a new `say-good-morning` rung (first check inside `if (isMorning)`, firing on `morningAnalysis == null`) slots into that pattern with no structural change. 95.2 only needed a narrow guard at the `primary` computation in `DashboardPage.tsx` (`analysis == null && phase === 'rest_day' ? 'today' : primarySection(...)`) rather than teaching `primarySection` about brief-state, since `pre_training`'s default is already `today` and only `rest_day` was wrong. **Implementation:** (1) `homeActions.ts` — `nextAction`'s morning ladder gains a `say-good-morning` rung (`to: '/check-in'`) ahead of the sleep-review rung, firing whenever no brief exists; outside the morning phase the ladder is unchanged (the hero still shows regardless of phase, but the day/evening ladders keep their own priorities). (2) `DashboardPage.tsx` — the `primary` section computation guards `rest_day` pre-brief to `today`, so `lastNight` renders collapsed to its one-line summary instead of auto-expanding. (3) `SleepPage.tsx` — reuses `GoodMorningCta` at the top of the page when `manualEntry == null` (pt 4), linking through the same `/check-in` route as Home and the page's existing footer check-in card. **Boundaries:** frontend-only, no API/shared-schema/migration change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Verification (local, green):** targeted web vitest **69 passed** (`homeActions.test.ts`, `DashboardPage.test.tsx`, `SleepPage.test.tsx`, incl. new coverage for the pre-brief rung's precedence over a pending eased ride, the rest-day lastNight collapse, and Sleep's check-in CTA presence/absence), full web vitest **222 passed**, `tsc` clean, web lint clean aside from the pre-existing 6 Fast Refresh warnings + 1 pre-existing `tailwind.config.ts` require-import error (untouched by this batch), web production build clean under Node 20. Tier 🟢 Mid. **Shipped** (PR #118, squash `7e9770c`): both CI waves passed all 7 jobs in push and PR-context plus a Vercel preview; squash-merged to `main` as `7e9770c9ffa18d8e3f4df41ae7be2a10823b684c`. **Production verified on the merge SHA:** Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both `7e9770c`, web `/` returned 200, and unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returned 401 direct and via Vercel. 169. **Batch 96 gives Home a first-class unviewed-brief state, and stops offering to regenerate a brief that already exists.** Implemented on `feat/batch-96-brief-lifecycle-cta` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, Batch 96; second of the 2026-07-12 walkthrough's Batches 95-102 sequence, builds on Batch 95's brief-state model). **Why:** once today's brief lands it competed for attention with `TodayActions`' thermal/plan nudges (e.g. "Pre-cool the bedroom") rather than leading, and `/check-in`'s primary button kept reading "Get today's brief" even after a brief existed, so tapping it again silently regenerated the read instead of just opening it (pt 8, pt 9). **Implementation:** a new per-day client flag (`apps/web/src/lib/briefReview.ts`, `hasReviewedBrief`/`markBriefReviewed`) mirrors Batch 60's `sleepReview.ts` pattern exactly — keyed by subject date, set when `MorningBriefPage` mounts with a loaded analysis, degrading safely to "not reviewed" on storage failure. `DashboardPage.tsx` renders a new `UnviewedBriefCta` immediately above `TodayActions` whenever `analysis != null && !hasReviewedBrief(subjectDate)`, so the unread brief outranks every action card including the thermal nudge inside it;
