170. **Batch 97 makes the morning brief generate passively after check-in: the save returns immediately, the server finishes the brief off-request, and the user is pulled back by a ready notification while the page still has an in-app fallback.** Implemented on `main` from Batch 97 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-12 walkthrough). **Why:** Batch 85 had already moved morning generation onto the check-in, but it still held the request open behind "Reading your morning…", making the user wait on the LLM in place. The walkthrough's desired behaviour was closer to Domino's-tracker ergonomics: save, leave, get notified when the read is ready. **Kickoff decision (97.4): use an in-process FastAPI `BackgroundTasks` job, not a new job row or scheduler queue, and use timed staged progress on the client rather than fake backend progress.** The existing seam was already narrow and durable: `DailyLoopService.upsert_manual_entry(...)` commits the check-in, `ExecutableCoachingService.regenerate_after_morning_checkin(...)` already encapsulates the force-regenerate + downgrade-only / never-touch-an-approved-ride guardrails, and `NudgeAlertService` already owns one-per-day push idempotency. A new queue table or polling API would add schema/surface area for a private single-user app without changing the real reliability profile, while "real progress" would be synthetic because the backend has no stage-level job telemetry. **Implementation:** `PUT /api/v1/daily-loop/{date}/manual-entry` now queues `_generate_brief_after_checkin(...)` only for today's local date; that helper opens its own `AsyncSessionLocal`, reloads the active profile, runs the existing regeneration service with `commit=False`, then sends a new one-per-day `brief-ready-{date}` push via `NudgeAlertService.push_brief_ready(...)` before one final commit. The new push deep-links to `/brief` (same transport/idempotency pattern as the verdict/workout pushes) and reuses the brief's first reason as the one-line body when available. On the web, `CheckInPage.tsx` keeps the same write endpoint and daily-loop query but swaps the blocking spinner for an immediate acknowledgement + a three-stage waiting card ("Syncing your overnight data" → "Reading your morning" → "Writing your brief"), with the stages driven by local time windows, not backend job state. **Fallback decision:** when push is denied, missed, or delayed, the page itself polls the normal daily-loop snapshot and offers a manual refresh button — no new API shape, no migration. **Known dependency carried forward:** the ready push now includes `data.url="/brief"`, but focused-client navigation on iOS PWA still needs Batch **99**; until then the cold-start deep-link works and the in-app fallback covers a missed in-place route jump. **Boundaries:** no migration; no verdict logic change; #133, #135, and Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Verification (local, green):** backend pytest **22 passed / 13 skipped** (`test_nudge_alerts.py`, `test_daily_loop.py`), backend `ruff check` clean; web `CheckInPage.test.tsx` **8 passed**; web `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint clean on touched files aside from 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings in unrelated shared files. **Shipped:** implementation commit `0310cd6ae40c142e301b6c6af8581e48f3ae05ee` was pushed to `main`; GitHub Actions run `29210486906` then passed all 7 jobs; production verification on that SHA showed Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both serving `0310cd6`, web `/check-in` + `/brief` returning 200, and unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returning 401 via Vercel. The real ready-push-on-device proof remains deferred to live use, and Batch 99 is the focused-client iOS deep-link follow-on. Tier 🟢 Mid.

171. **Batch 98 treats an explicit holiday or a non-empty all-skipped plan as a rest day, while keeping recovery colour and live-workout truth separate.** Implemented on `feat/batch-98-rest-day-verdict` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-12 walkthrough). **Why:** the morning packet had the skipped workout row but no holiday/rest-day concept, and `_plan_adjustments` checked only whether any row existed, so a Green holiday morning could say "Proceed with the planned workout" for an endurance ride already paused by Batch 15. **Kickoff decision:** reuse Batch 90.2's `HolidayPauseService.get_windows(...)` loader **and** derive rest when the day's non-empty active-row set is entirely `status='skipped'`. The holiday signal protects against a stale/unversioned plan row; the all-skipped signal protects against a missing or historical window. An empty plan remains unknown/conservative rather than being silently declared intentional rest. **Implementation:** the morning packet gains `restDay {isRestDay, reason, insideHolidayWindow, allPlannedWorkoutsSkipped, holidayWindows}`; `_morning_verdict` preserves the existing Green/Amber/Red recovery classification but adds `dayType='rest'`, excludes skipped/completed work from live VO2, and emits one rest-day adjustment. Rest days bypass swap-first, eased-ride Today actions, hard-prior-day easing copy, and weekly-mix shortfall/re-patch prose. The prompt bans treating skipped/holiday sessions as live and `PROMPT_VERSION` moves to `morning-analysis-v13-2026-07-12`. **Boundaries:** no migration, frontend/shared change, or change to #133/#135/Red-never-VO2; the colour remains a recovery read, not permission to train. **Verification:** targeted morning/weekly-mix pytest 39 passed / 9 local DB skips; Ruff check + format and touched-service mypy clean. The first two CI runs exposed test-fixture-only profile-order and seeded-version collisions; after correction, both final CI waves passed all seven jobs with 813/813 backend tests plus the Vercel preview. **Shipped:** PR #120 squash-merged as `a0e133dc5b7b7ccc15b7f483da8e47f7911fcf03`; Railway + Vercel same-origin health matched the merge SHA, web `/` + `/brief` returned 200, and unauthenticated daily-loop returned 401 direct/proxied. The genuine rest/holiday wording eyeball remains live-use verification. Tier 🔴 High.

172. **Batch 99 routes warm notification taps through the app shell, not `WindowClient.navigate()`: the service worker posts a normalized same-origin URL to the focused client, the SPA listens on `navigator.serviceWorker.message` and calls `react-router` navigation, and cold-start taps still use `openWindow(...)`.** Implemented on `feat/batch-99-ios-notification-deeplink` (batch row `docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-12 walkthrough). **Why:** the walkthrough confirmed the exact iOS PWA failure mode: tapping the good-morning push while the app was already open just resurfaced the last-viewed screen. `sw.ts` focused an existing `WindowClient` and called `client.navigate(url)`, but on iOS PWAs that call is a no-op, so the route never changed. **Decision:** keep the fix entirely inside the existing frontend + push-payload seam. A focused client should receive a typed `postMessage` with the target URL and let the already-mounted SPA router own the in-app transition; `clients.openWindow(url)` remains the cold-start fallback when no window is open. URLs are normalized to same-origin path/query/hash before either path, and unrelated service-worker messages are ignored. *Why:* this is the narrow additive fix the batch asked for; it solves the focused-client iOS path without inventing a second notification endpoint, changing payload shape, or relying on browser-specific `navigate()` behavior. **Implementation:** new shared web helper `apps/web/src/lib/pushNavigation.ts` centralizes URL normalization, typed message construction, and the focused-client-vs-cold-start branching; `apps/web/src/sw.ts` now delegates `notificationclick` to that helper instead of calling `WindowClient.navigate(...)`; new app-shell `PushNavigationController` listens for service-worker `message` events inside `BrowserRouter` and routes them with `useNavigate`. Existing payload builders already met the batch's deep-link requirement and remain unchanged: good-morning targets `/check-in`, brief-ready targets `/brief`, and verdict push keeps `/`. **Boundaries:** frontend + push-payload only; **no migration**, no backend endpoint change, no verdict / #133 / #135 / Red-never-VO2 change. **Verification (local, green):** backend `test_nudge_alerts.py` **22 passed / 3 skipped** confirms payload `data.url`; new web regression `pushNavigation.test.tsx` **5 passed** covers same-origin normalization, focused-client `postMessage`, cold-start `openWindow`, SPA routing on message, and ignoring unrelated messages; web `tsc --noEmit` and production build both pass. Tier 🟢 Mid.

173. **Batch 100 promotes the fan surface from one anonymous bedroom-fan blob to a stable per-fan list keyed by Dreo identity, with the overnight auto-target staying pinned separately.** Implemented on `main` from Batch 100 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-12 walkthrough). **Kickoff decisions:** (a) **identity = Dreo's own serial + device label/model, not a new user-labelled table or profile JSON.** The app now needs to show and target more than one controllable fan, but adding a rename layer would be a brand-new state model for a private single-user app; Dreo already gives a stable serial and human label, so reuse it directly. (b) **The overnight auto-target remains the configured `DREO_DEVICE_SN` (or the first controllable fan when unset), even if a manual command temporarily targets another fan.** Manual control must not silently move the scheduler's bedroom-fan ownership. (c) **"Next on" is a concrete local clock time (`21:30`), not a vague "until tonight".** That answers Mark's walkthrough question directly and falls straight out of the existing overnight window. (d) **This batch intentionally supersedes Decision #97's "daily-loop fan read stays cloud-free" on this one surface.** Multi-fan identity, oscillation, and per-fan targeting are not available from the old computed-intent-only blob; the daily-loop fan list now does a best-effort live Dreo inventory/state read, then merges the existing overnight intent onto the auto-target fan and falls back to the old single-fan synthetic payload if Dreo is unavailable. **Why:** once Mark has multiple fans, a single `thermalState.fan` object cannot tell him which device is which or safely target commands. Using Dreo's own identity keeps the change additive and migration-free, while a best-effort live read is the smallest way to surface per-fan mode/speed/oscillation honestly.**

174. **Batch 101 gives the room/fan surface its own primary `Climate` tab, while Sleep keeps only the sleep-context summary and the handoff link into it.** Implemented on the current branch from Batch 101 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-12 walkthrough). **Kickoff decisions:** (a) **Name the tab `Climate`, not `Environment`.** The bottom bar needs a short, plain word; `Climate` is clearer in one glance for Mark than the broader `Environment`, and it matches what the surface actually owns: room temperature, fan control, and overnight weather context. (b) **Make it a top-level tab, not a `More` destination.** The multi-fan surface is now a recurring nightly control surface, not an occasional settings page, so burying it under `More` would hide a real day-to-day action area. Four primary tabs plus `More` stays legible on the phone while keeping Sleep focused on the sleep narrative. (c) **Keep Sleep as the hybrid summary surface.** The full `BedroomBody` controls move to the new `/environment` route, but Sleep's Tonight view keeps a concise thermal stats card plus one clear next action (`Open Climate`) so the bedtime story is still in one place. (d) **Retire `/bedroom` to the new tab, not back to Sleep.** Once Climate owns the live room/fan surface, the legacy bedroom route should land on the new home for that functionality. **Why:** Batch 100 made the climate surface materially larger by introducing multiple real fans and richer telemetry; giving it its own primary home avoids overloading Sleep without stripping out the sleep-relevant thermal context. This keeps the UI additive, frontend-only, and easy to understand.

Pre-check-in `/sleep` therefore shows `GoodMorningCta`, the collapsed `SleepDateCalendar`, and a locked-today card with the current-date check-in CTA; selecting a past date loads that stored sleep snapshot plus a new in-place whole-day summary card (verdict badge/reason + planned sessions) while the overnight chart still follows the selected night. `SleepDateCalendar.tsx` now defaults collapsed behind a Show/Hide toggle. **Boundaries:** frontend-only; no API/shared-schema/migration change; no change to Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2, or the Batch 103 current-day gate itself. **Verification (local, green):** targeted web vitest **10 passed** (`SleepPage.test.tsx`, including the new pre-check-in browse regression and whole-day historical view), web `tsc --noEmit` clean, web lint clean aside from the 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings in unrelated files, and web production build clean. 182. **Batch 109 completes Batch 105's holiday-awareness on the frontend by keeping the evening/bedroom surfaces *dormant*, not hidden, and by extending the existing holiday seam into `/api/v1/daily-loop` rather than inventing a second away-state model.** Implemented on `feat/batch-109-holiday-home-sleep` from Batch 109 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough). **Kickoff decisions:** (a) **Choose dormant placeholders over full hide.** Batch 105 already proved that an active holiday means "Mark is away", so the frontend should stop acting as if tonight's room and wind-down are live; but making the sections vanish would make Home/Sleep look inconsistent with the rest of the app's object-permanence direction. Dormant cards keep the information architecture intact while honestly saying the system is paused until he is back. (b) **Use the existing active holiday window as the one away flag.** This matches Batch 105's private-app rule: the app already has an explicit, user-controlled holiday window and that is sufficient truth for away-ness; no parallel boolean or settings model is needed. (c) **Carry only the minimal frontend truth on the daily-loop payload:** `holiday { isActive, activeWindow { startDate, endDate } }`. The frontend needs to know whether the holiday is active and when the away state ends so it can render the dormant copy; it does not need the full holiday-history envelope. **Implementation:** `DailyLoopService` now loads `HolidayPauseService.get_active_window_for_date(...)` for the subject date and the router serializes that into the new daily-loop `holiday` object; Home's `tonight` and `bedroom` sections swap from live `SleepPrepBody` / `BedroomBody` content to quiet away-state placeholders with a Holiday handoff and resume date when `holiday.isActive`; Sleep's Tonight tab collapses to one holiday-away card instead of rendering the prep + climate cards; and the Home `nextAction(...)` ladder suppresses the evening `protect-sleep` CTA during an active holiday so the action strip cannot contradict the dormant surfaces. **Boundaries:** no migration; no scheduler/fan/verdict/threshold change; the existing backend holiday behavior from Batch 105 stays the source of truth. **Verification (local):** a focused daily-loop API test covers the new holiday payload, shared-schema tests parse both active and inactive shapes, and web tests cover Home/Sleep dormant holiday rendering plus the suppressed protect-sleep action. Tier 🟢 Mid.

183. **Batch 110 de-dups the brief flow by replacing UI in place rather than adding new state, and by trusting Batch 96's Home surfacing instead of duplicating the brief on Check-in.** Implemented on `feat/batch-110-brief-flow-dedup` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough). **Kickoff decisions:** (a) **In-place progress, not a second card.** The staged generation progress (`BRIEF_STAGES`) already existed from Batch 97; the only change needed was moving it to render where the button/entry area was, instead of alongside it, so the check-in doesn't show two competing "what's happening" surfaces at once. (b) **Drop the inline brief render entirely, don't gate it further.** Once Batch 96 shipped `UnviewedBriefCta` on Home, the Check-in page's own `VerdictHero` + Markdown render became a second place the same brief showed up; the simplest fix is deleting it and leaving Check-in's job as "save, then hand off to `/brief`" via the existing View brief button. (c) **On Home, drop the duplicated date rather than rewrite the verdict copy.** The greeting lockup's date (`friendlyDate(daily.subjectDate)`) was a literal duplicate of `VerdictHero`'s/`GoodMorningCta`'s own `dateLabel` immediately below; `personalStatusLine`'s prose framing ("You're good to go this morning") and `VerdictHero`'s badge ("Good to go") are different enough in register (personal narration vs. status label) that rewriting the greeting risked losing tone for no real de-dup gain, so only the redundant date was removed. **Boundaries:** frontend-only, no API/shared-schema/migration change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Verification (local, green):** full web vitest **243 passed**, `tsc --noEmit` clean, web lint clean aside from the 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings in unrelated files, web production build clean. 184. **Batch 111 stays on-device for the read-aloud voice — it improves `SpeechSynthesis` voice *selection*, not a hosted TTS swap — and explicitly excludes remote-service voices to hold the line Decision #179 drew.** Implemented on `feat/batch-111-natural-voice` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough). **Kickoff decision (111.2): on-device over hosted.** #179 chose the browser's `SpeechSynthesis` API specifically to avoid sending the health-data brief text to a third party; better voice quality alone doesn't outweigh that, so this batch stays inside the same API and fixes the actual complaint (the default voice sounds robotic) by picking a better voice, not a better backend. **The sharper finding:** some `SpeechSynthesisVoice` entries reported by `getVoices()` — e.g. Chrome's default "Google UK English" voices — are not actually on-device; `voice.localService === false` for them because the audio is synthesized on Google's servers, meaning naively picking "the best-sounding voice by name" could silently reintroduce the exact privacy leak #179 avoided. **Implementation:** new pure `selectBestVoice(voices, targetLang)` (`apps/web/src/lib/speechVoice.ts`) filters to `localService === true` only, scores by locale match (exact `lang` match beats same-language-different-region beats no match) then a small bonus for quality-signal names (`natural`/`neural`/`premium`/`enhanced`), and returns `null` when nothing local matches — in which case `BriefListenControls` leaves `utterance.voice` unset and the platform's own default takes over, exactly as it did before this batch. `BriefListenControls` now loads `speechSynthesis.getVoices()` (with the async `onvoiceschanged` load handled) and applies the selected voice per-utterance. **Boundaries:** frontend-only; no API/shared-schema/migration change; no hosted TTS integration; #179's privacy posture unchanged; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Verification (local, green):** full web vitest **249 passed** (incl. new `speechVoice.test.ts` and a `MorningBriefPage.test.tsx` case proving a remote "Natural"-named voice loses to a plainer local one), `tsc --noEmit` clean, web lint clean aside from the 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings in unrelated files, web production build clean. Tier 🟢 Mid.

186. **Batch 113 suppresses the morning brief's thermal/environment review and pre-cool action only inside an active holiday window (`restDay.insideHolidayWindow`), not for every rest day, and fixes the pre-cool link to `/environment`.** Implemented on `feat/batch-113-holiday-thermal-suppression` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough). **Kickoff decision (113.4): holiday-window-only, not any rest day.** `restDay.isRestDay` also covers an all-skipped local rest day where Mark is still sleeping at home — the bedroom is genuinely occupied and the thermal read stays relevant there; only an active holiday window means the room isn't being slept in, so that's the narrower, already-named `insideHolidayWindow` flag the batch row itself specified. **Implementation:** `assemble_context_packet` now derives `thermal_review_for_output = None if rest_day["insideHolidayWindow"] else thermal_review`, used for both `environment.thermalReview` (null on holiday) and the `build_today_actions(...)` call (so `_thermal_action` sees no flags and never emits the "Pre-cool the bedroom" action); the `include_thermal_environment_review` output rule is filtered out of `prompt.outputRules` under the same condition, and `SYSTEM_PROMPT` gains a line telling the model not to fabricate a thermal review when the field is null. `_thermal_action`'s `href` moves from the stale `/sleep` to `/environment` unconditionally (post-Batch-101 route), independent of the holiday gate. 188. **Batch 115 folds the personable status line into `VerdictHero`'s own `line` prop instead of dropping it, and suppresses the "You're all set" strip only when the day itself already says nothing's planned (`dayState.isRest || holiday.isActive`), not on every all-clear.** Implemented on `feat/batch-115-home-dedup` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough, Issues 4 and 5). **Kickoff decision (115.1): fold, don't drop.** `personalStatusLine(verdict, name)` carries a personal, named greeting (`"Good morning, Mark. You're good to go this morning."`) that `VerdictHero`'s own generic `line` (`"Train as planned today."`) doesn't; dropping the paragraph outright would have lost that personal register entirely (Batch 110's Decision #183 explicitly declined to touch it for the same reason). Passing `personalStatusLine(...)` into `VerdictHero`'s existing `line` prop keeps the personal wording but renders it exactly once, inside the hero, instead of twice — once above it restating the verdict, once inside the hero's own badge. The plain `greeting` line (no verdict restated) still renders above the pre-verdict CTAs (`GoodMorningCta`/`BriefGeneratingCta`), since neither of those carries a greeting of its own. **Kickoff decision (115.2): gate the suppression on the day, not on the all-set state generally.** The existing all-clear `NextActionStrip` test (Batch 50) uses a normal workout day, where "You're all set" is the *only* place that says nothing's pending — suppressing it unconditionally would leave a genuinely all-clear cycling day with no next-step signal at all. The redundancy the walkthrough actually flagged is specific to rest/holiday days, where the Today card's own summary (`"Rest is the plan today."` or the holiday-dormant state) already conveys it; `dayState.isRest || holiday.isActive` is the existing, already-computed signal for exactly that case, so no new day-type field was added. **Boundaries:** frontend-only, no API/shared-schema/migration change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Verification (local, green):** targeted web vitest **45 passed** (`DashboardPage.test.tsx`, 3 new), full web vitest **254 passed**, `tsc --noEmit` clean, web lint clean aside from the 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings in unrelated files, web production build clean. **CI:** both branch-push and PR-context waves passed all 7 jobs plus the Vercel preview. **Production on merge SHA `b97e90b9dc286ff932ab71c33c7cb8b744cbc958`:** Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both served that SHA; web `/` returned `200`; unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returned `401` both direct and via Vercel. 189. **Batch 116 escalates the read-aloud voice to a hosted/neural option via OpenAI's TTS API, but only behind an explicit per-user opt-in that defaults off, with the on-device voice (Batch 111) as the automatic fallback — re-opening, not overturning, #179/#184's on-device-first stance.** Implemented on `feat/batch-116-hosted-tts` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough). **Kickoff decision (116.2, decided with Craig at `/batch-start`): consent-gated hosted TTS, on-device fallback.** #179 chose the browser's `SpeechSynthesis` API specifically to keep brief text off third-party servers; #184 held that line while improving on-device voice selection. A hosted/neural voice is a real quality upgrade the on-device path can't match, so rather than reversing #179 for everyone, the tradeoff is made explicit and per-user: `Profile.hosted_tts_consent` (migration `016`, default `false`) must be switched on in Settings before any brief text is ever sent off-device, and any hosted-path failure (stale consent, unconfigured key, network) falls back to on-device speech rather than failing silently. **Engine decision (also at `/batch-start`): OpenAI TTS over a self-hosted model (e.g. Piper) or ElevenLabs.** A self-hosted neural model would have avoided the third-party-data question entirely, but at meaningfully more build/ops cost (container, cold-start/latency tuning on Railway) for a Mid-tier batch; OpenAI's hosted API was chosen as the pragmatic middle ground over ElevenLabs (comparable third-party exposure, added subscription cost) given the consent gate already makes the tradeoff explicit either way. **Implementation:** new `openai_api_key`/`openai_tts_model`/`openai_tts_voice` settings (`config.py`, unvalidated in prod since the feature is optional); `services/openai_tts.py` mirrors the existing `anthropic_text.py` httpx boundary pattern; `routers/tts.py` exposes `PUT /api/v1/tts/consent` (toggles the profile flag, mirrors `fan.py`'s `PUT /auto`) and `POST /api/v1/tts/synthesize` (403 if consent is off, 503 if no key configured, 6000-char cap, `audio/mpeg` response) — consent is re-checked server-side on every synthesize call, not just remembered client-side. Synthesized audio is cached **in-process only** (a small `OrderedDict` LRU, never persisted to disk/DB), consistent with #179's "read aloud, keep nothing" precedent — Batch 116.3's "caching" requirement is satisfied without a new storage decision. `daily-loop`'s payload gains `hostedTtsConsent: bool` so the frontend knows the current setting without a separate profile fetch (mirrors how `holiday` was threaded in Batch 109). `BriefListenControls.tsx` tries the hosted path first when `hostedTtsConsent` is true (`apiFetchBlob` → `HTMLAudioElement`), and falls back to the existing on-device `SpeechSynthesis` flow on any failure; a new Settings "Voice" section (`SettingsPage.tsx`) carries the off-by-default consent toggle with explicit copy about what turning it on does. **Boundaries:** the on-device path (#179/#184) is completely unchanged and remains the default; no scheduler/verdict/threshold change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Verification (local, green):** backend pytest **618 passed** (210 skipped, DB-backed; 3 new non-DB `openai_tts` tests plus 6 new DB-backed `tts` router tests), `ruff check` clean, `mypy src` clean on all 107 source files; web vitest **259 passed, 1 pre-existing unrelated `WeekAheadPage.test.tsx` timeout** (documented flake, Batches 114/115), including new `BriefListenControls.test.tsx` (4) and `SettingsPage.test.tsx` (2); shared-package `schemas.test.ts` **16 passed**; `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint clean aside from the 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings in unrelated files; web production build clean under Node 20. Tier 🟢 Mid.

190. **Batch 116's hosted-voice engine is swapped from OpenAI's TTS API to a self-hosted Piper model, superseding the engine half of #189 — the consent-gated, on-device-fallback design from #189 is unchanged.** Implemented on `feat/batch-116-piper-tts` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, requested by Craig directly in chat immediately after #189/PR #137 shipped). **Why:** Craig asked what the OpenAI key would cost and, on hearing it wasn't free, asked for a free alternative — self-hosted Piper was the option already on the table at the original `/batch-start` kickoff (offered alongside OpenAI and ElevenLabs) but not chosen then because of its higher build/ops cost; that tradeoff reads differently now that the alternative's actual cost is the deciding factor, not just build effort. Piper also happens to fully remove the third-party-data question #189's consent gate was built to manage — brief text now never leaves our own Railway infra even when a user opts in — though the consent toggle is kept as-is rather than removed, since hosted synthesis still costs more server CPU per use than the free on-device path. **Not a silent reversal:** #189's kickoff decisions (consent-gated, off by default, automatic on-device fallback on any failure) stand; only the *engine* behind `POST /api/v1/tts/synthesize` changes. **Implementation:** `services/piper_tts.py` replaces `services/openai_tts.py`, shelling out to the `piper` console script (from the `piper-tts` pip package) via `asyncio.to_thread` rather than using Piper's in-process Python API — the CLI surface is more stable across Piper releases. A British voice model (`en_GB-alan-medium`, .onnx + .onnx.json) is baked into the Docker image at build time from the public `rhasspy/piper-voices` Hugging Face repo, so a synthesize call never needs an outbound download at runtime. `config.py`'s `openai_api_key`/`openai_tts_model`/`openai_tts_voice` are replaced by `piper_voice_model_path`/`piper_voice_config_path`; the router's "is the hosted voice configured" check moves from "is an API key set" to "does the voice model file exist on disk", and the synthesize response's `Content-Type` moves from `audio/mpeg` to `audio/wav` (Piper's native output format). The in-process-only audio cache, the 403/503/400 error shape, the `hostedTtsConsent` daily-loop field, and `BriefListenControls.tsx`'s hosted-then-fallback flow are all unchanged. Settings copy no longer says "via OpenAI" / "sends off-device", now "generated on our own server (no third party)". **Known unknowns (cannot be verified in the agent sandbox — no internet access to install `piper-tts`, download a voice model, or run a container):** the exact Piper CLI flag surface and the voice-model download URL are believed correct from the public Piper/`piper-voices` project conventions but unverified end-to-end; first production deploy needs a Railway build-log check (does the image build, does the model download succeed) and a real synthesize call to confirm audio quality and that `PIPER_TIMEOUT_SECONDS = 45` is enough headroom for a full brief-length text on Railway's shared CPU. **Boundaries:** the on-device default path (#179/#184) and the consent-gate design (#189) are unchanged; no scheduler/verdict/threshold change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Verification (local, green):** backend pytest 619 passed (210 skipped DB-backed; new `test_piper_tts.py` mocks `subprocess.run`, `test_tts.py` updated to point at a real-vs-missing temp model file instead of an API key), `ruff check`/`mypy src` clean; web vitest 256/260 passed locally under parallel load (4 timeouts — `DashboardPage`/`SleepPage` both pass in isolation, confirming a load flake unrelated to this change; 2× `WeekAheadPage` is the same pre-existing flake documented in Batches 114/115/116), `tsc --noEmit` clean, web lint clean (6 pre-existing unrelated warnings), web production build clean under Node 20. Tier 🟢 Mid.

191. **Batch 117's day-step chevrons keep only the `maxDate` upper bound; no lower bound was added, matching the existing month grid's own behavior.** Implemented on `feat/batch-117-sleep-calendar-day-step` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, Issue 9, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough). **Why:** the batch row said "respecting max/earliest bounds", but `SleepDateCalendar` has never had an earliest-date concept — the month grid only ever disables days *after* `maxDate` (`isAfter(day, maxDateObj)`), with no floor — and no earliest-date field exists anywhere else in the frontend (checked before implementing). Inventing a lower bound for the chevrons that the month grid itself doesn't enforce would have made the two navigation paths inconsistent for no product reason, so the day-step chevrons mirror the grid's existing single-bound behavior (`nextDayDisabled = !isAfter(maxDateObj, selectedDateObj)`) rather than adding a new one. **Kickoff decision (repurposing the header chevrons):** the header prev/next controls previously paged `displayMonth` by month; day-stepping needed that slot, so month-to-month paging moved to a new small control pair placed inline with the `MMMM yyyy` label inside the expanded grid section — the grid's own "jump to any date" capability (the batch's explicit requirement) is unchanged, it just navigates via a different pair of buttons now. **Implementation:** `SleepDateCalendar.tsx`'s header chevrons call `onSelectDate(format(subDays/addDays(selectedDateObj, 1), 'yyyy-MM-dd'))` directly rather than touching `displayMonth` state; the existing `useEffect` that resyncs `displayMonth` to `selectedDate` means the grid (when expanded) follows the day-stepped date into whatever month it lands in, with no separate wiring needed. **Boundaries:** frontend-only, no API/shared-schema/migration change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Verification (local, green):** 4 new `SleepDateCalendar.test.tsx` cases (day-step both directions, `maxDate` disabling "Next day" and no-op on click, month-grid date selection still working after paging months), full web vitest 264 passed, `tsc --noEmit` clean, web lint clean, web production build clean under Node 20. **CI:** both branch-push and PR-context waves passed all 8 checks (7 jobs + Vercel) each. Tier 🟢 Mid.

192. **Batch 118's one-tap "what's off" vocabulary is kind-scoped multi-select reason-tag chips, not always-visible dimension tags or a cautious↔aggressive slider.** Implemented on `feat/batch-118-brief-feedback-reasons` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, Issue 13, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough). **Kickoff decision (118.2, decided with Craig at `/batch-start`):** three vocabularies were on the table — always-visible dimension tags, a single too-cautious/too-aggressive slider, or reason chips revealed on a negative tap. The slider only fits the `suggestion` axis (a `summary` read isn't cautious or aggressive, it's right or wrong about a specific fact), so it can't cover both of `FeedbackControl`'s existing kinds. Always-visible tags add visual weight to every brief for a signal only useful on the minority of negative taps. Reason chips revealed alongside the existing correction box on a negative tap — the same reveal trigger `showCorrection`/`isNegative` already use — extend the existing interaction instead of adding a second one, and can be kind-scoped like the ratings already are. **Vocabulary:** `summary` gets `sleep_read` / `load_read` / `thermal_read` / `plan_mismatch` / `other`; `suggestion` gets `too_cautious` / `too_aggressive` / `bad_timing` / `not_practical` / `other`. Multi-select (an off read can be wrong in more than one way at once), each tap saves immediately via the same upsert the rating uses — no separate "save reasons" step. **Implementation:** `feedback.reason_tags` (migration `017`, JSONB array, default `[]`) alongside the existing `correction_text`; `FeedbackService._validate` now also rejects a reason tag that doesn't belong to the given kind (422, same shape as the existing rating/kind check); `recent_corrections` now surfaces a row that has reason tags but no free text too (`correction_text IS NOT NULL OR jsonb_array_length(reason_tags) > 0`), and `RecentCorrection.to_packet()` carries `reasonTags` into the morning packet the model reads (Decision #137's fed-forward correction is now text-and/or-tags, not text-only). Shared `feedbackReasonTagSchema`/`feedbackInputSchema` validate the same kind-scoping client-side. `FeedbackControl.tsx` renders the reason chips in the same reveal block as the correction textarea; switching to a positive rating clears any tags picked under an abandoned negative tap. **Boundaries:** no change to the existing rating axis, the correction free-text flow, Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, or Red-never-VO2; reason tags are additive context for the next read, same non-overriding footing as free-text corrections (#137). **Verification (local, green):** backend pytest 623 passed (213 skipped, DB-backed; 4 new `test_feedback.py` cases — kind-scoped save, cross-kind rejection, reason-tags-only row feeding forward), `ruff check`/`mypy src` clean; shared `schemas.test.ts` 19 passed (3 new); web vitest — targeted `FeedbackControl.test.tsx` 7 passed (3 new), full suite 265/266 passed (1 `WeekAheadPage.test.tsx` timeout under full-suite load, confirmed a pre-existing flake — passes 12/12 in isolation, same flake documented in Batches 114–116); `tsc --noEmit` clean; web lint clean aside from the 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings in unrelated files; web production build clean under Node 20. **CI:** both branch-push and PR-context waves passed all 8 checks (7 jobs + Vercel) each, including the DB-backed pytest job against real Postgres. **Production on merge SHA `e208509616ad8bf1bb500254801d3268a9744d5d`:** Railway logs confirmed the `016 -> 017` Alembic migration ran cleanly on container start; Railway + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` both served that SHA; web `/` returned `200`; unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` returned `401` both direct and via Vercel. Tier 🟢 Mid.

193. **Batch 116's Piper voice moves from `medium` to `low` quality, and from `en_GB-alan` to `en_GB-southern_english_female`, after a real production 502 confirmed `medium` synthesis on Railway's CPU exceeded the 45s timeout for a full brief.** Implemented on `fix/batch-116-piper-low-voice` (requested by Craig after trying the hosted voice and hearing nothing — `railway logs --http` showed `POST /api/v1/tts/synthesize 502 46427ms`, i.e. Piper hit the internal timeout, not a bug in the on-device fallback logic). **Why `low` over other fixes:** raising the timeout further just makes the wait longer without addressing that Piper's `medium` tier is too slow for Railway's shared CPU on brief-length text; truncating the synthesized text would silently change what "Listen" reads. `low` quality trades some audio fidelity for synthesis fast enough to stay interactive, which is the actual constraint. **Voice/gender change is incidental, not a choice:** `en_GB-alan-low` is not confirmed to exist in the `rhasspy/piper-voices` catalog (only `alan-medium` was verified, by the previous build succeeding); `en_GB-southern_english_female-low` is the low-quality British voice believed most likely to exist from the catalog's public structure, so the fallback voice differs by gender from the original `medium` pick as a side effect of picking a name confidently believed to exist over a guessed one. `PIPER_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` also raised 45→60s as additional headroom, since actual `low`-tier synthesis speed on Railway's CPU is still unverified ahead of a real deploy. **Boundaries:** no change to the consent-gate design (#189) or the engine choice (#190) — only the specific voice model and timeout constant. **Verification (local, green):** backend pytest 619 passed (213 skipped DB-backed), `ruff check`/`mypy src` clean; no frontend files touched, so the web suite was not re-run. **Unverified until the real Railway build:** whether `en_GB-southern_english_female-low` actually exists at the guessed Hugging Face path, and whether `low`-tier synthesis now completes within 60s for a full brief on Railway's CPU — both need a live build-log + synthesize check, same as #190's original caveat. Tier 🟢 Mid.

194. **Batch 119's follow-up chat on a brief: new `brief_messages` table (not transient), a 10-user-turn-per-brief cap, and chat-triggered proposals gated by a deterministic keyword check on Mark's own question rather than the model.** Implemented on `feat/batch-119-brief-followup-chat` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, Issue 10, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough). **Kickoff decisions (119.3, decided with Craig at `/batch-start`):** three forks were open. **(1) Storage** — a new `brief_messages` table keyed to `analysis_id`, mirroring `Feedback`'s referential pattern, over a transient/in-memory history: every other AI interaction in this app is stored and inspectable (Decision #137's `analyses`/`feedback` precedent), and a transient history would lose Mark's question on a refresh or app restart. **(2) Turn cap** — a fixed 10 user-question cap per brief (`MAX_USER_TURNS_PER_ANALYSIS` in `services/brief_chat.py`), a 422 past that, over no cap: bounds runaway Anthropic spend from an accidental loop on a single brief without meaningfully constraining the advisory back-and-forth the batch is for. **(3) Action scope** — Craig's first answer ("allow it to trigger existing propose/approve actions") was followed up to settle the concrete mechanism against Decision #29's propose→approve→push gate: the model itself never calls a mutating endpoint. Instead, a **deterministic keyword check on Mark's own question** (`_wants_adjustment`, matching words like "ease"/"lighter"/"swap"/"adjust") — never the model's free-form answer — decides whether to attach `proposed_planned_workout_id` to the assistant turn, and only when today's plan has a deliverable, non-rest-day bike workout (`_todays_adjustable_workout_id`, reusing `is_bike_workout_type`). The frontend's "Propose this adjustment" button then calls the **existing** `POST /api/v1/workout-delivery/planned-workouts/{id}/proposals` endpoint directly — the exact same first step Delivery's own UI would call — so approval/push still only ever happens through the existing Delivery flow; chat is a new entry point into an unchanged gate, not a new mutation path. **Implementation:** `services/brief_chat.py` (`BriefChatService.ask`/`.history`, `AnthropicBriefChatClient`, `SYSTEM_PROMPT` embedding the brief's own `context_packet` + `output_markdown` so answers are grounded, with the same floors as the morning prompt); `generate_anthropic_text` (`services/anthropic_text.py`) gained an optional `prior_messages: list[dict[str, str]] | None` param, backward-compatible for every existing single-turn caller, so one boundary now serves both single-shot analyses and multi-turn chat; `routers/brief_chat.py` (`GET`/`POST /api/v1/briefs/{analysis_id}/messages`, user-scoped 404/403 like `feedback`); migration `018` (`brief_messages` table) + `019` (RLS `ENABLE` on it — the first new coach table since migration 015, so `test_coach_rls_migration.py` was generalized from "load migration 015's `RLS_TABLES`" to "load every RLS migration in `RLS_MIGRATION_FILES`", so the next new table follows the same two-migration pattern instead of needing a bespoke test rewrite). Shared `briefMessageSchema`/`briefMessageInputSchema`/`briefMessageTurnSchema` in `@coach/shared`; `BriefFollowUpChat.tsx` renders on `MorningBriefPage` below the coach read. **Boundaries:** no change to Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2, the morning brief's own generation path, or the propose→approve→push contract's approval/push steps. **Verification (local, green):** backend ruff + format + mypy `src` clean; full local pytest 619 passed/222 skipped (new DB-backed `test_brief_chat.py` cases skip locally without `DATABASE_URL`, same as every prior batch — they run in CI); shared `tsc` + vitest 19/19 clean; web `tsc --noEmit` clean, lint clean (6 pre-existing Fast-Refresh warnings only), full web vitest 42 files/269 tests passed, web production build clean under Node 20. Tier 🟢 Mid.

195. **Batch 116's hosted voice was still silent after two backend fixes (#190, #193) because the root cause was frontend, not Piper: `vercel.json`'s Content-Security-Policy had no `media-src` directive, so it fell back to `default-src 'self'` — which does not cover `blob:` URLs — silently blocking `BriefListenControls.tsx`'s `Audio(URL.createObjectURL(blob))` playback of the hosted voice's WAV response.** Implemented on `fix/batch-116-csp-media-src` (Craig reported hearing nothing a third time on iPhone Safari after ruling out the mute switch). **How this was actually diagnosed:** `railway logs --http` showed the real production calls succeeding (`POST /api/v1/tts/synthesize 200`, 284–394ms) — not the 502s #193 fixed — so the backend was not the problem this time. `railway ssh` into the live container reproduced the exact synthesis call the service makes and confirmed genuinely valid, non-silent audio (max amplitude 32767/32767, RMS ~6743, correct mono/16kHz/16-bit WAV header) — ruling out both Piper and the voice model. That left only the client: the button changing to "Pause" (i.e. `Audio.play()` resolving and `onplay` firing) while producing no sound is the signature of a resource that loads but is policy-blocked from actually playing, not a codec/hardware issue — pointing at CSP's `blob:` scheme gap, which `img-src` already carved an explicit exception for (`img-src 'self' data: blob:`) but `media-src` was never added when Batch 116 introduced blob-based audio playback. **Fix:** added `media-src 'self' blob:` to the CSP header in `vercel.json`. **A process note, not a decision:** two prior investigations (#190, #193) chased real, confirmed backend problems (an unverified Docker build, then an actual 502 timeout) that were legitimate bugs worth fixing — but neither was the reason hosted voice stayed silent afterward; the actual blocker was introduced un-diagnosed all the way back when Batch 116 first shipped `BriefListenControls.tsx`'s hosted-audio path, since blob-URL playback was never manually tested against the app's own CSP before this. **Boundaries:** no backend change; no change to the consent-gate design (#189), engine (#190), or voice/timeout (#193); `apps/api/src/middleware.py`'s separate `default-src 'none'` CSP on JSON API responses is unrelated and untouched — the page's own CSP (not the audio response's) governs blob-URL playback. **Verification:** `vercel.json` validated as syntactically correct JSON; no backend/frontend source files touched, so no test suite re-run was needed. **Unverified until real deploy:** whether this is the complete fix — needs a live check with the Settings toggle on, on the same iPhone that reported silence twice before. Tier 🟢 Mid.

196. **Batch 120's Sleep calendar verdict colouring uses a new lightweight range read over stored morning analyses, rather than extending either the one-night overnight chart endpoint or the full daily-loop history fetch.** Implemented on `feat/batch-120-sleep-calendar-verdicts` (`docs/phase-batches.md`, wave-3 Issue 2, surfaced by Craig's 2026-07-14 walkthrough). **Kickoff decision (120.2): dedicated `GET /api/v1/sleep/verdicts?from&to`.** The batch wanted each visible calendar window tinted cheaply, not a full `daily-loop` per cell. The existing reads each have a narrow job: `GET /api/v1/bedroom/overnight` is a heavy one-night temp/fan/sleep detail join, while `/sleep` uses one historical `daily-loop` fetch only for the currently selected day. Extending either would have mixed a month-grid summary concern into a single-day detail seam. The additive, truthful seam is a small range read returning only the freshest stored morning verdict per date for this user. **Implementation:** new router `apps/api/src/routers/sleep.py` exposes `GET /api/v1/sleep/verdicts?from=YYYY-MM-DD&to=YYYY-MM-DD`, filtered to `analysis_type='morning'`, ordered so a later regenerated brief wins for that date, and normalized to the existing lowercase API verdict vocabulary. Shared `sleepCalendarVerdicts*` schemas were added in `packages/shared/src/schemas.ts`; `SleepPage.tsx` now owns the visible calendar month, fetches one verdict map for that month-grid window via `useSleepCalendarVerdicts`, and passes it into `SleepDateCalendar.tsx`. The calendar itself stays presentational: day cells tint by verdict when present, carry a `G`/`A`/`R` marker as the non-colour cue, render a legend, and expose verdict-aware aria labels (`Friday 19 June 2026 - Amber verdict`). Days with no stored brief stay honestly uncoloured. **Boundaries:** no migration; no change to the selected-day history fetch, the overnight chart endpoint, verdict logic, Green/Amber/Red thresholds, #133, #135, or Red-never-VO2; this is a read-only calendar enhancement over already-stored verdict truth. **Verification (local, green):** targeted web vitest **18 passed** (`SleepDateCalendar.test.tsx`, `SleepPage.test.tsx`), web `tsc --noEmit` clean, web production build clean, backend `ruff check` clean, backend `mypy` clean on the new router. The new DB-backed router test file `apps/api/tests/test_sleep_verdicts.py` exists but **skipped locally** because the Postgres-backed fixture was unavailable in this run, so CI should be the first real backend execution of that endpoint. Tier 🟢 Mid.

197. **Batch 116's hosted voice reverts from `low` back to `medium` quality after a live benchmark on the real production container showed `low` wasn't dramatically faster than `medium` at realistic brief length, only noticeably more robotic.** Implemented on `fix/batch-116-medium-voice-quality` (Craig heard the fixed hosted voice for the first time after #195's CSP fix and reported it sounded "very robotic"). **Why the earlier `low` choice looked faster than it was:** #193's production logs showed real `POST /api/v1/tts/synthesize` calls completing in 284–394ms, which read as evidence `low` was dramatically fast — but a direct `railway ssh` benchmark of `low` against realistic ~2000-character, 317-word brief-length text (matching a real morning brief) took **23.27s**, meaning those fast production calls were for much shorter text than a full brief, not representative. The same benchmark against `medium` quality (`en_GB-alan-medium`, the original voice from #190) took **33.83s** for identical text — only ~40% slower than `low`, not the "several times faster" assumption that justified downgrading quality in #193. **Decision:** with the speed gap this small and the quality gap this noticeable, `medium` is worth the extra ~10 seconds, especially since `BriefListenControls.tsx` already shows a loading state throughout. `PIPER_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` raised 60→90s (roughly 2.5x the measured 33.83s) for real-world headroom beyond a clean isolated benchmark. **Method note:** this is the first of the three Batch 116 hotfixes actually validated against realistic brief-length text on the real container before shipping, rather than either a short test phrase (#193's Dockerfile `curl` verification) or reasoning from first principles about relative model speed (#193's original `low`-for-speed decision) — worth carrying forward for any future Piper tuning. **Boundaries:** no change to the consent-gate design (#189), the self-hosted engine choice (#190), or the CSP fix (#195); only the voice model file and timeout constant. **Verification:** `ruff check`/`mypy` scoped to the touched files (`config.py`, `piper_tts.py`) clean — the concurrent Batch 120 work-in-progress sharing this working directory (`sleep.py`) has an unrelated pre-existing type error, left untouched; targeted `test_piper_tts.py`/`test_tts.py` (4 passed, 6 DB-backed skipped locally). **Unverified until real deploy:** the actual synthesis time under real request load (DB/auth overhead, concurrent traffic) vs. the clean SSH-benchmark numbers above. Tier 🟢 Mid.

198. **Batch 116's hosted voice is pre-generated in the background right after a brief finishes generating, rather than only on-demand when a consenting user first taps Listen.** Implemented on `feat/batch-116-pregenerate-audio` (Craig asked whether the ~30s medium-quality synthesis wait, measured in #197, could happen ahead of time instead of when the user actually wants to listen). **Design: warm the existing in-process cache, don't change the on-demand endpoint's contract.** `POST /api/v1/tts/synthesize` already caches by `sha256(model_path + spoken_text)` (`services/tts_cache.py`, factored out of `routers/tts.py` so both the router and the new pre-generation path share one cache); pre-generation just needs to compute the *same* cache key ahead of time and populate it, so the frontend's existing call is either an instant cache hit or, on a miss (first brief after this ships, or a cold cache after a restart), falls through to synthesizing fresh exactly as before — no frontend change, no new endpoint. **The one real piece of new work: `services/markdown_speech.py` is a line-for-line Python port of `apps/web/src/lib/markdownSpeech.ts`.** The cache key is keyed on the *spoken* text, not the raw brief markdown, and that markdown→speech transform only existed client-side; pre-generation has to reproduce it exactly or the cache key it computes won't match what the browser later requests. Verified against the frontend's own `markdownSpeech.test.ts` cases (both fixtures pass unchanged in the Python port) plus additional cases for code fences, numbered lists/checkboxes, blockquotes, and blank-line collapsing — the two implementations must be kept in sync by hand; a future frontend-only change to the markdown transform will silently desync the two unless this file is also updated (called out in both files' docstrings). **Hook points:** `services/tts_pregenerate.py::pregenerate_brief_audio(player, analysis)` is called from both brief-generation paths — `daily_loop.py`'s `_generate_brief_after_checkin` (after `session.commit()`) and `scheduler.py`'s `run_morning_weather_sync` backstop (after the brief-ready push, inside the `if analysis_result.generated:` block) — gated on `player.hosted_tts_consent` and on the voice model file existing, and wrapped so a Piper failure (timeout, process error) is logged and swallowed, never breaking brief generation or the backstop's push/proposal-regeneration steps that follow it in the same loop. **Persistence decision (asked explicitly): stay in-memory only, don't add audio persistence.** The alternative — storing synthesized audio so it survives a backend restart between pre-generation and playback — was explicitly declined to keep the "generate fresh, never store" precedent (#179) intact; a deploy landing in that window just means the on-demand path re-synthesizes once, same as before this batch. **Boundaries:** no change to the consent gate (#189), engine (#190), CSP fix (#195), or voice/timeout (#197); no new API contract, no migration. **Verification (local, green):** backend pytest 629 passed (224 skipped DB-backed; 10 new — 5 `test_markdown_speech.py` parity cases, 5 `test_tts_pregenerate.py` cases covering consent-off/model-missing/cache-hit/synthesis-failure/happy-path), `ruff check`/`mypy src` clean on all 113 source files; no frontend files touched. Tier 🟢 Mid.

201. **Batch 123 keeps Home to one loud prompt under the verdict by making the unread brief, Today actions, and Next strip a strict priority stack rather than three independent blocks.** Implemented on local `main` from Batch 123 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, the third of the 2026-07-15 UX-review batches 121-128). 203. **Batch 125 keeps Sleep and Climate as separate surfaces, with Climate staying a primary tab, but removes the duplicated live-room fact block so each bedroom fact has one clear home.** Implemented on `closeout-124-docs` from Batch 125 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, the fifth of the 2026-07-15 UX-review batches 121-128). After Batch 104, the overnight chart already belonged only to Sleep and the fan controls only to Climate, but Sleep Tonight and Climate still both rendered the same 4-stat live-bedroom block (`Indoor now / Thermostat / Overnight low / Wind`), forcing Mark to learn "summary on both, chart on one, controls on the other." **Decision 125.2:** keep the split rather than fold Climate into Sleep, and keep Climate as a primary tab. *Why:* the Climate surface is not just explanatory context; it is the active, stateful control plane for the overnight fan, with a live read and manual commands that deserve a stable top-level home. Folding that into Sleep would blur the retrospective/prospective sleep story with device control and make the sleep hub heavier again just after Batch 104 intentionally separated them. **The duplication fix:** Climate now explicitly owns the canonical live-room read plus controls, while Sleep Tonight steps down to one concise summary line (`Indoor … · fan on auto/manual`) and one direct handoff to `/environment`; it no longer repeats the full 4-stat block. The "Last night" handoff on Climate remains in the opposite direction so the IA is symmetrical: Climate → live/control, Sleep → retrospective/wind-down. A tiny shared `bedroomLiveSummary(...)` helper now formats the same summary for Sleep Tonight and Home's bedroom section so the live-summary wording itself has one rule instead of drifting across pages. **Boundaries:** frontend-only; no migration, no API/shared-schema change, and Batch 121's holiday-dormant behavior remains intact. Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, and Red-never-VO2 are untouched. **Verification (local, green):** targeted web vitest 16/16 passed (`SleepPage.test.tsx`, `EnvironmentPage.test.tsx`), `tsc && vite build` clean, and web lint clean aside from the 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings in unrelated files. Tier 🟢 Mid.

204. **Batch 126 makes Week a read-first weekly glance for Mark, with the existing organiser demoted to an admin-only second layer.** Implemented on `main` from Batch 126 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, the sixth of the 2026-07-15 UX-review batches 121-128). The old `WeekAheadPage` contradicted the product reality Craig named at kickoff: Mark's weekly plan "won't change", but the Week tab opened with the full edit rail first — move/add/build/skip/remove/reset/restructure — as if the primary user were there to administer the plan rather than to glance at it. **Decision 126.2:** settle the edit audience as **Craig-as-admin only** on this surface, while keeping Week itself visible to Mark as a primary tab. *Why:* the nav and the rest of the product already treat Week as a daily reader surface for Mark, not an internal admin tool, and there is already precedent in the app for read-for-everyone with structured tools behind an admin gate (`CoachStatePage`, #202). Hiding Week itself from Mark would have removed a useful weekly summary; leaving the organiser first-class for him would keep the exact problem the batch was meant to solve. **Implementation shape:** `WeekAheadPage.tsx` now matches the nav label with a **Week** header and defaults to a glance-first view built entirely from the existing schedule payload — a compact session-count summary, done/to-do totals, read-only per-day rows for **This week**, and a simple **Coming up** preview for the later days already in the 14-day window. The pre-existing organiser is preserved unchanged behind an explicit admin-only **Edit week** tab, where the move/add/build/skip/remove/reset/restructure controls and the Holiday / New training block links still live; no new endpoint or mutation path was introduced. **Boundaries:** frontend-only; no migration, no API/shared-schema change; `/api/v1/plan-actions/*` and `/api/v1/restructure/*` behavior is untouched; Home/Sleep/Climate and Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 stay as-is. **Verification (local, green):** targeted web vitest 13/13 passed (`WeekAheadPage.test.tsx`), web lint clean aside from the 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings, and web production build clean. Tier 🟢 Mid.

205. **Batch 127 sets a 12px floor for meaning-bearing microtype on the daily-reader surfaces, rather than preserving 10–11px labels for "cleanliness".** Implemented on `feat/batch-127-daily-reader-legibility` from Batch 127 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, the seventh of the 2026-07-15 UX-review batches 121-128 after #203/#204 were used by Batches 125/126 on `main`). The live app still had meaning-bearing copy at `text-[10px]`/`text-[11px]` in exactly the places the batch row named: the metrics table's status/age guidance, the verdict/date eyebrows, and the Home **More detail** / **Next** mono labels. **Decision:** raise all of those to a readable floor (`text-xs` for labels, `text-sm` for explanatory/status copy) while leaving purely decorative micro-elements alone. *Why:* this batch's user is a real 57-year-old reading at phone distance, so "tiny but tidy" is the wrong optimization when the text itself carries the meaning; the right boundary is not "make everything bigger", but "nothing meaning-bearing is smaller than the app's minimum comfortable reading size." The pass therefore keeps the existing type scale and hierarchy, but removes 10–11px from the load-bearing daily-reader copy. **Boundaries:** frontend-only; no behavioural/API change; no new typography system; no copy or verdict-logic change. **Verification (local, green):** full web vitest 281/281 passed with new floor-lock assertions in `MetricComparisonTable.test.tsx`, `VerdictHero.test.tsx`, and `DashboardPage.test.tsx`; web build clean; web lint clean aside from the 6 pre-existing Fast Refresh warnings. Tier 🟢 Mid.

207. **Batch 129 fixes the metrics-table direction allow-list to cover every emitted baseline row, and clears four small daily-reader polish gaps found on the 2026-07-16 walkthrough re-run.** Implemented on `feat/batch-129-post-review-polish` from Batch 129 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, 2026-07-16 walkthrough re-run). The re-run on synced `origin/main` confirmed two earlier findings were already shipped (Week redesign #152, Sleep⇄Climate overlap #151); these are the gaps that survived, bundled into one frontend-only pass. **129.1 (correctness):** `MetricComparisonTable.tsx`'s `HIGHER_IS_BETTER`/`LOWER_IS_BETTER` sets covered only 6 of the 8 baseline keys the backend emits (`metric_baselines.py::_current_metric_values`), so `readiness_score` and `average_respiration` had "no direction" — an above-normal readiness (good) rendered as an amber ⚠. Added `readiness_score` (higher-is-better) and `average_respiration` (higher-is-worse: an elevated overnight respiration signals stress/illness/poor recovery, below-baseline stays green). *Why higher-is-worse for respiration:* Mark's resting respiration is low (10–12) and a rise, not a fall, is the concern. **129.2 (Climate de-dup):** `BedroomBody.tsx` rendered a single fan's live status on both the "Overnight autopilot" row and the "Bedroom fan" card, and printed literal "Mode unknown · Oscillation unknown"; the autopilot row now describes the toggle ("Following the room overnight; winds down by morning." / "Off — the fan holds your manual setting.") and the mode/oscillation line renders only for fields the integration actually reports. **129.3 (copy + shared helper):** dropped "canonical" (`EnvironmentPage.tsx`) and the developer phrasing "…rail one layer down" (`WeekAheadPage.tsx`, admin-only tab); a new shared `workoutTypeLabel()` in `lib/workoutCategories.ts` replaces three copies of a `type.replace(/[_-]+/g,' ')` prettifier (Home, Week, Sleep) that leaked the raw discipline prefix ("Bike sweet spot", "Bike z2") beneath an already-friendly title — the category badge/icon conveys the discipline, so the label reads as the session's character ("Sweet spot", "Zone 2"). **129.4 (prep bullets):** `SleepPrepBody.tsx`'s tonight prep actions used a green check that reads as "done"; swapped for a neutral bullet. **Boundaries:** frontend-only; no migration; no API/shared-schema change; no verdict/delivery/scheduler change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2 untouched. **Verification (local, green):** web vitest **293 passed** (new: `MetricComparisonTable` readiness/respiration direction cases, `workoutCategories.test.ts`, `BedroomBody.test.tsx`, `SleepPrepBody.test.tsx`), `tsc --noEmit` clean, eslint clean on touched files, production build clean (Node 20). **Closeout:** Shipped via PR #155, squash `8a58618`; CI green on both push and PR-context waves; production verified on Railway direct + Vercel same-origin `/api/v1/health` SHA `8a58618e30cc38f5c0a5d4b5d3a7e699c89c9660`, web `/`+`/sleep`+`/environment`+`/delivery`+`/brief` `200`, unauthenticated `/api/v1/daily-loop` `401` both direct and via Vercel. Tier 🟢 Mid.

209. **Batch 131 ships a first-cut strength watching-brief on `/trends` (a `StrengthTrendCard` mirroring `WalkingBaseCard`) rather than waiting on Mark's scope decision, on Craig's explicit call to build a best-guess version and let Mark's feedback refine it.** Implemented on `feat/batch-131-strength-watching-brief` from Batch 131 (`docs/phase-batches.md`, marked design-pending: "decide with Mark first" on what signal drives the read and where it surfaces). **Root cause, not a data gap:** Batch 19 (#Decision unspecified, 2026-06-23) already computes a rolling 4-week/12-week strength frequency/duration/load-proxy rollup with a deterministic `increasing`/`stable`/`decreasing`/`insufficient_data` trend (`StrengthBriefResult`/`StrengthBriefService`, `apps/api/src/services/strength_brief.py`) and it was already serialized onto the daily-loop payload (`StrengthBriefOut`, `daily_loop.py`) — but the **shared Zod `dailyLoopSchema` never declared a `strengthBrief` field**, so the frontend silently dropped it on parse and no UI ever read it, unlike its sibling `walkingBrief`/`breathworkBrief` which were declared. **131.1 (scope call, made without Mark):** reused the exact precedent already shipped for the same "standing read on a rolling activity type" need — `WalkingBaseCard` on `/trends` — rather than inventing a new pattern: added `strengthBrief` to `dailyLoopSchema` (`packages/shared/src/schemas.ts`, mirroring `WindowStatsOut`'s `sessionCount`/`totalDurationMin`/`totalLoadProxy`/`sessionsPerWeek` shape), a new `StrengthTrendCard` component (`apps/web/src/components/StrengthTrendCard.tsx`) copying `WalkingBaseCard`'s layout (trend badge + rolling-window summary + reason line), and wired it onto `TrendsPage.tsx` directly below Walking base. Surfaced on Trends (not Home/Brief) because that's where the existing longitudinal reads (Walking base, sleep/readiness charts, year-on-year) already live, keeping "today" and "over time" separated the way the rest of the app already does. **Open for Mark's feedback:** whether 4w/12w is the right horizon for slower-adapting resistance work, and whether frequency-only trend is the right signal vs. weighting load/duration. **Boundaries:** frontend + shared-schema only; no backend/service change (the engine already existed); no migration; no verdict/delivery/scheduler change; Green/Amber/Red, #133, #135, Red-never-VO2, and the strength recovery-isolation invariant (#49/#80) untouched. **Verification (local, green):** shared vitest **19 passed** + `tsc --noEmit` clean; web vitest **294 passed** (new: `TrendsPage.test.tsx` strength-trend assertions), `tsc --noEmit` clean, eslint clean (0 errors, 6 known warnings), production build clean (Node 20). No live-login browser verification — the local dev preview proxies to the real production API and this pass didn't have Mark's credentials; the `TrendsPage.test.tsx` render (full component tree, realistic mock data) stands in for it. Tier 🟢 Mid.

210. **Batch 116's hosted voice moves from `en_GB-alan-medium` to `en_GB-northern_english_male-medium`, chosen by Craig from a live side-by-side listen of 6 real synthesized samples rather than another guess.** Implemented on `fix/batch-116-northern-english-male-voice` (Craig asked "is there any way we can get celebrity voices to do it" after finding `alan-medium` boring — declined outright: cloning a specific real person's voice without consent is a real legal/ethical line regardless of scale, not something to build even privately). **What was actually offered instead:** (1) trying other free Piper voices, (2) reopening the hosted-API-for-quality tradeoff (ElevenLabs, ~$22/mo Creator plan for the app's real ~60k chars/month usage, researched live via `WebSearch`). Craig chose to try Piper voices first. Pulled the authoritative voice list from `rhasspy/piper-voices`' `voices.json` (rather than guessing catalog paths again, after #197's guess-and-fail cycle), synthesized the same sample paragraph across `alan-medium`, `cori-high`, `jenny_dioco-medium`, `northern_english_male-medium`, `lessac-high`, then `ryan-high` on request, and published them as a self-contained HTML artifact with embedded base64 `<audio>` players so Craig could actually listen and choose, rather than picking from names alone. **Ryan (`high` quality) was Craig's first pick but ruled out on measured cost:** a live full-brief-length benchmark showed `ryan-high` took 95s in isolation — and #197 already established real production requests run roughly 2.4x slower than an isolated `railway ssh` benchmark under CPU contention (a `medium`-quality request once measured 82s vs. a 34s isolated benchmark), so `ryan-high` would likely run 150–230s+ in practice. Offered three ways to still use Ryan (drop to a shortened brief, accept a multi-minute wait, or pick a different voice); Craig chose to stay within `medium` quality. Of the three medium candidates tried, Northern English Male benchmarked fastest (27.22s, vs. 33.83s for `alan-medium`) with comfortable timeout headroom. **Boundaries:** no change to the consent-gate design (#189), engine (#190), timeout constant (#197), or pre-generation (#198) — only the specific voice file. **Verification:** `ruff check`/`mypy` scoped to the touched `config.py` clean; no test files reference the specific voice filename (they use `tmp_path`-based fake models), so no test changes needed. **Unverified until real deploy:** whether the new voice's `curl` download resolves in the actual Railway build (same class of caveat as #190/#193/#197 — this project's CI doesn't build the Dockerfile). Tier 🟢 Mid.
